1 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Venetian Salami Co. v. Parthenais


No. 73,848


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


554 So. 2d 499; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 1245; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 595



December 14, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal, Direct Conflict of Decisions, First District, Case No. 88-1414, Alachua County.



DISPOSITION:  The court held that the state did not have jurisdiction over petitioner, a foreign corporation, unless it had minimum contacts with the state sufficient to satisfy the federal constitutional requirement of due process and met the requirements of the state's long arm statute. Because the jurisdictional facts were in dispute, the court remanded the case with instructions for the trial court to hold an evidentiary hearing on the jurisdiction issue.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a foreign corporation, appealed the decision from the First District, Alachua County, Court of Appeal (Florida) that reversed the order of the trial court and found that because respondent alleged that petitioner entered into a contract with him in Florida, the requirements of Fla. Stat. Ann. § 48.193(1)(g) had been met, and no further showing of minimum contacts was needed. The appellate court certified a conflict with other courts.


OVERVIEW: Respondent filed an action in Florida, alleging that an agent of petitioner, a foreign corporation, hired respondent to assist it in collecting an account. The trial court granted petitioner's motion to dismiss for lack of personal jurisdiction, finding that respondent did not have the minimum contacts with the state. The appellate court reversed, finding that because petitioner was alleged to have entered into a contract in Florida, the requirements of Fla. Stat. Ann. § 48.193(1)(g) had been met, and thus minimum contacts with the state was not needed. The appellate court certified a conflict with other appellate courts. The court held that § 48.193 merely established Florida's basis for jurisdiction over a non-resident defendant. However, the federal constitutional requirement of minimum contacts had to be met, based on whether petitioner's conduct in the state was such that it could reasonably expect to be haled into court in Florida. Although respondent alleged sufficient facts to satisfy the minimum contacts requirement, petitioner denied the allegations. Therefore, the court remanded the case for the trial court to hold an evidentiary hearing on the issue of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court held that the state did not have jurisdiction over petitioner, a foreign corporation, unless it had minimum contacts with the state sufficient to satisfy the federal constitutional requirement of due process and met the requirements of the state's long arm statute. Because the jurisdictional facts were in dispute, the court remanded the case with instructions for the trial court to hold an evidentiary hearing on the jurisdiction issue.

 

2 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


In re T.W.


No. 74,143


Supreme Court of Florida


1989 Fla. LEXIS 1226



October 12, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] 
This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion dated October 5, 1989


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory/Constitutional Invalidity, Fifth District, Case No. 89-893.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guardian ad litem for unborn sought review of judgment rendered by the District Court of Appeal, Fifth District (Florida) that found that a parental consent statute was invalid under the Florida constitution.


OVERVIEW: Prior to undergoing an abortion, a minor must obtain parental consent, or convince a court that she is sufficiently mature to make the decision herself, or that, if she is immature, the abortion nevertheless is in her best interests. Pursuant to this procedure, minor petitioned for a waiver of parental consent under the judicial bypass provision of Fla. Stat. ch. 390.001(4)(a)(1988). The trial court appointed counsel for minor and guardian ad litem for the fetus. Guardian ad litem argued that the judicial bypass portion of the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The district court found that the statute's judicial alternative to parental consent was unconstitutionally vague. Guardian ad litem sought review. Minor legally had abortion but because the questions raised were of great public importance and likely to recur, the court accepted jurisdiction. The court affirmed the judgment and found that the statute was invalid under the Florida constitution. The statute failed to provide adequate procedural safeguards and the statute did not have the least intrusive means of furthering the state's interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding that a parental consent statute was invalid under the Florida unconstitutional because the statute lacked procedural safeguards.

 

3 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


In re T.W.


No. 74,143


Supreme Court of Florida


551 So. 2d 1186; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 972; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 531



October 5, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Withdrawn October 12, 1989. Rehearing Denied December 4, 1989. Substituted Opinion Reported at 1989 Fla. LEXIS 1226.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal, Statutory/Constitutional Invalidity, Fifth District, Case No. 89-893.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guardian ad litem sought review of a ruling from the District Court of Appeal, Fifth District (Florida), which declared Fla. Stat. ch. 390.001(4)(a) unconstitutional and quashed the trial court's order requiring parental consent in an action involving abortion by a minor.


OVERVIEW: A pregnant minor petitioned for a waiver of parental consent under a judicial bypass provision in order to obtain an abortion. The trial court appointed counsel for the minor and appellant guardian ad litem for the fetus and conducted a hearing. The trial court found that the judicial bypass provision of Fla. Stat. ch. 390.001(4)(a) was unconstitutional because it failed to make sufficient provision for challenges to its validity, was vague, and made no provision for testimony to controvert that of the minor. In addition, the trial court denied the minor's petition and required her to obtain parental consent. The appellate court declared ch. 390.001(4)(a) entirely unconstitutional, quashed the trial court's order requiring parental consent, and dismissed the petition. Appellant sought review. The court found that ch. 390.001(4)(a) failed because it intruded upon the privacy of the pregnant minor from conception to birth and was not the least intrusive means of furthering the state interest. In addition, the court found that ch. 390.001(4)(a) failed to provide adequate procedural safeguards because it did not make any exception for emergency or therapeutic abortions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court order declaring state statutory law unconstitutional because such statute violated the state constitution.

 

4 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Cape Publications, Inc. v. Hitchner


No. 71,554


Supreme Court of Florida


549 So. 2d 1374; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 974; 16 Media L. Rep. 2337; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 492



October 5, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 9, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal, Statutory Validity, Fifth District, Case No. 87-277, Brevard County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant newspaper appealed from the decision of the Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida) that (a) upheld the entry of partial summary judgment in favor of plaintiff parents in an action, brought under Fla. Stat. ch. 827.07 (1981), alleging tortious public disclosure of private facts regarding plaintiffs being acquitted of child abuse allegations and (b) ruled that ch. 827.07 was not unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: A week after plaintiff parents were acquitted of child abuse charges, defendant newspaper published a story about the case and the evidence that was presented. Ten days later, defendant published another story, retracting the description of some of the evidence that was presented at plaintiffs' trial. Plaintiffs then sued defendant for, inter alia, invading their privacy by public disclosure of private facts, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 827.07 (1981), which concerned the confidentiality of child abuse proceedings. Plaintiffs were granted partial summary judgment on this claim and the appellate court affirmed, ruling ch. 827.07 was valid under U.S. Const. amend. I. Defendant appealed. In quashing the decision in favor of plaintiffs, the court ruled that the information involved here did not involve purely private facts, but was of legitimate public concern. The public had an interest in media coverage of judicial functions; thus, on these facts, defendant could not be held liable. The court made no ruling concerning the constitutionality of ch. 827.07.


OUTCOME: The decision in favor of plaintiffs was quashed, without reaching the question regarding the constitutionality of the statute, because, under the facts of this case, the information disclosed by defendant was of legitimate public concern and did not involve purely private facts; society had an interest in media coverage of judicial proceedings.

 

5 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sarasota County


No. 73,912


Supreme Court of Florida


549 So. 2d 659; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 968; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 465



September 28, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Sarasota County, Bond Validations, Gilbert A. Smith, Chief Judge, Case No. 88-5873.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review from the Circuit Court of Sarasota County (Florida) judgment approving appellee county's proposed bond issue, arguing that pursuant to Sarasota, Fla., County Charter § 4.3.E, a voter referendum was required before approval of the proposed issue.


OVERVIEW: After appellee county proposed a bond issue to be secured by prior lien upon and pledge of county gas tax, voted gas tax, and local option gas tax, appellant state filed suit to prevent the issue absent a voter referendum. Lower court found for appellee, and appellant sought review. Court held that since no ad valorem tax revenues were pledged, appellee was exempt from the constitutional requirement of securing voter approval, but found that it was still possible that appellee's own charter required approval of the bond issue by referendum. Pursuant to Sarasota, Fla., County Charter § 4.3.E, court held that since the taxes in question were received by appellee and spend locally, the bond issue was invalid without first being submitting to referendum. Finally, court held that appellee's argument that its charter conflicted with state law was unpersuasive, since the provisions at issue were not incompatible.


OUTCOME: Court reversed lower court's judgment, holding that although no constitutional requirement of voter approval applied, appellee was required by its own charter to seek a referendum on the bond issue, since the funds to be collected would be given to appellee.

 

6 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Bull v. State


No. 70,723


Supreme Court of Florida


548 So. 2d 1103; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 865; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 443



September 14, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions, Second District - Case No. 86-123, (Polk County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of a decision from the Second District Court of Appeal, Polk County (Florida). The appeals court affirmed the imposition of a lien on petitioner for the appointment of services of counsel after petitioner was charged with escaping or attempting to escape from prison in violation of Fla. Stat. § 944.40 (1985).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner inmate was convicted of escaping or attempting to escape from prison in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 944.40 (1985). Petitioner had executed an affidavit of insolvency and requested appointed counsel; petitioner also authorized the trial court to impose a lien for the services of counsel without notice of a hearing. The trial court imposed a lien at sentencing and gave petitioner 30 days to challenge the amount of the lien. The court of appeals affirmed, holding that petitioner's affidavit of insolvency waived the notice and hearing rights of Fla. Stat. ch. 27.56(7) (1985). The court affirmed the imposition of a lien. The court agreed with petitioner that the court of appeals erred in relying on the waiver in the affidavit of insolvency. However, the trial court gave petitioner 30 days to object and to ask for a hearing pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.720(d)(1). Petitioner's failure to object or to request a hearing constituted a valid waiver. Further, petitioner could only have challenged the amount of the lien, not the actual imposition of the lien, because imposing such a lien was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the imposition of a lien on petitioner inmate for the appointment of services of counsel but disagreed with the reasoning of the appeals court. Petitioner's affidavit of insolvency did not waive petitioner's notice and hearing rights. However, petitioner was given the proper time to object to the amount of the lien, and petitioner's failure to do so constituted a valid waiver.

 

7 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


State v. Crenshaw


No. 72,181


Supreme Court of Florida


548 So. 2d 223; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 834; 1 A.L.R.5th 1075; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 421



August 31, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied November 1, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions, First District - Case No. BM-281, (Escambia County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the state of Florida, sought review of a decision from the District Court of Appeal (Florida), which set aside a forfeiture associated with respondent's possession of cocaine. The decision was premised on a holding that a forfeiture of a vehicle was only justified if the use of that vehicle played some part in carrying out a criminal transaction involving the illegal drugs.


OVERVIEW: Discovered in possession of cocaine while in his car, respondent was arrested for possession of cocaine; the police took his automobile into custody, and timely filed a petition for forfeiture. Respondent admitted possessing the cocaine for his own use. The district court set aside the forfeiture, holding in order to justify a forfeiture, the use of the vehicle must have played some part in carrying out a prohibited criminal transaction involving the contraband drugs more than remotely incidental to an occupant's possession of illicit drugs for purely personal use. The court held, pursuant to Fla. Stat. Ann. §§ 932.702(4), 932.703(1), 932.701(2)(a)-(d), that possessing drugs, even solely for personal use, subjected individuals not only to criminal penalties but also to forfeiture of the vehicle, boat, or aircraft in which the drugs were found. It made no difference whether the drugs were on the seat, in the console, or in the occupant's pocket. Accordingly, the decision of the district court was quashed, and the case was remanded for reinstatement of the forfeiture.


OUTCOME: The decision that set aside a forfeiture was quashed, and the case was remanded for reinstitution of the forfeiture, because possessing drugs, even solely for personal use, subjected respondent not only to criminal penalties but also to forfeiture of the vehicle in which the drugs were found, whether the drugs were on the seat, in the console, or in the occupant's pocket.

 

8 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


The Florida Bar re Amendment to Rules of Civil Procedure


No. 73,263


Supreme Court of Florida


550 So. 2d 442; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 1114; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 397



July 27, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised on Denial of Rehearing, November 7, 1989. Reported at: 1989 Fla. LEXIS 1111.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding - Rules of Civil Procedure.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Civil Procedure Rules Committee proposed a new rule to replace Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.442 with a rule that imposed sanctions on parties who refused a bona fide offer of settlement prior to trial based on computations comparing the settlement offer to the actual verdict. The Board of Governors of the Florida Bar rejected the proposed rule and recommended that Fla. Stat. Ann. §§ 768.79 and 45.061 be declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court withdrew Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.442, effective January 1, 1990, and replaced it with a new rule. The court rejected the rule proposed by the Civil Procedure Rules Committee that would alter the procedure by which parties are sanctioned for failure to accept bona fide offers of settlement prior to trial by requiring a sanction equal to 15 percent of an unaccepted offer to pay any time the jury verdict is less than 75 percent of the offer; and 15 percent of an unaccepted offer to accept any time the jury verdict is more than 125 percent of the offer. The court agreed that the proposed rule raised serious question of whether the court would be impinging on the legislature if it adopted a procedural sanction of this type. Instead the court adopted a rule that permitted sanctions based on costs and attorney fees whenever an offer of judgment was unreasonably refused and the subsequent judgment was disproportionate to that offer by more than 25 percent. The court declined to address the constitutionality of the purely substantive aspects of Fla. Stat. Ann. §§ 768.79 and 45.061, but held that where they were inconsistent with new rule, the new rule would supercede .


OUTCOME: The court rejected the Committee's proposed rule and instead adopted a new rule that permitted sanctions based on costs and attorney fees when a settlement offer was unreasonably refused and the subsequent judgment was disproportionate to that offer by more than 25 percent. The court declined to declare the statutes unconstitutional, but held that where they conflicted with the new rule, the new rule would supercede.

 

9 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Hillsborough County Hospital & Welfare Bd. v. Taylor


No. 73,458


Supreme Court of Florida


546 So. 2d 1055; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 717; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 364



July 20, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance, Second District - Case No. 87-2350.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a certified question appeal, petitioner state hospital sought review of a judgment from the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) that held that petitioner, which had established a self-insurance trust fund, had waived sovereign immunity up to the maximum amount in the fund. Petitioner asserted that its legal liability was limited to $ 50,000 under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 768.28(5) (1980).


OVERVIEW: In a certified question appeal, the court held that a government hospital, which had established a self-insurance trust fund, had not waived sovereign immunity against claims up to the amount of the fund under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 286.28 (1979). Respondent was injured at petitioner's hospital. Petitioner admitted liability and stipulated actual damages of $ 2.5 million, but maintained that under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 768.28(5) (1980), their legal liability was limited to $ 50,000. The court rejected respondent's argument that petitioner, by establishing a self-insurance fund, had waived its sovereign immunity up to the limits of the fund. The court found that self-insurance was not the same as insurance when there was no contract with an insurer and no shifting of the burden of risk. The court concluded that petitioner's self-insurance fund could not be equated with commercial insurance for purposes of determining the waiver of sovereign immunity under § 286.28. The court quashed the portion of the judgment that conflicted with this ruling and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the portion of the judgment that held that petitioner had waived sovereign immunity up to the amount of the trust fund and remanded for further proceedings. The court found that self-insurance was not the same as commercial insurance for the purposes of waiver of sovereign immunity when there was no contract and no shifting of risk.

 

10 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Kane v. Robbins


No. 72,697


Supreme Court of Florida


556 So. 2d 1381; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 719; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 368



July 20, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 8, 1990


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Constitutional Construction, Fourth District - Case No. 4-86-1440.

Reported at 1990 Fla. LEXIS 381 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, members of a county political party board, sought review of a judgment from the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) that held Fla. Stat. ch. 76-432, which required school board members to be elected in nonpartisan elections, was valid. Petitioners asserted Chapter 76-432 was invalid, because it violated Fla. Const. art. III, § 11(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, members of a county political party board, filed suit seeking to have Fla. Stat. ch. 76-432, which required school board members to be elected in nonpartisan elections, declared invalid in violation of Fla. Const. art. III, § 11(a)(1). The district court concluded Chapter 76-432 was valid. Petitioners challenged the decision. The court noted, under § 11(a)(1), no special law or general law of local application pertaining to election, jurisdiction, or duties of officers, except officers of municipalities, chartered counties, special districts, or local governmental agencies was permitted. The court held that a school board member was an officer for purposes of § 11(a)(1). Because the state constitution and the state legislature, through various statutes, distinguished between school boards and special districts, the court held a school board was not excluded from the operation of § 11(a)(1) as a special district. The court concluded Chapter 76-432 was invalid because it was passed as a special act in contravention of § 11(a)(1). Accordingly, the district court's opinion was vacated, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The judgment that the challenged statute was valid was vacated and the case was remanded, because the challenged statute was invalid where it was passed as a special act in contravention of the state constitution.

 

11 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Jackson v. Dugger


Nos. 73,982, 74,067


Supreme Court of Florida


547 So. 2d 1197; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 655; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 355



July 6, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 20, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus and An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Donald R. Moran, Judge - Case No. 83-4600-CF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, under sentence and warrant of death, petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus, requested a stay of execution, and appealed from the denial by the Duval County Circuit Court (Florida) of her Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion to vacate or modify the judgment and sentence.


OVERVIEW: During the penalty phase of defendant's trial, the victim impact evidence was impermissibly presented to the jury. Defendant's counsel vigorously objected. After defendant's direct appeals, the United States Supreme Court held that presentation of victim impact evidence to a jury in a capital case violated the Eighth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. VIII. The change in interpretation of the law was so significant that, where objection was made during trial, the case was given retroactive application. Rather than focusing the jury's attention on the defendant's character and the circumstances of the crime, the victim impact evidence diverted the jurors' attention to the victim's character and reputation and the effect of his death. The court could not say beyond a reasonable doubt that the jury would have recommended a sentence of death had it not heard the victim impact evidence. Therefore, the court vacated the sentence and ordered a new sentencing proceeding to be held before a newly empanelled jury. The court found nothing in the record to support claims of a deficient psychiatric evaluation or ineffective assistance of counsel, and the Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion was denied.


OUTCOME: The court granted the habeas corpus petition, vacated the death sentence, and remanded the case for resentencing, as the victim impact evidence had been presented to the jury during the penalty phase of defendant's trial, over her counsel's objection. The court affirmed the trial court's denial defendant's motion for relief because the record did not support her claims of a deficient psychiatric evaluation or ineffective assistance of counsel.

 

12 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Smalley v. State


No. 72,785


Supreme Court of Florida


546 So. 2d 720; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 657; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 342



July 6, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Sumter County, John W. Booth, Judge - Case No. 87-504-CF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court in and for Sumter County (Florida) which sentenced him to death after he was found guilty of first-degree murder of his girlfriend's 28-month-old daughter. Appellant challenged his sentence only.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of first-degree murder of his girlfriend's 28-month-old daughter and was sentenced to death. On appeal, he challenged his death sentence only. The supreme court commuted his death sentence to life in prison without eligibility for parole for 25 years. The court found that, although the crime was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel, the mitigating evidence was not insubstantial. The court found a lack of prior significant criminal activity, that appellant's mental state was the major contributing factor in the killing, that mental health experts agreed that the circumstances under which appellant was living impaired his ability to appreciate the criminality of his conduct, and that the record showed appellant's genuine remorse. The court also found testimony that appellant was a good employee, that he cared deeply for the deceased child, and that he normally was not abusive to the children. The court held that any one or two of these factors might not have been sufficient to result in a reversal on proportionality grounds, but the entire picture of mitigation and aggravation was that of a case which did not warrant the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The supreme court commuted appellant's death sentence for first-degree murder of a 28-month-old child to life in prison without eligibility for parole for 25 years. The court held that, although the crime was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel, the mitigating evidence was not insubstantial. The court found that, given the entire picture of mitigation and aggravation, the case did not warrant the death penalty.

 

13 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Perez v. State


No. 72,161


Supreme Court of Florida


545 So. 2d 1357; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 625; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 320



June 29, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions, First District - Case Nos. BQ-153, BQ-154, BQ-155 (Santa Rosa County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an application for review of the decision of the District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida), in which it reversed and remanded the grant of petitioner's motions to dismiss certain charges against him, holding that an applicable statute of limitations period was to have been determined from the perspective of the date a crime was committed, which was in express and direct conflict with other case law.


OVERVIEW: In 1986, petitioner was charged with three counts of sexual battery upon children 11 years of age or younger. The incidents allegedly occurred between June 1, 1975, and June 1, 1976, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 794.011(2) (Supp. 1974 and 1975). Petitioner filed motions to dismiss all three counts, alleging that the crimes were no longer "capital" because the death penalty could not have been imposed, and therefore, the statute of limitations had expired for the offenses charged. The trial court granted the motions. Respondent state appealed to the district court of appeal, which reversed and remanded the case. Petitioner sought review because of express and direct conflict with other case law. The district court of appeal correctly concluded that the limitations period in effect at the time of the incident that gave rise to the criminal charges controlled the time within which prosecution had to have begun. Death was a possible penalty at the time of commission of the crimes at issue; thus, no statute of limitations controlled the prosecution of the offenses. The supreme court receded from the quoted language of the other case law to the extent that it conflicted.


OUTCOME: The supreme court approved the decision that reversed and remanded the grant of petitioner's motions to dismiss the charges against him. The statute of limitations period in effect at the time of the incident that gave rise to criminal charges controlled the time within which prosecution had to have begun. The supreme court receded from certain language of the conflicting case law to the extent that it was in conflict.

 

14 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Kibler v. State


No. 70,067


Supreme Court of Florida


546 So. 2d 710; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 555; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 291



June 15, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 17, 1989; Petition for Rehearing Filed June 30, 1989; Petition for Rehearing Denied August 17, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions, Fifth District - Case No. 86-876, (Orange County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court reviewed a decision from the Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida), which held that petitioner did not have standing to challenge a prosecutor's use of peremptory challenges in petitioner's trial for burglary and sexual battery.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, a white man, was convicted of burglary and four counts of sexual battery. On appeal, he challenged the trial judge's refusal to dismiss the jury on the ground that the prosecutor used peremptory challenges to strike all three black persons on the prospective jury. The district court of appeal held that petitioner did not have standing to raise the issue because he was not of the same race as the jurors who were challenged. Additionally, the record did not demonstrate that the challenges had been exercised on a racial basis. The state supreme court held that under Fla. Const. art. I, § 16, it was unnecessary that petitioner, who objected to peremptory challenges directed to members of a cognizable racial group, be of the same race as the jurors who were being challenged. The court added that race could be relevant in determining whether the challenges were being unconstitutionally exercised because of group bias. The court further held that the prosecutor did not carry the burden of showing that his challenges of two jurors were not exercised because of their race. Petitioner's conviction was reversed and the case remanded for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The district court of appeal's decision that petitioner could not challenge a prosecutor's use of peremptory challenges was disapproved, petitioner's conviction was reversed, and the case remanded because petitioner did not have to belong to the same racial group as the jurors who were being challenged.

 

15 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Spencer v. State


No. 69,883


Supreme Court of Florida


545 So. 2d 1352; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 572; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 296



June 15, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County, Richard B. Burk, Judge - Case No. 86-5921 CF A02.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County (Florida), which convicted him of two counts of first degree murder and twice sentenced him to death. Additionally, he was convicted and sentenced on four counts of robbery with a firearm, attempted first degree murder with a firearm, and aggravated assault with a firearm. Appellant raised three issues on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted, among other crimes, of two counts of first degree murder, and for which he received two death sentences. Appellant, who was black, challenged that order and raised several issues. One issue concerned the use of a special redistricting process as adopted in an administrative order to select the jurors in appellant's case, which resulted in appellant's county being divided into two jury districts for the eastern and western parts of the county. The court found that the record did not establish any intentional discriminatory conduct in the adoption of the administrative order and the creation of the jury districts. The effect of the administrative order, however, did create districts that resulted in an unconstitutional systematic exclusion of a large portion of the black population from the jury pool of the district from which the jury for appellant's trial was drawn. The court also agreed with appellant that he was denied equal protection, because the predominantly black district allowed an offender charged there to choose where to be tried, while the predominantly white district where appellant was charged did not. The order was reversed for a new trial.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for two counts of first degree murder was reversed for a new trial because the court found that an administrative order that created special districts for jury selection caused an unconstitutional exclusion of a large portion of the black population from the jury pool of the district from which the jury for the trial of appellant, a black, was drawn. The jury districts also posed an equal protection violation as well.

 

16 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


In re Amendment to Florida Rule of Criminal Procedure 3.220


No. 73,734


Supreme Court of Florida


550 So. 2d 1097; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 711; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 240



May 3, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended on Denial of Rehearing November 2, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Original Proceeding - Florida Rules of Criminal Procedure.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court considered the findings and recommendations of the Florida Supreme Court Commission on Criminal Discovery pursuant to a Concurrent Resolution from the Florida Legislature requesting the court to appoint a commission for the purpose of reviewing Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.220, regarding the discovery process in criminal cases.


OVERVIEW: The Florida Supreme Court Commission on Criminal Discovery (commission) made findings and recommendations to the court for the purpose of reviewing Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.220. The legislature requested the commission to consider: (1) Protection for victims and other witnesses. (2) Limiting depositions to only essential witnesses. (3) Prohibiting the defendant from attending the deposition unless good cause is shown. (4) Use of technological advances to reduce costs and scheduling problems. (5) Potential savings of public funds and the time of law enforcement, witnesses, prosecutors, defense counsel, and court personnel that may be derived by employing alternative discovery techniques. (6) Any other appropriate issues. With some notable exceptions and some minor changes, the court accepted the commission's proposed amendments to rule 3.220.


OUTCOME: The court accepted the proposed amendments of the Florida Supreme Court Commission on Criminal Discovery to the rule regarding discovery in criminal cases, with some notable exceptions and some minor changes.

 

17 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Valencia Center, Inc. v. Bystrom


No. 72,548


Supreme Court of Florida


543 So. 2d 214; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 384; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 222



April 27, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Rehearing Denied June 13, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity, Third District - Case Nos. 87-2404, 87-2405, 87-2406, 87-2407, (Dade County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of a decision of the Third District Court of Appeal, Dade County (Florida), which found Fla. Stat. ch. 193.023(6) (1987) unconstitutional and which held that appellee property appraiser had arrived at a correct assessment of appellant's property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant property owner brought suit against appellee property appraiser alleging that appellee's assessment of appellant's property for tax purposes was improper. The court found that appellee's assessment was proper and that Fla. Stat. ch. 193.023(6) was unconstitutional. Appellant challenged the decision. The appellate court affirmed and held that Fla. Stat. ch. 193.023(6) was unconstitutional. The court said that the legislature could not establish different classes of property for tax purposes other than those enumerated in Fla. Const. art. VII, § 4. The court found that appellee arrived at a proper assessment of appellant's property because in arriving at fair market value, a willing buyer most certainly would have considered the zoning of the property, regardless of its current use, and appellee properly considered the potential future use when assessing the property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order that found a statute unconstitutional. The court said that the legislature could not establish different classes of property for tax purposes other than those listed in the state constitution. The court also found that appellee property appraiser correctly assessed appellant's property based on its potential use.

 

18 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Winshare Club of Canada v. Department of Legal Affairs


Nos. 72,924, 73,074


Supreme Court of Florida


542 So. 2d 974; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 271; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 179



April 6, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 5, 1989.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners sought review of a decision of the Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida), which found Fla. Stat. ch. 849.09 (1985) to be constitutional and certified a question regarding whether the commerce clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, prohibited Florida from interfering with the sale of out-of-state lottery tickets within its borders.


OVERVIEW: Respondent sought an injunction prohibiting petitioners' advertisement and promotion of the sale of out-of-state and foreign nations' lottery tickets, alleging a violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 849.09 (1985). The trial court denied the request and declared ch. 849.09 unconstitutional under the commerce clause, U.S. Const. art. I. § 8. The appellate court reversed, certifying a question regarding whether U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, prohibited Florida from interfering with the sale of out-of-state lottery tickets within its borders. The supreme court approved the reversal, holding that ch. 849.09 did not violate the commerce clause and that Florida was not prohibited from regulating the sale of out-of-state lottery tickets within its borders. The court ruled that ch. 849.09 regulated evenhandedly to effectuate a legitimate local public interest where it forbade Florida and out-of-state citizens alike from selling lottery tickets and had only an incidental effect on interstate commerce. Chapter 849.09 was not preempted by federal legislation or as a matter requiring uniform regulation, and selling lottery tickets through the mails and across state lines was unlawful under federal law.


OUTCOME: The court approved the appellate court's ruling that a statute prohibiting the unauthorized sale of out-of-state lottery tickets within Florida's borders was constitutionally valid. The court held that the commerce clause of the U.S. Constitution did not prohibit Florida from interfering with the sale of out-of-state lottery tickets within the state.

Dep't of Business Regulation v. Classic Mile


Nos. 73,119, 73,121


Supreme Court of Florida


541 So. 2d 1155; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 273; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 183



April 6, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory/Constitutional Invalidity, First District - Case No. 87-1950.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A mandatory review was required pursuant to Fla. Const. art. V, § 3(b)(1), of a decision of the First District Court of Appeal (Florida), which declared unconstitutional a law that was codified as Fla. Stat. ch. 550.355(2) (1987).


OVERVIEW: The supreme court was required to review a decision of the district court of appeal which declared unconstitutional Fla. Stat. ch. 550.355(2) (1987) as a special law in the guise of a general law and found it had been enacted in violation of Fla. Const. art. III, § 10. The statute dealt with simulcasts of horse races. The district court determined that the statute was fatally defective even as a general law under Fla. Const. art. III, § 11(b), because there was no reasonable relationship between the express class characteristics enumerated in the statute and the purpose of the legislation. The supreme court agreed with the district court on both points and affirmed its decision. Based on the criteria of the statute, only one county would ever fall within the statutorily designated class of counties eligible for licensure of a facility, thus making the statute a special law. The court also noted that because the primary purpose of ch. 550.355(2) was the establishment of facilities for the receipt of simulcast horse races, there was no important and necessary state function to justify classifying the statute as a general law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the district court declaring a statute unconstitutional because the statute was a special law, which contravened the Florida constitution. The statute failed as a general law because there was no reasonable relationship between the express class characteristics enumerated in the statute, which dealt with simulcasts of horse races, and the purpose of the legislation.

Eutzy v. State

P. 3.850 motion, since the claims were procedurally barred, and denied both his petition for writ of habeas corpus and request for stay of execution because the court's definition of the cold, calculated, and premeditated aggravating factor did not warrant retroactive application.

 

22 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Martinez v. Florida Legislature


No. 73,601


Supreme Court of Florida


542 So. 2d 358; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 252; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 127



March 23, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied May 16, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Leon County, William Gary, Judge, Case No. 88-3976 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 89-90.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Judgment of trial court, in and for Leon County (Florida), certified by the First District Court of Appeal in case involving appellant governor's veto of portions of specific appropriations enacted by appellee legislature.


OVERVIEW: Appellant governor argued that his veto of portions of a line item referred to in an appropriations bill, but only appearing in so-called intent documents, was valid because the letter transmitting the intent documents expressly incorporated the intent documents into the appropriations bill. The court disagreed, ruling that the vetoed items were not specific, identifiable items adopted by appellee legislature in the appropriations bill and did not meet state constitutional requirements that vetoes only apply to specific appropriations that were part of an appropriations bill. Explaining, the court held that the intent documents were not part of the appropriations bill enacted by appellee, because Fla. Stat. Ann. § 216.181(1)(1988) unequivocally and unambiguously provided that the statement of intent could not appropriate funds. Not being part of the appropriations bill, appellant's veto could not reach the intent documents or the contested portions of the line item, the court added. The court concluded that the statement of intent merely provided guidance on how appropriations should be spent, ruling that only specific appropriations in an appropriations bill were enforceable.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed expunging appellant governor's veto of portions of specific appropriations enacted by appellee legislature, because portions vetoed, incorporated by reference into appropriations bill from intent documents, were invalid, because intent documents -- statutorily barred from allocating funds -- were not part of appropriations bill that a gubernatorial veto could constitutionally reach, but mere documents of guidance.

Ivey v. Bacardi Imports, Co.


No. 73,424


Supreme Court of Florida


541 So. 2d 1129; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 201; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 129



March 23, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] District Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Leon County, Charles E. Miner, Jr., Judge - Case No. 88-2881 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 88-3033.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state agency director over alcoholic beverages regulation, and intervenors, Florida alcohol beverage producers, sought review of the final judgment of the Trial Court, Leon County (Florida), which declared amendments to state's alcoholic beverage tax scheme, Fla. Stat. ch. 564.06 and 565.12 (1988) unconstitutional under the commerce clause. The question was certified to the court by the First District Court of Appeal (Florida).


OVERVIEW: Appellees, an importer and a distributor of alcoholic beverages, filed suit contending that an import tax on imported alcoholic beverages violated the commerce clause, the export-import clause, and the equal protection clause of the United States Constitution. The trial court found the U.S. Const. amend. XXI purposes allegedly served by the legislation were illusory and, therefore, insufficient to validate the discriminatory tax. Appellants, a state director and two in-state alcohol producer intervenors sought review. The lower appellate court certified the action to the court herein. The court held that the interests which the state maintained were furthered by this legislation were not substantial enough to outweigh the federal interest in free and unrestricted trade among the several states. Inter alia, the court found, the asserted interest in enhancement of the state's regulatory control over the distribution chain of wines and distilled spirits was likewise insufficient to outweigh the clear federal interest implicated. The court affirmed the lower court's decision that Fla. Stat. ch. 564.06(1 -10) (1988) and Fla. Stat. ch. 565.12(1 - 5) (1988), were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision in favor of appellees finding amendments to state's alcoholic beverage tax laws unconstitutional under the commerce clause. The court upheld the trial court's finding that the amendments discriminated against interstate commerce. The court held the state's Twenty-first Amendment interests were not sufficiently implicated to allow a clearly discriminatory tax scheme to stand.

Carr v. Broward County


No. 70,545


Supreme Court of Florida


541 So. 2d 92; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 169; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 110



March 16, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 1, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions, Fourth District - Case Nos. 85-2690, 85-2820 and 4-86-0209.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners sought review of a decision from the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions, Fourth District (Florida) that dismissed their action against respondent hospital and physicians to recover for brain damage suffered by petitioners' child as a result of respondents' negligent treatment. The district court concluded the action was barred by the statute of repose contained in Fla. Stat. Ann. § 95.11(4)(b) (1975).


OVERVIEW: Petitioners filed a complaint against respondent hospital and physicians, alleging respondents' negligent treatment caused severe brain damage in petitioners' child. The district court dismissed petitioners' action, holding it was barred by the statute of repose contained in Fla. Stat. Ann. § 95.11(4)(b) (1975). Petitioners argued the ten-year lapse between the birth of the child and the filing of the complaint was excusable because they were unable to discover the facts and circumstances surrounding prenatal and obstetrical care and the care rendered during birth. The court noted, under § 95.11(4)(b), a statute of repose of seven years was applicable where there was an allegation that fraud, concealment, or intentional misrepresentation of fact prevented discovery of the negligent conduct. Because the legislature found an overriding public necessity in its enactment of § 95.11(4)(b), and no less stringent measure would have obviated the problems the legislature sought to address, the court held the statute was constitutionally enacted and barred petitioners' medical malpractice action. Accordingly, the district court's decision was approved.


OUTCOME: The decision that dismissed petitioners' complaint was approved because petitioners did not bring their medical malpractice claim within the seven-year limitations period, and the limitations period was constitutionally valid because the legislature found an overriding public necessity in its enactment of the statute of repose, and no less stringent measure would have obviated the problems the legislature sought to address.

De Ayala v. Florida Farm Bureau Casualty Ins. Co.


No. 70,308


Supreme Court of Florida


543 So. 2d 204; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 163; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 92



March 9, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Rehearing Denied June 12, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity, Fourth District - Case No. 85-1588 (St. Lucie County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, the wife and minor children of a worker killed while working in Florida, sought review of a decision of the Fourth District Court of Appeal, St. Lucie County (Florida), that upheld the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. Ann. § 440.16(7) (1983). Section 440.16(7) provided that the workers' dependents were not eligible for full workers' compensation benefits because they did not reside in the United States or Canada.


OVERVIEW: After decedent was killed while working in Florida, petitioners, decedent's wife and minor children residing in Mexico, filed a claim with respondent workers' compensation insurer for benefits. Citing as authority Fla. Stat. Ann. § 440.16(7) (statute), respondent insurer issued a check for only $ 1,000. Petitioners filed suit for declaratory relief on grounds that § 440.16(7) was unconstitutional as a violation of the equal protection clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, the due process clauses of the Florida and United States Constitutions, and the access to courts provision of the Florida Constitution. The trial court found that § 440.16(7) arbitrarily discriminated against resident aliens killed in work-related accidents whose dependents were not residents of the United States or Canada and declared the statute unconstitutional. The appellate court reversed, and petitioners sought review. The court held the statute was unconstitutional because it used alienage as a classifier and could not pass the heightened scrutiny applicable when official discrimination occurred based on alienage. The court, therefore, quashed the decision below and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the decision below and remanded the case for further proceedings after holding that a state statute that used alienage as a classifier could not pass heightened scrutiny and was unconstitutional.

Supreme Court of Florida

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court accepted an application for review of a decision from the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida), which affirmed a trial court's decision to cap petitioner attorney's fees in a murder case at $ 3500.00 pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 925.036(2)(d) (1985).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner attorney represented a criminal defendant in a death penalty case and moved for attorney fees of $ 6700. The trial court denied the request because Fla. 29 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Magaw v. State


No. 72,419


Supreme Court of Florida


537 So. 2d 564; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 22; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 27



January 12, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance, First District - Case No. BS-353, Escambia County


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The action was before the court after the First District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified a question as being of great public importance. The question was whether a case that held there was no causation requirement in the manslaughter by intoxication statute was still valid in light of Fla. Stat. ch. 316.193(3)(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of manslaughter by intoxication. The district court denied defendant's claim that the trial court erred in denying her request to argue causation to the jury. The court answered in the negative the question whether a case that held causation was not required in order to convict under the manslaughter by intoxication statute was still valid. The court concluded Fla. Stat. ch. 316.193, the new statute as amended, required a finding of causation because the court's analysis of the legislative history of the statute made clear that causation was required. However, the new statute did not say that the driver of the vehicle had to be the sole cause of the accident. The new statute did not require the state to prove that the driver's drinking caused the accident. The new statute only required that the operation of the vehicle caused the accident. Any lack of care on the part of the drunken driver to which a fatal accident could be attributed sufficed. The new statute did not apply to defendant because it was effective after the accident.


OUTCOME: The court answered in the negative the question whether a case that held there was no causation requirement in the manslaughter by intoxication statute was still valid. The court found that the new statute required a finding of causation, but that any lack of care on the part of the drunken driver to which a fatal accident could be attributed sufficed to satisfy the requirement that operation of the vehicle caused the fatal accident.

 

30 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Glock v. Dugger


Nos. 73,363, 73,493


Supreme Court of Florida


537 So. 2d 99; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 30; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 29



January 12, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus and An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County, Wayne L. Cobb, Judge - Case No. CR 83-1383.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court was defendant's habeas corpus petition, a request for a stay of execution, and an appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County (Florida), which denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief from his murder conviction and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and co-defendant kidnapped the victim and robbed her. Defendant killed the victim after co-defendant had previously shot her. Defendant raised two claims from the denial of his motion for postconviction relief. Defendant claimed that the admission of codefendant's confession was erroneous and that trial counsel was ineffective. The court affirmed the decision denying defendant's motion for postconviction relief. There was no error in the admission of codefendant's confession. Defendant and codefendant entered into a joint confession resolving all prior inconsistencies in their statements. Codefendant's confession was sufficiently reliable and did not prejudice defendant. Trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to obtain information from defendant's family to aid mental health experts in showing deficiencies in defendant's personality that affected defendant's confession. Trial counsel had three experts assist him in determining whether defendant's mental condition could be utilized during trial or penalty phase. Defendant's additional information was not new, and defendant's family testified to the substance of his family background.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's habeas corpus petition and request for stay of execution and affirmed the circuit court's denial of defendant's motion for postconviction relief. Admission of codefendant's confession was not erroneous because the confession was sufficiently reliable given that defendant and codefendant entered into a joint confession and ironed out prior inconsistencies in their statements.

 

31 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Texaco, Inc. v. Department of Transp.


No. 71,914


Supreme Court of Florida


537 So. 2d 92; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 12; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 5



January 5, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance, Second District - Case No. 87-1171, Pinellas County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The action was before the court after the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified a question as being of great importance. The question certified was whether a lessee of property taken by eminent domain was entitled to business damages pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 73.071(3)(b) (1985) when the lessee was a wholesale supplier of products to a sublessee who actually operated a retail business on the property.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was a long-term lessee that subleased an automobile service station to a dealer and was the wholesale supplier of products to the dealer. Petitioner claimed it was entitled to business damages under Fla. Stat. ch. 73.071(3)(b) (1985) after respondent state transportation department instituted eminent domain proceedings as to part of the property. The court found that petitioner was not entitled to business damages under ch. 73.071(3)(b). Petitioner did not have the requisite physical existence on the condemned property to be entitled to business damages. The employees of the service station were employees of the dealer, not petitioner. Operating losses incurred by the service station were borne by the dealer. Petitioner did not possess a license to do business at the location and did not sell gas to the public at that location. The fact that ch. 73.071 distinguished between wholesalers and retailers did not violate equal protection because it did not create an unreasonable, unconstitutional classification.


OUTCOME: The court answered in the negative the certified question of whether a lessee of property and wholesale supplier of products to a sublessee who actually operated a retail business on the property was entitled to business damages after the property was partially taken by eminent domain proceedings. A wholesaler was entitled to business damages only if it were conducting its wholesale business on the condemned property.

The court remanded the case for resentencing with directions that the sentence imposed be pursuant to the constitutional guidelines, with no departure permitted. The court vacated the new sentence imposed after appellant was convicted of burglary and sexual battery because it departed from the replacement guidelines, which were constitutional.

Watson v. First Florida Leasing, Inc.


No. 71,717


Supreme Court of Florida


537 So. 2d 1370; 1989 Fla. LEXIS 27; 14 Fla. L. Weekly 1



January 5, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions, Third District - Case Nos. 86-1751 & 86-2492 (Dade County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon application for review of the decision of the District Court of Appeal, Third District, Dade County (Florida), which reversed an order that struck respondent's probate claim for failing to file notice of an independent action pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 733.705(3) (1985), which directly conflicted with Fla. R. Prob. & Guardianship P. 5.065, which required petitioner personal representative to file the notice.


OVERVIEW: The court approved the district court's order reversing the probate court's order. Petitioner, the personal representative of an estate, objected to respondent's claim against the estate, and respondent filed an independent action, but failed to file a notice with the probate court under Fla. Stat. ch. 733.705(3) (1985). The probate court ordered the claim stricken, but on appeal the district court reversed, finding a conflict with Fla. R. Prob. & Guardianship P. 5.065, which required the personal representative to file the notice. On review the court found there was a dual responsibility to report the action, and one did not negate the other. The court found that the notice requirement served to give notice to all persons interested in or potentially affected by the suit, was not jurisdictional, and did not warrant dismissal if respondent demonstrated that no harm to an interested party resulted by the failure. Dismissal is the most significant penalty possible and should not be used in rule violations where less severe penalties exist. Because petitioner had actual notice of the action and the same duty to report it as respondent, there was no harm by the failure to file notice.


OUTCOME: The district court's order reversing the probate court's order striking respondent's independent claim was approved because both parties had the responsibility to file notice, petitioner personal representative was on actual notice of the claim, and no harm was caused by the failure to file the notice. The court noted that the notice requirement was not jurisdictional, like the time requirement, and did not warrant dismissal absent harm.

 

34 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Chandler v. State


No. 69,708


Supreme Court of Florida


534 So. 2d 701; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 1295; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 713



December 8, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for St. Lucie County, William G. Tye, Judge - Case No. 84-1329 CF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the St. Lucie County Circuit Court (Florida), which imposed sentences of death upon resentencing pursuant to a remand from the appellate court. Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly admitted hearsay statements in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141(1) and that the admission of hearsay violated his right of confrontation under U.S. Const. amend. VI.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. The convictions were affirmed on appeal but the sentence was vacated. Upon remand, a new sentencing phase trial was held and defendant again received death sentences for the murders. Defendant appealed and the court affirmed the sentences, rejecting defendant's claim that his U.S. Const. amend. VI confrontation right had been violated by the admission of hearsay statements. Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141(1) provided the trial judge wide leeway in admitting evidence in a sentencing hearing, including hearsay, subject to defendant's fair opportunity to rebut any hearsay statements. The hearsay admitted concerned the testimony of other witnesses in the guilt phase of the trial where those witnesses had been subject to cross-examination by the defense. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutional as applied in this case and that the trial court had not abused its discretion in admitting the hearsay statements. The court also, sua sponte, reviewed the imposition of the death sentences and found that they were justified by several aggravating factors and the absence of any mitigating factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's death sentences, holding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in permitting hearsay testimony in the sentencing phase regarding the testimony of other witnesses in the guilt phase of the trial. The non-testifying witnesses had been subject to cross-examination in the guilt phase and defendant had a fair opportunity to rebut the hearsay evidence in the sentencing trial.

Perez v. State

On appeal, the court affirmed. Chapter 90.803(23) was constitutional, and the trial judge correctly applied the provisions of the statute to petitioner's case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of both the lower appellate court and the trial court, concluding that the statute was both constitutional and correctly applied in petitioner's case.

Glendening v. State

Stat. ch. 90.803(23) (1985), which governed the admission of hearsay statements of a child victim of sexual abuse.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted and sentenced to life in prison with a mandatory minimum 25 years of incarceration for sexual battery upon a child 11 years of age or younger, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 794.011(2) (1985). On appeal, the conviction and sentence were affirmed. Petitioner appealed the intermediate court's ruling, which rejected petitioner's arguments that the trial court erred in admitting videotaped testimony of the alleged victim, petitioner's 3.5-year-old daughter, under Fla. The appellate court upheld the intermediate court's ruling that affirmed petitioner's conviction and sentence. The court concluded that the intermediate court correctly held that ch. 90.803(23) was constitutional and was properly applied.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the intermediate court ruling that affirmed petitioner's conviction and sentence. Sandlin v. Criminal Justice Standards & Training Com.


No. 71,104


Supreme Court of Florida


531 So. 2d 1344; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 1142; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 619



October 13, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance, First District - Case No. BJ-283.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The First District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified the issue of whether a full pardon of a person convicted of a felony, relieves the pardoned person from disqualification from certification as a law enforcement officer, as imposed by Fla. Stat. Ann. § 943.13(4).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was employed as a court bailiff. When petitioner was very young he was convicted of robbery, escape, and assault. Petitioner later received a full pardon from the governor. The sheriff's office asked respondent, the Criminal Justice Standards & Training Commission, to certify petitioner as a police officer. Respondent refused certification because it determined that the legislature did not intend to allow a pardoned felon to hold the sensitive position of law enforcement officer. The court remanded, ordering respondent to reconsider petitioner's request for certification consistent with its opinion. The court held that while a full pardon removes all disabilities resulting from a crime, persons seeking to practice certain professions or employments can be required to demonstrate their good moral character, even though they may have been fully pardoned for previous crimes.


OUTCOME: The court remanded and ordered respondent to reconsider petitioner's request for certification, holding that even though they may have been fully pardoned for previous crimes, persons seeking to practice certain professions or employments can be required to demonstrate their good moral character.

 

38 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


State v. Grassi


No. 69,359


Supreme Court of Florida


532 So. 2d 1055; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 1118; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 604



October 6, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 21, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity, Fourth District - Case No. 85-1360 (Broward County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the decision of the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District, Broward County (Florida), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the charge filed against defendant for knowingly and unlawfully qualifying as a candidate for Broward County Commissioner, District #3, without being a resident of the county in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 99.032.


OVERVIEW: Defendant submitted qualifying papers so that he could run for county commissioner in Broward County, District #4. After learning that the seat for District #4 was not open, he changed his papers to run for District #3, even though he was a resident of District #4 at that time. Defendant was charged with violating Fla. Stat. ch. 99.032 by knowingly and unlawfully qualifying as a candidate for Broward County Commissioner, District #3, even though he was not a resident of that district when he qualified as a candidate. Defendant's motion to dismiss the charge against him was granted, and plaintiff appealed. The appeals court affirmed the dismissal of the charge because the trial court properly held that ch. 99.032 was unconstitutional, as Fla. Const. art. VIII, § 1(e) enumerated the requirements for the office of county commissioner and that the legislature could not impose additional requirements. Thus, because Fla. Const. art. VIII, § 1(e) required residency at the time of election, ch. 99.032 was unconstitutional because it imposed an additional qualification for the office of county commissioner by requiring the candidate to be a resident of county when he qualified to run.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision to grant defendant's motion to dismiss was affirmed because the Florida Constitution required that defendant be a resident of the county in which he sought election as county commissioner as of the time of election. Thus, the law requiring that a candidate for county commissioner to be a resident of the county when he qualified to run was unconstitutional because it imposed an additional qualification for the office.

Lanca Homeowners, Inc. v. Lantana Cascade of Palm Beach, Ltd.


No. 71,767


Supreme Court of Florida


541 So. 2d 1121; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 1034; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 568



September 22, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 25, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity, Fourth District - Case No. 87-0315


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both parties challenged an order of the Fourth District Court of Appeal, which held that Fla. Stat. ch. 723.079(1) (1985) was unconstitutional and could not be used as a basis for finding that appellant mobile homeowner's association had standing to bring a counterclaim in appellee corporation's action for declaratory relief. Appellee corporation challenged the finding that the counterclaim could be maintained as a class action.


OVERVIEW: Both parties challenged the district court's order that a counterclaim filed by appellant association, which represented mobile home owners in a park owned by appellee corporation, was maintainable in an declaratory judgment action filed by appellee corporation. The trial court had found that appellant association was an appropriate class representative under Fla. Stat. ch. 723.079(1) (1985). The district court ruled that the counterclaim itself was suitable for presentation as a class action. However, the district court held that the statute was unconstitutional and could not be used as a basis for finding that appellant association had standing to represent the class. Appellant association challenged the finding that it was an improper class representative, and appellee corporation cross-appealed the finding that the counterclaim was maintainable. The supreme court reversed, holding that while the statute was unconstitutional because it constituted an intrusion on the court's rulemaking authority, the unique features of mobile home residency required adoption of a procedural format to allow associations like appellant association to represent members of such class of homeowners.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the portion of the district court's opinion that found the statute at issue unconstitutional and that found appellant association's counterclaim maintainable. The supreme court reversed the portion of the opinion that found appellant association an improper class representative. The statute was an unconstitutional intrusion on the court's rulemaking authority, and the counterclaim was maintainable as a class action.

Lamb v. State


No. 70,369


Supreme Court of Florida


532 So. 2d 1051; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 924; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 530

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder, burglary with assault, and grand theft, and sentenced him to death for the murder.

Defendant was indicted and a jury returned guilty verdicts for first-degree premeditated murder, felony murder, burglary with assault, and grand theft. The circuit court imposed the jury's recommended sentence of death for the first-degree murder, 40 years imprisonment for the burglary, and 5 years imprisonment for the grand theft. The court found that the murder was heinous, atrocious, and cruel because defendant planned the burglary and theft, planned violence to the victim in perpetrating the theft, brought a weapon to the scene, and after committing the felony, he concealed himself and waited for the victim to return because of his pique at the frugal results of the burglary. The court found that resentencing was necessary because the circuit court erred in failing to utilize the sentencing scoresheet in sentencing defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions, but vacated the sentences because it was not sure whether the circuit court properly considered all the mitigating evidence or whether it found that the aggravation outweighed the mitigation, and remanded the matter for resentencing.

Hildwin v. State


No. 69,513


Supreme Court of Florida


531 So. 2d 124; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 955; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 528

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from judgment by the Circuit Court of Hernando County (Florida), which found defendant guilty of first-degree murder and imposed a sentence of death, for the strangulation and rape of a 42-year-old woman whose body was found in the trunk of her car, which was hidden in dense woods.

OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction of first-degree murder and death sentence was affirmed over several meritless allegations of procedural and evidentiary error. The fact that an unsworn juror caught sight of defendant in the custody of the sheriff did not constitute error.

Department of Transp. v. Fortune Federal Sav. & Loan Asso.


No. 70,680


Supreme Court of Florida


532 So. 2d 1267; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 1210; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 466



August 18, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Original Opinion of August 18, 1988 Substituted. Motion for Rehearing or Clarification Denied October 17, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal -- Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity and An Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal -- Certified Great Public Importance, Second District, Case No. 86-955.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a decision from the District Court of Appeal, Second District (Florida), which held for appellee landowner and declared Fla. Stat. ch. 337.27(3) (1985), which permitted condemnation of more land than necessary if it would reduce acquisition costs, unconstitutional. Appellant argued that ch. 337.27(3) satisfied a public purpose, and thus was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Under Florida's eminent domain laws, if only part of a property was condemned, its owner was entitled to recover, under Fla. Stat. ch. 73.071(3)(b) (1985), in addition to the value of the property, all business damages that resulted from the condemnation. If the entire property was condemned, business damages were not recoverable. Fla. Stat. ch. 337.27(3) (1985) allowed condemnation of more property than was necessary if the cost of doing so was less than condemning only what was necessary. The state sought to save $ 2 million by condemning all of appellee landowner's property at a certain location. The court quashed the judgment that declared ch. 337.23(3) unconstitutional. The court held that the allowance of business damages in ch. 73.071(3)(b) was a matter of legislative grace only; thus ch. 337.23(3) did not effect a taking of property to the extent of business damages, and did not implicate constitutional considerations unless it was arbitrary or capricious. The court held that the declared public purpose of ch. 337.23(3), which was to save money, was valid, and that ch. 337.23(3) was, therefore, not arbitrary or capricious, and not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the decision in favor of appellee landowner, and held that the statute that permitted appellant state to condemn more property than it needed to implement a valid public purpose was constitutional. The court held that this statute, which effectively limited the damages appellee could recover for the condemnation, was not arbitrary or capricious, and thus constitutional, because it fulfilled a valid public purpose.
