The Florida Bar re Schwarz


No. 70,702


Supreme Court of Florida


526 So. 2d 56; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 675; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 373



June 2, 1988 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorney applied for the appointment of an ad hoc commission to study the authority the state bar was given by the court to exercise political power.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner attorney sought appointment of an ad hoc commission to study the authority the court had to exercise political power through the activities of the state bar. Petitioner argued the court had improperly failed to place limits on the scope of its delegation of political activity to the bar. The court first noted that, prior to making his application at issue, petitioner had proposed a state bar rule amendment, yet to be ruled upon, that prohibited the bar from engaging in political activities not directly related to the organization. The court also held that it had previously rejected a prior proposed amendment prohibiting the bar from engaging in any political activity. In refusing petitioner's application for appointment of a commission, the court nonetheless noted that other jurisdictions restricted the scope of a state bar's political authority to those activities directly related to the organization's purpose of regulating its membership. The court refused to decide precisely which of a state bar's activities were improper, but ordered the issue reviewed by the state bar in light of the decisions of other jurisdictions restricting the authority of their state bars.


OUTCOME: Petitioner's application for appointment of an ad hoc commission to study the court's political authority through the activities of the state bar was denied; however the state bar's board of governors were directed to study the issue in light of analogous decisions in other jurisdictions restricting the scope of bar political activities.

Harmon v. State

Supreme Court of Florida


527 So. 2d 182; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 593; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 332

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Marion County, William T. Swigert, Sr., Judge - Case No. 85-2454-CF-B-X.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction and death sentence from the Circuit Court in and for Marion County (Florida) for first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: An accomplice told the police that he and appellant had been with victim and appellant shot victim and then took his wallet. A statement that appellant was previously convicted of a felony which involved the use or threat of violence to another person was contained in a written report. The jury could have reasonably questioned the degree of participation by accomplice, together with the disparity between the maximum sentence for accomplice and a recommendation of death for appellant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction because the evidence was more than sufficient to support the conviction and any errors were harmless. National Distributing Co. v. Office of Comptroller


No. 71,638


Supreme Court of Florida


523 So. 2d 156; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 445; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 248



April 7, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Direct Appeal and Cross-Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Leon County, Charles E. Miner, Jr., Judge Case No. 87-1260 - Certified by District Court of Appeal, First District - Case No. 87-1859.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida), certified an appeal from a summary judgment granted by the trial court in favor of appellee, the Office of the Comptroller for the State of Florida, in appellants' action for a refund of excise taxes they paid on alcoholic beverages they distributed in Florida. The trial court also denied mandamus and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: Appellants challenged Fla. Stat. ch. 564.06 and 564.12 (1981 to 1984 Supp.), which imposed an excise tax on alcoholic beverages they distributed in Florida. Appellants argued that because the tax expressly favored alcoholic beverages produced from Florida-grown products by granting them tax exemptions, it was unconstitutional and the state was thus required to refund taxes to the extent it discriminated against interstate commerce. The trial court granted summary judgment against appellants. In light of a decision by the United States Supreme Court, which held that commerce clause restrictions applied to state taxing schemes that favored in-state manufacturers of such beverages, and its own prior decision, the court favored the trial court's conclusion that certain provisions of the taxing statutes violated the commerce clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8. The court held, however, that its decision was only to be given prospective application because an unreasonable disruption of state government would be caused by retroactive application and an unconscionable windfall would have accrued to appellants who had already passed the tax onto their customers. The decision below was approved.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment to appellee, the Office of the Comptroller for the State of Florida, and a refund of excise taxes denied to appellant distributors, were affirmed. Although the court agreed with appellants that certain excise tax statutes were constitutional, it opted to apply its decision prospectively, because retroactive application would have severely disrupted state government and appellants would have received an unconscionable windfall.

Hillsborough County Governmental Employees Ass'n v. Hillsborough County Aviation Auth.


No. 68,336


Supreme Court of Florida


522 So. 2d 358; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 371; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 199



March 17, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance, Second District - Case No. 85-867.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A question was certified for review from a judgment from the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida), which reversed the administrative order in favor of petitioner negotiators which had held that respondent public employers had committed an unfair labor practice by refusing to implement the new provisions under the parties' collective bargaining agreement.


OVERVIEW: On review, the appellate court quashed that portion of the district court of appeal's judgment that conflicted with the appellate court's decision. OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded with directions to enter a prospective administrative order holding that respondent public employers had committed an unfair labor practice by refusing to implement the new provisions under the parties' collective bargaining agreement because the statute granting respondents the authority to amend such agreements was unconstitutional as applied to the instant situation.

 

48 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Celotex Corp. v. Meehan


Nos. 66,937, 66,938, 66,939


Supreme Court of Florida


523 So. 2d 141; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 378; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P11,718; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 204



March 17, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Case No. 66,937 Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal, Certified Great Public Importance, Third District, Case No. 82-122. Case No. 66,938 Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal, Certified Great Public Importance, Third District, Case No. 81-382. Case No. 66,939 Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal, Direct Conflict of Decisions, Third District, Case No. 84-507.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Third District Court of Appeals (Florida) certified for review three cases that raised questions as to the application of Florida's borrowing statute, Fla. Sta. ch. 95.10 (1979), to asbestosis claims.


OVERVIEW: The court certified for review three cases that raised questions as to the application of Florida's borrowing statute, Fla. Sta. ch. 95.10 (1979), to asbestosis claims that arose from asbestos exposure in other states. The court noted that whether the borrowing statute would be applied depended on whether the claim had "significant relationships" with Florida. If there were no such significant relationships, the other state's limitations period would apply. The court further noted that under Florida law, a cause of action did not accrue for limitation purposes until the injured party discovered or had a duty to discover the act constituting an invasion of his legal rights; but that this was not the law in many other states. Applying these principles, the court found that in one case, the claim had a significant relationship to Florida, and so Florida's limitation period would apply; in another case, there was no such significant relationship, and the action was time-barred under the rules of the state in which the asbestos exposure had occurred. The court remanded the third case, finding that it could not determine whether the claim had a significant relationship with Florida.


OUTCOME: The court held that Florida's borrowing statute did not apply to extend the statute of limitations for a claim of asbestosis that arose from asbestos exposure in another state unless the claim had significant relationships with Florida. Applying these principles, it quashed all three of the lower court decisions for reasons particular to each case.

 

49 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cogswell


No. 70,647


Supreme Court of Florida


521 So. 2d 1081; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 335; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 193



March 10, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal, Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity, Fourth District, Case No. 4-86-1029.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prosecution challenged a decision of the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) that concluded that Fla. Stat. ch. 849.25 was constitutionally invalid to the extent that it permitted the prosecution as a felony of the same conduct treated as a misdemeanor under Fla. Stat. ch. 849.14.


OVERVIEW: Appellant prosecution challenged a determination that Fla. Stat. ch. 849.25, which dealt with bookmaking, was constitutionally invalid to the extent that it permitted the prosecution as a felony of the same conduct treated as a misdemeanor under Fla. Stat. ch. 849.14. In concluding that the statute was constitutional and reversing the lower court decision, the state supreme court concluded that there was no appreciable difference between the discretion a prosecutor exercised when deciding whether to charge under one of two statutes with different elements and the discretion exercised when choosing between statutes with identical elements. While the prosecutor may be influenced by the penalties available upon conviction, this fact alone did not establish an equal protection or due process violation. Further, it was not unusual for criminal conduct to violate laws that overlapped yet varied in their penalties, and the state legislature traditionally left to the prosecutor's discretion those violations to prosecute and that range of penalties to seek in punishment of a criminal offense. The matter was remanded for a trial of appellee.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court of appeal was reversed, for the sole fact that one state statute treated conduct as a felony that was treated as a misdemeanor under another state statute was insufficient to establish a due process or equal protection violation sufficient to render the former unconstitutional. The matter was remanded for trial the appellee.

In re Advisory Opinion to Attorney Gen., etc.


No. 71,701


Supreme Court of Florida


520 So. 2d 284; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 220; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 170



February 26, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Original Proceeding - Advisory Opinion to the Attorney General Limitation Of Non-Economic Damages In Civil Actions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state attorney general requested an advisory opinion (Florida) on the validity of an initiative petition amending Fla. Const. art. I, § 21 to place a cap on non-economic damages in civil actions.


OVERVIEW: Exercising its jurisdiction under Fla. Const. art. IV, § 10 and Fla. Stat. ch. 16.061 (1987), the court reviewed petitioner state attorney general's request for an advisory opinion on the validity of an initiative petition amending Fla. Const. art. I, § 21 to place a cap on non-economic damages in civil actions. Section one of the proposed amendment set forth a non-inclusive list of economic damages. Section two provided a method of adjusting the cap through use of the consumer price index. Section three provided a severability clause and an effective date. The court held that the proposed amendment contained a single subject and directly related matter and, thus, met the legal requirements of Fla. Const. art. XI, § 3. The court also held that the ballot summary accurately tracked and described the proposed amendment and, thus, complied with Fla. Stat. ch. 101.161.


OUTCOME: The court held valid the initiative petition and ballot summary for amending the state constitution to place a cap on non-economic damages in civil actions.

 

51 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Tafero v. Dugger


No. 71,946


Supreme Court of Florida


520 So. 2d 287; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 229; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 161



February 26, 1988 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death, petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus (Florida) for relief under Hitchcock, based on the trial judge and jury's limited consideration of mitigating circumstances.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. After numerous state and federal court proceedings, petitioner filed for writ of habeas corpus requesting relief under Hitchcock. Petitioner alleged that the trial judge restricted his mitigating evidence and the jury's consideration of mitigating evidence to those circumstances listed in Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141(6) (1975). Petitioner claimed that, even though he presented no mitigating evidence at sentencing, the trial judge and jury could have gleaned certain nonstatutory mitigating evidence from the guilt phase. This evidence included residual doubt about the extent of petitioner's participation in the crime and his guilt, the disparate treatment of petitioner's co-defendants, and petitioner being a father. Noting the weakness of the nonstatutory mitigating evidence, petitioner's waiver of presenting and arguing mitigating evidence, the overwhelming evidence of guilt, and substantial aggravating factors, the court found that any Hitchcock error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. Accordingly, the court denied the petition for writ of habeas corpus and denied petitioner's request for a stay of execution.


OUTCOME: Finding that any Hitchcock error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt, the court denied petitioner's request for a writ of habeas corpus and denied his request for a stay of execution.

 

52 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Combs v. State


No. 68,477


Supreme Court of Florida


525 So. 2d 853; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 167; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 142



February 18, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 27, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Lee County, Thomas S. Reese, Judge - Case No. 79-465CF-TSR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court in and for Lee County (Florida), which denied his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion to vacate his conviction and death sentence. Appellant argued that counsel was ineffective, that the sentencing phase was tainted by the failure to consider nonstatutory mitigating factors as well as prosecutorial comment and jury instructions that denigrated the jury's advisory role.


OVERVIEW: The court summarily vacated appellant's death sentence and remanded for a new sentencing hearing, because the trial court limited its and the jury's consideration of mitigating factors to those statutorily enumerated. The court summarily affirmed the conviction, finding no ineffective assistance. The court then held that the role of the sentencing jury in Florida's capital sentencing process was indeed advisory. The court held that the jury instructions accurately stated the jury's advisory role, citing Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141 (1985), and did not disparage or denigrate that role in the sentencing process. The court acknowledged that it was constitutionally impermissible to rest a death sentence on a determination made by a sentencer who had been led to believe that the responsibility for determining the appropriateness of the defendant's death lay elsewhere. The court reiterated, however, that under Florida law, the judge was solely responsible for assessing capital punishment; the jury was not empowered with the final sentencing decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction, but vacated his death sentence and remanded for resentencing. The court held that appellant's sentencing hearing unconstitutionally failed to permit consideration of nonstatutory mitigating factors. The court held, however, that jury instructions and prosecutorial comment to the effect that the jury's role was advisory were correct and did not disparage the jury's role.

 

53 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Grossman v. State


No. 68,096


Supreme Court of Florida


525 So. 2d 833; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 279; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 127



February 18, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Revised, Justice Shaw's Specially Concurring Opinion Modified and Rehearing Denied May 25, 1988, Reported at: 1988 Fla. LEXIS 971.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Crockett Farnell, Judge - Case No. CRC 84-11698 CFANO-K. Previously Reported at: 1988 Fla. LEXIS 972.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction of first-degree murder and the death sentence imposed by the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida). Appellant cited numerous errors, inter alia, introduction of codefendant's statement in the joint trial; state and court's denigration of the importance of the jury's recommended sentence of life or death; application of aggravating factors; and lack of written findings on the death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death for the killing of a wildlife officer in an effort to avoid arrest. The court held it was error to admit codefendant's statement in the joint trial as evidence against codefendant only, but this error was harmless under the facts and circumstances of the case. Further the court found that the prosecutor correctly stated during voir dire: that the judge is the sentencing authority and the jury's role, merely advisory. The trial court's instructions fully advised the jury of the importance of its role and correctly stated the law. The court further found that under Florida's death penalty statute, appeal was automatic and under Fla. R. App. P. 9.140(b)(4), governing capital appeals, the trial court retained concurrent jurisdiction for preparation of the complete trial record for filing in the appellate court. Since the trial judge's written findings were made prior to the certification of the record to the appellate court there was no error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence. The court found that by appellant's failure to make a timely objection to the introduction of the victim impact evidence procedurally barred appellant from claiming relief under Booth. The court also held it was error to admit codefendant's statement in the joint trial as evidence against codefendant only, but that this error was harmless under the facts and circumstances of the case.

Division of Alcoholic Beverages & Tobacco, Dep't of Business Regulation v. McKesson Corp.


No. 70,368


Supreme Court of Florida


524 So. 2d 1000; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 214; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 120



February 18, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Three Consolidated Direct Appeals and a Cross-Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Leon County, Charles E. Miner, Jr., Judge, Case Nos. 86-2997, 86-3430 & 86-773. Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case Nos BS-402, BS-304 & BS-404.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, Department of Alcoholic Beverages and Tobacco, sought review of the trial court's order, which found portions of Fla. Stat. Ann. §§ 654.06 and 565.12 (1985) to be unconstitutional. Two appellees, wholesale distributors and manufacturers of alcoholic beverages, filed cross-appeals. The First District Court of Appeal (Florida) consolidated cases and certified cause to the court for it involved a question of great public importance.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, wholesale distributors and manufacturers of alcoholic beverages, brought an action against appellant, Department of Alcoholic Beverages and Tobacco, which challenged the revised tax scheme in Fla. Stat. Ann. §§ 564.06 and 565.12 (1985) that granted exemptions or tax preferences to wines and distilled spirits manufactured from citrus, sugar cane, and certain grape species, all of which were grown in Florida or were from by-products or concentrates thereof. Appellees claimed the preference and disqualification provisions under the new tax scheme discriminated in favor of local commerce and against interstate commerce contrary to the mandates of an applicable case. The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of appellees, appellant sought review, and the appellate court certified the cause to the court as a question that involved great public importance. The court found the tax scheme placed a clear discriminatory burden on interstate commerce, and the state failed to justify in terms of legitimate local benefits other than the admitted benefits to local industry flowing from the statute; therefore, the challenged provisions violated the commerce clause.


OUTCOME: Because the court found that the challenged tax preference scheme violated the commerce clause, it affirmed the summary judgment on that basis. The court noted that a state may not constitutionally impose a discriminatory burden upon the business of other states, merely to protect and promote local business.

 

56 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Department of Revenue v. General American Transp. Corp.


Nos. 69,756, 69,757 (Consolidated)


Supreme Court of Florida


521 So. 2d 112; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 281; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 115



February 18, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 29, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance, First District - Case No. BI-257, and An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity, First District - Case No. BI-257.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Department of Revenue applied for review of a decision of the District Court of Appeal (Florida), which held unconstitutional, as applied, the ad valorem taxation of private line railroad cars under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 193.085(4)(1979), and the issue was whether the assessment was unconstitutionally discriminatory in that the similarly situated rolling stock of nonresident railroads was not similarly assessed.


OVERVIEW: Respondents, as private carline corporations, were in the business of leasing private railroad cars to shippers. The state's ad valorem taxing scheme taxed private railcar owners to the extent their cars were used in that state and taxed railroad cars of resident railroads on the basis of a formula that compared the amount of track in the state to the total track owned by the railroad. Nonresident railroads were not taxed in the state because their railroad cars retained tax situs in the states in which their parent railroad owned track under Fla. Stat. ch. § 193.985(4)(b)(1979). Respondents challenged the tax assessments of their rolling stock on the grounds that the statutory scheme discriminated against private carline owners because rail cars owned by nonresident railroads were not taxed in Florida. The court found the tax was not discriminatory because the taxing scheme allowed fair taxation of all railroad cars by sovereign states and avoided double taxation. The decision of the lower court was reversed and remanded to reinstate the tax assessment under § 193.085(4)(b).


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court was reversed and remanded because the court found that the ad valorem tax was not discriminatory because the taxing scheme allowed fair taxation of all railroad cars by sovereign states and avoids double taxation.

 

57 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Florida Freedom Newspapers, Inc. v. McCrary


No. 69,660


Supreme Court of Florida


520 So. 2d 32; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 172; 14 Media L. Rep. 2374; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 92



February 11, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions, First District - Case No. BM-47.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Asking for a determination of whether the lower court correctly construed U.S. Const. amends. I and VI, petitioner newspaper company applied for review of a decision of the District Court of Appeal (Florida), which granted in part motions to prevent public disclosure of certain pretrial discovery information and to prohibit public comment on the evidence and charges.


OVERVIEW: A newspaper reported that prisoners were being mistreated, and jailers were charged. Respondents filed motions to control prejudicial pretrial publicity by preventing public disclosure of pretrial discovery information and by prohibiting public comment on the evidence and charges. The trial court entered an order granting, in part, the measures requested. The trial court prohibited the release of the existing discovery materials and future discovery materials pending in-camera inspection, and petitioner newspaper company appealed. On appeal, the court approved the lower court's decision finding that there was no U.S. Const. amend. I right of access to pretrial discovery material. The court held that there was a statutory right of access to such material when it became a public record, but that statutory right had be balanced against the constitutional rights of a fair trial and due process. The court also held that there was no constitutional impediment to a court prohibiting prosecutors, defense counsel, witnesses, and other interested parties involved in the case before the court from making prejudicial pretrial comments which were intended for publication.


OUTCOME: The lower court's decision which granted in part the motion to prevent public disclosure of pretrial discovery information and to prohibit public comment on the evidence and charges was affirmed, because there was no First Amendment right of access to pretrial discovery material, and no constitutional impediment to a court prohibiting parties from making prejudicial pretrial comments that were intended for publication.

DuBoise v. State


No. 67,082


Supreme Court of Florida


520 So. 2d 260; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 146; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 79



February 4, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] An Appeal and Cross-Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Harry Lee Coe III, Judge - Case Nos. 82-11925, 82-11926, 82-11670 & 83-12669, Division "A".

Opinion of February 19, 1987, withdrawn; Motion for rehearing denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: From the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County (Florida), defendant appealed his conviction for first-degree murder, violation of probation, and his death sentence, asserting many errors during both the guilt and penalty phases. The state also cross-appealed an order arresting judgment on a jury verdict of guilt for attempted sexual battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for first-degree murder, violation of probation, and his death sentence, asserting many errors in both the guilt and penalty phases. The state cross-appealed an order arresting judgment on a jury verdict of guilt for attempted sexual battery. The court affirmed the convictions, concluding that the evidence clearly and convincingly supported the trial court's evidentiary rulings regarding the admission of a bite mark identification and statements from defendant's cellmate about defendant's guilt. The court, however, reversed the order granting defendant's motion for arrest of judgment on a jury verdict of guilt for sexual battery, concluding that the reference of a statute that defined the elements of the charged offense in the state's indictment sufficiently placed defendant on notice of the charged crime. Finally, the court vacated defendant's death sentence and adopted the jury's recommendation of life imprisonment, holding that it was error to override this recommendation, as the facts of the case were not so clear and convincing as to warrant death and reasonable persons could have differed regarding the propriety of a death sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions for first-degree murder and probation violation. However, the court reversed the order granting defendant's motion for arrest of judgment on the charge of sexual battery, concluding that the indictment was not defective as to this count. The court also reversed the death sentence and imposed life imprisonment because the facts were not so clear and convincing as to warrant a sentence of death.

 

60 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Day v. High Point Condominium Resorts


No. 69,519


Supreme Court of Florida


521 So. 2d 1064; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 109; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 55



January 28, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied and Revised March 31, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal and Cross-Appeal from the Fifth District Court of Appeal, No. 85-1403, Statutory/Constitutional Invalidity.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tax appraiser and appellee tax payers brought an appeal and cross-appeal regarding a decision of the Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida), which held that Fla. Stat. ch. 192.307 (1985) violated due process and equal protection by the manner in which it set forth the method for ad valorem taxation of fee time-share units.


OVERVIEW: Appellant tax appraiser and appellee tax payers brought an appeal and cross-appeal regarding a decision which held that Fla. Stat. ch. 192.307 (1985) was an unconstitutional deprivation of due process and equal protection. The statute set forth the method for ad valorem taxation of fee time-share units. Appellees claimed that the statute was unconstitutional because it placed time-share owners at a substantial disadvantage relative to other property owners in avoiding penalties for nonpayment of taxes and denied them a proper opportunity to receive notice and contest their taxes. The court reversed, holding that the statute was constitutional. First, time-share owners were treated the same as other multiple owners of a single parcel of real property. Also, there was a rational legislative basis to support the provisions for collection of ad valorem taxes contained in the statute, and the method of tax collection, the tax bill being mailed to one address, was not arbitrary and did not discriminate against the owners. Finally, the method of collecting taxes from owners was neither substantially different nor less protective than the method utilized for other owners of real property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the district court of appeal to the extent that it held the tax statute unconstitutional, because the statute did not violate the due process or equal protection clauses of the constitution.

State v. Pettis


No. 69,097


Supreme Court of Florida


520 So. 2d 250; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 148; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 44



January 21, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 16, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions, Fourth District - Case No. 85-992.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state petitioned for review of a decision from the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida), denying its petition for writ of certiorari to review an interlocutory evidentiary ruling by the trial court in a criminal case.


OVERVIEW: In a criminal case involving drugs, the state appealed an order that denied its request for writ of certiorari to review an adverse evidentiary ruling by the trial court. The court affirmed the denial of the writ of certiorari, finding that the state failed to meet its heavy burden of showing that the adverse ruling was a clear departure from the essential requirements of law. The court determined that although Fla. R. App. P. 9.030(b)(2) provided authority for certiorari jurisdiction to review non-final orders of lower tribunals, the writ was still an extraordinary one reserved only for situations where the order departed from the essential requirements of law and the state would have no other avenue of review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the petition for writ of certiorari, finding the challenged ruling was not a departure from the essential requirements of law. The court determined that although the evidentiary ruling by the trial court was in error, it was not such clear error as to merit the use of an extraordinary writ.

Bernie v. State


No. 67,535


Supreme Court of Florida


524 So. 2d 988; 1988 Fla. LEXIS 20; 13 Fla. L. Weekly 17

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a decision of the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) that applied the exclusionary rule's good faith exception and upheld the search and seizure of cocaine from a residence.


OVERVIEW: An envelope addressed to petitioner wife broke open during transit, revealing a suspicious substance. The substance was tested and identified as cocaine. Police obtained a search warrant for petitioners', husband and wife, residence relative to the prospective controlled delivery of the cocaine. A few minutes after the controlled delivery, police executed the warrant, arrested petitioners, and charged them with possession of cocaine. The court concluded that there was probable cause to obtain a warrant to seize a package already in law enforcement's constructive possession and that law enforcement knew contained contraband.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the lower court's decision and held that the state constitution brought the state's search and seizure laws into conformity with all decisions of the United States Supreme Court. The court also found that the anticipatory search warrant issued under the circumstances of the case was valid and did not violate the provisions of the federal or state constitutions.

 

63 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Brackenridge v. Ametek, Inc.


No. 70,099


Supreme Court of Florida


517 So. 2d 667; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2540; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 589



December 3, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 28, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance, Third District - Case No. 85-2775.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Subsequent to finding petitioner's personal injury suit was barred by the statute of repose, the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida), certified questions to determine the statute's applicability.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was injured by a laundry extractor more than 12 years after its delivery to the original purchaser. At the time petitioner's cause of action accrued, controlling case law allowed retrospective application of a statutory amendment abolishing the state's statute of repose. However, that case law was subsequently overruled. In his suit against respondents, petitioner contended that case law allowing the retrospective abolition of the statute of repose controlled. However, the court noted that a decision of a court of last resort, which overruled a prior decision, generally operated retrospectively. The court then held that, because petitioner had not acted in reliance on the earlier decision that was overruled, the most recent case law applied to petitioner's suit. Thus, under the current case law, the court concluded that the statute of repose operated to bar petitioner's claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing petitioner's claim was affirmed because the statute of repose operated to bar the suit.

 

64 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Clausell v. Hobart Corp.


No. 70,566


Supreme Court of Florida


515 So. 2d 1275; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2544; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 591



December 3, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal, Certified Great Public Importance, Third District, Case No. 86-924.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff challenged a judgment of the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida) that affirmed the dismissal of his suit by the trial court, arguing that the retrospective application of a judicial decision deprived him of a vested interest, the right to bring a cause of action, and thereby deprived him of his constitutional due process rights.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff brought suit relying upon a judicial decision declaring Fla. Stat. ch. 95.031 to be unconstitutional. During the suit's pendency, the state supreme court issued the Pullam decision, which reversed the prior decision and declared the statute constitutional. After plaintiff's claim was dismissed, plaintiff appealed, and a certified question was presented to the state supreme court regarding whether application of the Pullam decision to bar a cause of action that accrued prior to that decision deprived the plaintiff of his due process rights under the United States Constitution. In affirming the decision of the lower court and answering the certified question in the negative, the court concluded that plaintiff had no vested property interest, including a right to bring a cause of action, in any rule of the common law. Fla. Stat. ch. 95.031 provided a defense to a cause of action rather than creating one. At most, plaintiff had a mere expectation that he had a cause of action to pursue in light of the prior decision; the subsequent decision holding the statute to be constitutional could not and did not deprive him of any vested right.


OUTCOME: The district court judgment was affirmed, as plaintiff had no vested property interest in any rule of the common law. At most, plaintiff had a mere expectation of a right to bring suit; the retrospective application of a subsequent judicial decision declaring that no such right existed did not deprive him of any vested right in violation of his due process rights.

 

65 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Palm Harbor Special Fire Control Dist. v. Kelly


No. 70,119


Supreme Court of Florida


516 So. 2d 249; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2560; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 592



December 3, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity, Second District - Case No. 86-1150.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of a judgment from the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida), which held unconstitutional Fla. Stat. ch. 447.04(1)(a) (1985), a statute that prevented the licensing of appellee noncitizen as a business agent on the ground that he was not a citizen of the United States.


OVERVIEW: Appellee noncitizen applied for a license to act as a business agent for firefighters' union, which represented the employees of appellant employer. Appellant opposed the application on grounds of appellee's lack of citizenship. The Florida Department of Labor and Employment Security (the department) granted appellee a license, finding that Fla. Stat. ch. 455.10 implicitly repealed Fla. Stat. ch. 447.04(1)(a) and the alienage restriction it contained. The court of appeal disagreed with the department's rationale, but it affirmed the department's action on a different ground. The court of appeal, held that ch. 447.04(1)(a) violated the equal protection clause, and the supreme court affirmed the judgment. Ch. 447.04(1)(a) involved alienage, one of the traditional suspect classifications, and was, therefore, subject to strict scrutiny. Because ch. 447.04(1)(a) did not advance a compelling state interest by the least restrictive means available, the statute was unconstitutional. The court rejected appellant's argument that an exception to strict scrutiny existed under the "political function" test, finding that a business agent's contact with public policy was indirect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that held unconstitutional a statute that prevented the licensing of appellee noncitizen as a business agent for firefighters' union on the basis that he was not a citizen of the United States. The statute was unconstitutional because it did not advance a compelling state interest by the least restrictive means available.

 

66 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Tal-Mason v. State


No. 69,508


Supreme Court of Florida


515 So. 2d 738; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2469; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 568



November 12, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity, Fourth District, D.C. No. 85-1754.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, prison inmate, sought review of decision from the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District (Florida), which expressly declared valid Fla. Stat. ch. 921.161(1) (1985). Petitioner was arrested and spent five years in custody at state mental hospitals. Subsequently, he was convicted of second degree murder and given a life sentence. Petitioner argued the time spent in state mental institutions should be credited against his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, prison inmate, appealed decision which expressly declared valid Fla. Stat. ch. 921.161(1) (1985). Petitioner was arrested, indicted, and spent five years in custody at state mental hospitals. Subsequently, he was convicted of second degree murder and given a life sentence. Petitioner contended that the time spent in state mental institutions should be credited against his sentence. The trial court held the statute, which permitted credit for time spent in county jail, unconstitutional. The intermediate court reversed. In quashing the reversal, the court concluded that coercive commitment to a state institution was indistinguishable from pretrial detention in a "jail," as understood in common and legal usage. The court declined to read Fla. Stat. ch. 921.161(1) as a statement that jail-time credit could only be granted for time spent in an institution formally designated as a "county jail." That would infringe on interests protected by Florida and federal constitutions, resulting in violation of equal protection and due process rights. The court's clear obligation was to interpret statutes in a manner consistent with constitutional rights wherever possible.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the order of the district court and remanded, in an appeal from a decision which declared the Florida statute valid. The court held that jail-time credit must be awarded for petitioner's preconviction coercive detention in state mental hospitals.

 

67 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Bonito Boats, Inc. v. Thunder Craft Boats, Inc.


No. 68,829


Supreme Court of Florida


515 So. 2d 220; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2542; 5 U.S.P.Q.2D (BNA) 1124; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 570



November 12, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity, Fifth District - Case No. 85-458.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from a judgment of the Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirming the trial court's dismissal of a complaint under Fla. Stat. ch. 559.94 (1985) and finding the statute unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: One boat manufacturer sued another for unauthorized duplication of a boat design in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 559.94 (1985). The trial court dismissed the complaint, ruling that Fla. Stat. ch. 559.94 (1985) was pre-empted by federal patent law and was therefore unconstitutional. The appellate court upheld the ruling. The supreme court affirmed, holding that a state may not forbid the copying of an idea in the public domain that does not meet the requirements for federal patent protection.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed, holding that a state may not forbid the copying of an idea in the public domain that does not meet the requirements for federal patent protection.

 

68 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Bertolotti v. Dugger


No. 71,286


Supreme Court of Florida


514 So. 2d 1095; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2450; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 548



October 30, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner death sentence inmate sought a writ of habeas corpus based on petitioner's claims of ineffective assistance of counsel. Petitioner sought a stay of his execution.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. He sought a writ of habeas corpus claiming ineffective assistance of counsel and sought a stay of execution. Petitioner's ineffective assistance claims were based on counsel's argument to the court that her client was guilty of sexual battery despite the fact that the trial court found, in petitioner's sentencing order, that sexual battery had not been proven beyond a reasonable doubt and counsel's failure to argue on appeal that the general verdict was void under Stromberg. The court denied the petition and the requested stay explaining that counsel's argument that petitioner was guilty of sexual battery was her attempt to point out petitioner's sexual problems as a mitigating factor justifying a life sentence. Under the circumstances, counsel's performance as to this issue was not deficient. Further, the court agreed with the state that petitioner's second challenge was not properly preserved for appellate consideration. Appellate counsel's failure to raise an issue not preserved for appellate review and which did not present a fundamental error did not amount to a serious deficiency in performance.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's request for a writ of habeas corpus based on ineffective assistance of counsel claims. The court explained that counsel's argument, that petitioner was guilty of sexual battery, did not indicate deficiency of counsel where the argument was used as a mitigating factor justifying a life sentence. Further, the failure to raise an issue not preserved for appellate review was not a serious deficiency in performance.

 

69 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. Dugger


Nos. 71,346, 71,362


Supreme Court of Florida


515 So. 2d 185; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2451; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 542



October 28, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus and An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Bradford County, Osee R. Fagan, Judge - Case No. 87-01CFE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, under sentence of death, sought a writ of habeas corpus, requesting that he be resentenced because the jury's consideration of mitigating circumstances had been limited. Petitioner also appealed the order from the Circuit Court in and for Bradford County (Florida) dismissing petitioner's motion for a determination of his competency to be executed and requesting a stay of execution.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner prisoner was sentenced to death. The trial court dismissed his motion for a determination of his competency to be executed and requesting a stay of execution. Petitioner appealed the trial court's order and also sought a writ of habeas corpus on the grounds that the jury's consideration of mitigating circumstances had been limited by the trial court. The court denied petitioner's request for a writ of habeas corpus because the trial court had not limited the jury to considering only the statutory mitigating factors. With respect to petitioner's motion regarding his competency to be executed, the court found that the combined procedure set out in Fla. Stat. ch. 922.07 and Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.811 did not give undue deference to the executive branch in determining petitioner's competency. The trial court erred in finding that petitioner waived his claim of incompetency to be executed because only petitioner's counsel, not petitioner himself, waived the claim. The court directed that petitioner not be executed unless the procedures regarding his competency to be executed were concluded.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's request for a writ of habeas corpus because the trial court had not limited the jury to considering only the statutory mitigating factors. The court reversed the trial court's order because petitioner had not waived his claim of incompetency to be executed, and the court directed that petitioner should not be executed unless the procedures to determine his competency were concluded.

 

70 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Melendez v. Dreis & Krump Mfg. Co.


No. 70,225


Supreme Court of Florida


515 So. 2d 735; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2397; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P11,568; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 519



October 15, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 14, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance, Third District - Case No. 86-249.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed a decision from the Third District Court of Appeal, (Florida) which affirmed summary judgment for defendant in a product liability action, alleging that legislative abolishment of Fla. Stat. ch. 95.031(2) (1983), a statute of repose, should have been applied retroactively to allow plaintiff's suit and that case law finding ch. 95.031 to be constitutional should have been given prospective effect only.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff challenged the order of summary judgment for defendant pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 95.031(2)(1983), a statute of repose that limited a product liability action to twelve years after the product was sold. Plaintiff was injured more than seven years after the statute had passed. The legislature subsequently amended ch. 95.031(2), repealing the statute of repose in product liability actions. Plaintiff argued that the repeal should have been applied retroactively. Before a statute of limitations could be applied retroactively, a clear manifestation of legislative intent that the statute be given retroactive effect had to exist. Because no such intent existed in the amendment, it could not be applied retroactively. While plaintiff's case was pending, the court receded from an earlier position and found ch. 95.031 constitutional as to causes of action accruing after the twelve-year statute of repose. Plaintiff argued that the decision should have been given prospective effect only. The court's decision was silent on the question of retroactivity, indicating intent to apply it retrospectively as well as prospectively. As such, summary judgment for defendant was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court of appeal's order granting summary judgment to defendant in plaintiff's product liability action, holding that legislative amendment abolishing a statute of repose was prospective only because no clear manifestation of retroactive effect existed and that since case law was silent on the question of retroactively, it was to apply retrospectively as well as prospectively.

 

71 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Booker v. State


No. 68,400


Supreme Court of Florida


514 So. 2d 1079; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2347; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 491



September 24, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 1, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Second District - Case Nos. 85-409 & 85-410.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a decision of the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirming a departure from the sentencing guidelines in connection with his sentence; the court certified the question of what criteria should be used in determining whether a sentencing court abused its discretion as one of great public importance.


OVERVIEW: The lower appellate court affirmed a sentencing court's departure from the sentencing guidelines in imposing sentence upon petitioner. The lower appellate court also certified the question of what criteria an appellate court should use in determining whether a sentencing court abused its discretion in deviating from the sentencing guidelines to be one of great public importance. On appeal, the court affirmed the departure from the sentencing guidelines with respect to petitioner's sentence, finding that the sentencing court did not abuse its discretion because there were valid reasons for the departure. The court also ruled that although 1986 Fla. Laws ch. 86-273 did not violate the separation of powers provision of Fla. Const. art. II, § 3, the statute could not be applied retrospectively. Finally, the court declined to develop a specific checklist to be utilized in determining whether a sentencing court abused its discretion in departing from the sentencing guidelines.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed petitioner's sentence, finding no abuse of discretion by the sentencing court; the court declined to set forth precise criteria to be used in determining whether a sentencing court abused its discretion.

 

72 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


King v. State


No. 68,631


Supreme Court of Florida


514 So. 2d 354; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2364; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 502



September 24, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 20, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Philip A. Federico, Chief Judge - Case No. 77-2173 CFANO.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the death sentence imposed upon him by the Circuit Court, Pinellas County (Florida) on resentencing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death. On appeal, the court held appellant's counsel rendered ineffective assistance at the penalty phase of his trial. At the resentencing, the jury recommended the death penalty. The trial court imposed the death sentence, finding five aggravating factors and no mitigating factors. Appellant challenged that sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed. Appellee state did not engage in a pattern of systematically excluding African-Americans from the jury panel because it did not exclude the two African-American jurors solely based on their of race. Appellant could not relitigate the question of guilt and was not denied the chance to rebut the hearsay evidence admitted pursuant to Fla. Stat. Ann. § 921.141(1). The evidence presented properly was limited to evidence going to aggravating and mitigating factors. Statistical studies were insufficient to show unconstitutional discrimination in imposing the death penalty. The finding that appellant knowingly created a great risk of death to many persons by setting fire to the victim's house could not establish an aggravating factor because only the victim was in the house.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the death sentence imposed upon appellant on resentencing. Although the court erred in finding, as an aggravating factor, that appellant created a great risk of death to many people when he set fire to the victim's house, there were four valid aggravating factors and no mitigating factors to support the death penalty. Appellee state did not engage in racial discrimination when it chose the jury for the resentencing.

 

73 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Department of Revenue v. First Union Nat'l Bank


No. 70,186


Supreme Court of Florida


513 So. 2d 114; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2717; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 489



September 24, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Florida Department of Revenue, challenged a judgment of the First District Court of Appeals (Florida) that declared invalid Fla. Stat. ch. 220.63, which imposed a franchise tax on appellee banks and associations.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, the Florida Department of Revenue, sought review of a decision declaring invalid Fla. Stat. ch. 220.63. Appellee banks filed suit challenging the validity of the franchise tax imposed on banks and savings associations by the statute on the ground that it violated the Federal Public Debt Statute, 31 U.S.C.S. § 3124. The trial court upheld the statute and entered summary judgment against the banks. The court of appeals reversed and held the taxing statute invalid to the extent that it purported to include federal instrumentalities in its measure. The court noted that consistent with the legislative findings and declaration of intent contained in Fla. Laws ch. 72-278, Fla. Stat. ch. 220.63 was a classic nonproperty excise tax on the privilege of operating a bank or savings association within the state. As such, it was a franchise tax as contemplated by the exception numbered (a)(1) of 31 U.S.C.S. § 3124. Therefore the court found that the Florida franchise tax on banks and savings associations was nondiscriminatory and qualified as an exception to the exemption. The decision of the appeals court was reversed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals invalidating a portion of the state's franchise tax imposed on appellee banks and savings associations was reversed because the court found that the statute was a valid exercise of the state's authority to impose a tax on appellees for doing business in the state.

 

74 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hume


Nos. 66,691, 66,704


Supreme Court of Florida


512 So. 2d 185; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2305; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 464



September 10, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Consolidated Cases - Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decision and Constitutional Construction, First District Case No. AW-279.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the First District Court of Appeal (Florida), which reversed a trial court's decision to suppress evidence of his conversation that was transmitted by an electronic eavesdropping device. The state appealed the portion of the judgment that affirmed the trial court's suppression of seized contraband on the ground that the arresting officers failed to comply with knock and announce statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 901.19(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested as the result of information transmitted by an electronic eavesdropping device worn by a police undercover agent in defendant's home. After the information was transmitted to other officers who possessed an arrest warrant they entered defendant's home and arrested him. Defendant was charged with controlled substances offenses. Defendant moved to suppress the evidence of the transmitted conversation. The trial court granted the motion, but the court of appeal reversed, concluding that the transmission did not violate U.S. Const. amend. IV and, thus, did not violate the conformity amendment to Fla. Const. art. I, § 12. The supreme court approved the court of appeal decision related to the transmission, but it quashed the portion of the decision that affirmed the trial court's suppression of seized contraband for failure to comply with the knock and announce statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 901.19(1). The supreme court determined that the undercover officer was lawfully inside defendant's apartment. Therefore, the enlistment of officers waiting outside did not constitute an intrusion offensive to ch. 901.19(1) or to defendant's claimed expectation of privacy.


OUTCOME: The court approved the portion of the judgment that reversed the trial court's suppression order where the electronic transmission of defendant's conversation did not violate the Fourth Amendment. The court quashed the portion of the judgment that affirmed the trial court's suppression of seized contraband where the arresting officers were not required to knock and announce because the undercover officer was lawfully inside defendant's home.

 

75 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Bystrom v. Diaz


Nos. 68,995, 69,502 (Consolidated)


Supreme Court of Florida


514 So. 2d 1072; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2272; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 462



September 10, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 25, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Consolidated Cases. An Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions, Third District Case No. 85-1863. An Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity, Second District Case No. 85-2748.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer and respondent appealed orders from the Second and Third District Court of Appeal (Florida), in which one court dismissed petitioner's taxpayer suit for failing to pay taxes while his suit was pending as provided in Fla. Stat. ch. 194.171(5) and (6) and the other court allowed respondent's taxpayer suit to go forward.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner taxpayer and respondent taxpayer filed suit challenging a tax assessment against their property. Petitioner's taxpayer suit was dismissed because petitioner taxpayer failed to pay his taxes before they became delinquent as provided in Fla. Stat. ch. 194.171(5) and (6). As to respondent taxpayer, the lower court held the requirement in section 194.171(5) and (6) was not a jurisdictional bar. On appeal, the supreme court held that the failure to pay taxes before they became delinquent while a suit was pending barred recovery under section 194.171(5) and (6). According to the supreme court, although section 194.171(5) and (6) appear to be somewhat harsh their meaning was clear. The supreme court held that section 194.171(5) plainly stated that a taxpayer could not maintain a suit contesting a tax assessment, and that such an action shall be dismissed, unless all taxes on the property assessed in years after the action was brought, which the taxpayer in good faith admitted to be owing, were paid before they become delinquent. The supreme court held that these requirements were jurisdictional and did not allow a court to retain jurisdiction once taxes become delinquent.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment dismissing petitioner's taxpayer suit and reversed the judgment allowing respondent's taxpayer suit to go forward because as a prerequisite to maintaining a tax assessment suit all taxes were to be paid before they became delinquent while the suit was pending.

Thompson v. Dugger


Nos. 70,739, 70,781


Supreme Court of Florida


515 So. 2d 173; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2296; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 469



September 9, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 7, 1987.
Writ of certiorari denied Dugger v. Thompson, 485 U.S. 960, 108 S. Ct. 1224, 99 L. Ed. 2d 424, 1988 U.S. LEXIS 1266 (1988)
Appeal after remand at Thompson v. State, 1992 Fla. LEXIS 997 (Fla., June 4, 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus, and An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Edward D. Cowart, Judge, Case No. 76-3350B.
Thompson v. Wainwright, 787 F.2d 1447, 1986 U.S. App. LEXIS 23851 (11th Cir. Fla., 1986)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida) denying his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion to vacate the judgment convicting him of first-degree murder, kidnapping, and involuntary sexual battery and sentencing him to death, and defendant petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus and a stay of execution from his second death warrant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to first-degree murder, kidnapping, and involuntary sexual battery. Defendant withdrew his plea on voluntariness grounds and entered a second plea of guilty to the offenses. An advisory jury recommended the death sentence, which the trial court imposed. The conviction and sentence were affirmed. Defendant filed a Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion, and the court affirmed the denial of relief. Defendant then petitioned for federal habeas corpus relief, relief was denied, and the federal court of appeals affirmed. Defendant filed a Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion to vacate judgment and sentence of death. The trial court denied the motion. Defendant appealed and filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus and a stay of execution from his second death warrant. The court reversed the denial of defendant's motion, continued the stay of execution, and remanded for a new sentencing hearing, holding that the trial court should have allowed defendant to present appropriate nonstatutory mitigating evidence at sentencing, but defendant's other claims were procedurally barred. In light of the opinion, the habeas corpus petition was moot.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of defendant's motion to vacate judgment and sentence of death, continued the stay of execution, and remanded for a new sentencing hearing, holding that the trial court should have allowed defendant to present appropriate nonstatutory mitigating evidence at sentencing, but defendant's other claims were procedurally barred. In light of the disposition, the petition for a writ of habeas corpus was moot.

 

77 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Downs v. Dugger


No. 71,100


Supreme Court of Florida


514 So. 2d 1069; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2407; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 473



September 9, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 23, 1987.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought an extraordinary relief, writ of habeas corpus, and stay of execution following petitioner's conviction of murder and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of murder and sentenced to death. He sought an extraordinary relief, writ of habeas corpus and stay of execution. In granting the writ, the court held that the "mere presentation" standard could no longer be considered controlling law. Under Hitchcock, the mere opportunity to present nonstatutory mitigating evidence did not meet constitutional requirements if the judge believed, or the jury was led to believe, that some of that evidence could not be weighed during the formulation of an advisory opinion or during sentencing. The factual situation presented by Hitchcock was also present in petitioner's case in substantially identical form, and the language was similar to the improper instruction given the jury in Hitchcock. Petitioner's jury was troubled by potential mitigating evidence, as reflected in a question asked of the judge regarding petitioner's firearms charge. The question showed that they considered that petitioner's accomplice could have been of equal or greater guilt. This, along with other mitigating evidence that was presented, precluded any finding of harmless error beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner's writ, stayed the execution, and vacated the death sentence in light of the requirements established by the United States Supreme Court in Hitchcock. The court ruled that the "mere presentation" standard could no longer be considered controlling law.

 

78 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Riley v. Wainwright


No. 69,563


Supreme Court of Florida


517 So. 2d 656; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2269; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 457



September 3, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 25, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a prisoner under sentence of death and execution warrant, asked the court to grant a writ of habeas corpus on the ground that the advisory jury at sentencing was improperly restricted in the consideration of mitigating factors.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus and asserted that the advisory jury at his sentencing hearing was improperly restricted in the consideration of non-statutory mitigating factors. Petitioner was under sentence of death and execution warrant and had exhausted all of his appeals. The court noted that in several cases decided since petitioner's conviction, the court had held that the sentencer could not refuse to consider or be precluded from considering any relevant mitigating evidence and that an appellant was entitled to a new sentencing hearing if the record showed the sentencing judge had limited the mitigating circumstances to be considered. Further, the court held that if the jury's sentencing recommendation resulted from an unconstitutional procedure, the entire sentencing process was tainted. In petitioner's case, because the sentencing judge found two aggravating factors and only one statutory mitigating factor and refused to consider non-statutory mitigating circumstances, the court could not say the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. The court therefore vacated petitioner's sentence and remanded for a new sentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: The court held that in light of the fact that the sentencing judge refused to consider non-statutory mitigating circumstances, petitioner was entitled to a new sentencing hearing. The court therefore vacated petitioner's sentence and directed that a new sentencing hearing before a jury be held.

 

79 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Jennings v. State


No. 68,835


Supreme Court of Florida


512 So. 2d 169; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2465; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 434



August 27, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 22, 1987; Original Opinion of August 27, 1987 Revised.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County, Charles M. Harris, Judge - Case No. 79-773-CF-A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County (Florida) that convicted him of first-degree murder, first-degree felony murder, kidnapping with intent to commit sexual battery, sexual battery, and burglary and imposed the death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder, first-degree felony murder, kidnapping with intent to commit sexual battery, sexual battery, and burglary and sentenced to death. Appellant sought review and alleged sixteen errors in the guilt and penalty phases of the trial. The court rejected almost all of appellant's allegations of error after concluding that each one was either without merit or constituted only harmless error. The one allegation that the court held had merit was that the trial judge erred in failing to certify appellant as a mentally disordered sex offender. The court found that under Fla. Stat. ch. 917.13(1), appellant was a mentally disordered sex offender and the trial court erred by refusing to so classify him. However, the court held the statute did not encompass first-degree murder because murder was not a sex offense per se. The court therefore affirmed appellant's convictions, the sentence of death for murder, and the sentence of life imprisonment for burglary but reversed appellant's sentences for kidnapping and sexual battery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions, the sentence of death for murder, and the sentence of life imprisonment for burglary. The court reversed appellant's sentences for kidnapping and sexual battery after holding the trial court erred in failing to classify appellant as a mentally disordered sex offender.

 

80 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


U.S. Sprint Communications Co. v. Marks


Nos. 69,169, 69,159 (Consolidated)


Supreme Court of Florida


509 So. 2d 1107; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2063; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 397



July 16, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Consolidated Notices of Appeal from the Public Service Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated action, appellant communications companies challenged Public Service Commission (Florida) rulings that denied appellants' requests to abolish toll monopoly areas.


OVERVIEW: Restricted operating areas for local telephone companies were established to provide competitive interstate long distance telephone services. Case law affirmed the need for such service and, as a result, the state public service commission (commission) created toll monopoly areas (TMAs). Appellant communications companies challenged the creation of these TMAs as a violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 364.335(4) because it was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative powers. The court affirmed the decision of the commission, stating that both Fla. Stat. ch. 364.335(4) and Fla. Stat. ch. 364.337 contained statutory authority for the commission to maintain the temporary TMAs and that the TMAs represented the commission's commitment to competition in long distance service.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the administrative decision to create and maintain temporary monopolies for local telephone companies because the authority to maintain them was found in two different statutes and, although technological and other cost savings changes had not occurred as rapidly as predicted, that did not transform the temporary monopolies into a permanent fact of life.
