Livingston v. State


No. 69,807


Supreme Court of Florida


510 So. 2d 295; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2099; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 411



July 16, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance, Fifth District, Case No. 86-557.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted an application for review of a decision of the District Court of Appeal, Fifth District (Florida), and reviewed a certified question.


OVERVIEW: The court reviewed a district court of appeal decision and accepted jurisdiction to answer a question certified to be of great public importance concerning the retroactive application of Fla. Stat. ch. 27.3455(1) (1985), which required that all court costs and court fees be paid in full prior to granting a prisoner gain time: "Does the application of § 27.3455, Florida Statutes (1985), to crimes committed prior to the effective date of the statute violate the ex post facto provisions of the constitutions of the United States and of the state of Florida, or does the statute merely effect a procedural change as is permitted under State v. Jackson, 478 So. 2d 1054 (Fla. 1985)?" The court answered that the application of the statute was unconstitutional, and approved the decision of the district court of appeal. The court said that it had previously answered a nearly identical question in the affirmative.


OUTCOME: The court approved the decision of the district court of appeal and answered the first portion of the certified question in the affirmative, because the retroactive application of the statute that required all court costs and court fees to be paid in full prior to granting a prisoner gain time was unconstituional.

 

82 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


In re Advisory Opinion to Governor


No. 70,533


Supreme Court of Florida


509 So. 2d 292; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2143; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 375



July 14, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Proceeding - Advisory Opinion to the Governor (Services Tax).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an original proceeding, the governor requested the opinion of the justices of the court whether the state legislature by enacting 1987 Fla. Laws ch. 87-6 validly created revenue sources from the tax imposed on the sale or use of services consumed or enjoyed in the state.


OVERVIEW: The governor requested the advice of the court on a question affecting his fiscal duties: "Did the legislature by enacting Chapter 87-6, Laws of Florida, validly create revenue sources from the tax imposed on the sale or use of services consumed or enjoyed in this state as enumerated therein or did it fail in that effort, which will require me to propose a supplemental budget that either reduces state expenditures or attempts to identify and propose alternative sources of revenue so that the budget of this state will be in balance as dictated by Article VII, Section 1(d), Florida Constitution?" Rejecting numerous constitutional challenges, the court's opinion was that the statute was facially constitutional, except for a provision that retroactively turned otherwise profitable contracts into losing propositions. Among other things, the general tax on the sale or use of services consumed or enjoyed in the state, including legal services, did not impermissibly burden the right to legal counsel and access to the courts in violation of due process, and did not violate the freedom of speech, press, or association of advertisers or of media in which advertising was carried.


OUTCOME: Except for a provision that retroactively turned otherwise profitable contracts into losing propositions, the court's opinion was that the statute was facially constitutional, because, among other things, the statute's general tax on the sale or use of services consumed or enjoyed in the state, including legal services, did not impermissibly burden the right to legal counsel and access to the courts in violation of due process.

 

83 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Metropolitan Dade County Fair Housing & Employment Appeals Bd. v. Sunrise Village Mobile Home Park, Inc.


No. 68,626


Supreme Court of Florida


511 So. 2d 962; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2047; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 346



July 9, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 8, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Third District - Case No. 85-1057.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the circuit court reversed petitioner board's decision because the local antidiscrimination ordinance resulted in an unconstitutional restraint on respondent company's right to utilize its property as a retirement community, the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida) denied petitioner's writ of certiorari because it found that the circuit court had correctly applied the law. Petitioner sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Characterizing its mobile home park as a retirement community, respondent company refused to allow a 29-year-old employed individual to move into the park. The individual filed a complaint with petitioner board, charging respondent with age discrimination in housing in violation of a local antidiscrimination ordinance. Petitioner adopted its executive director's recommendation to order respondent to allow complainant to move into the park and to pay damages for complainant's humiliation, embarrassment, and mental distress. The circuit court reversed because the ordinance did not allow for reasonable age restrictions. The appellate court denied petitioner's writ of certiorari, but certified an issue for review by the state supreme court. Although the ordinance's prohibition of reasonable age discrimination in housing was not an unconstitutional exercise of police power because its interference with otherwise protected rights bore a reasonable relationship to the elimination of invidious discrimination, the court held that the ordinance's authorization of common-law damages was an unconstitutional violation of separation of powers principles and the right to a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court held that a local antidiscrimination ordinance was a constitutionally proper exercise of police power to eliminate invidious age discrimination in housing. Petitioner board could not, however, award common-law damages to complainant, because in this respect the ordinance unconstitutionally violated the separation of powers and respondent company's right to a jury trial.

 

84 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


McRae v. J.D./M.D., Inc.


No. 68,370


Supreme Court of Florida


511 So. 2d 540; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2051; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 332



July 9, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 11, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance, Fourth District - Case No. 85-642.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirmed the trial court's denial of petitioner attorney's motion to quash service of process for a lack of personal jurisdiction under Florida's long-arm statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 48.193, finding that the forum selection clause in the parties' contract gave Florida jurisdiction over petitioner. Petitioner sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner attorney and his client were Mississippi residents who contracted with respondent Delaware company to provide an expert witness for use in a medical malpractice suit. All the parties' negotiations took place between Mississippi and respondent's New Jersey office. Nevertheless, the parties' contract contained a forum selection clause designating Florida as the forum for any dispute. Respondent filed a breach of contract action against petitioner and his client. Petitioner moved to quash service for a lack of personal jurisdiction, alleging that he did not do any of the acts specified in Florida's long-arm statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 48.193. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's denial of the motion, reasoning that the contract entered into between the parties provided the basis for personal jurisdiction. Petitioner sought further review. The court quashed and remanded the lower court's decision, holding that the parties' forum selection clause could not operate as the sole basis for Florida to exercise personal jurisdiction over the objecting nonresident petitioner. Thus, there was no independent basis for Florida to exercise jurisdiction over petitioner.


OUTCOME: The court quashed and remanded the lower court's affirmance of the trial court's denial of petitioner attorney's motion to quash service of process, holding that Florida could not exercise in personam jurisdiction over the objection of a nonresident petitioner who had done none of the acts specified in Florida's long arm statute, but who was a party to a contract designating Florida as the forum for any subsequent litigation between the parties.

 

85 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Riley v. State


No. 67,906


Supreme Court of Florida


511 So. 2d 282; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2055; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 343



July 9, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 11, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the district court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance, Second District, Case No. 84-2818.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a charge against petitioner for unlawful possession and manufacture of marijuana, under Fla. Stat. ch. 893.13 (1983), the District Court of Appeals, Second District (Florida), reversed the grant of petitioner's motion to suppress evidence obtained from an aerial surveillance and certified a question for review regarding what constituted a "search" for which a warrant was required under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Fla. Const. art. I, § 12.


OVERVIEW: A deputy flew a helicopter over petitioner's property at approximately 400 feet. Through openings in a greenhouse roof, marijuana was viewed. A search warrant was obtained and several marijuana plants were found. Petitioner was charged with unlawful possession and manufacture of marijuana, under Fla. Stat. ch. 893.13. The district court reversed an order to suppress evidence and certified a question for review. The question involved whether helicopter surveillance of the greenhouse constituted a "search" for which a warrant was required under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Fla. Const. art. I, § 12. The court held that the area was curtilage, and that under the Katz test, petitioner had a reasonable expectation of privacy. The court stated that there was a difference between a flying fixed-wing aircraft and a hovering helicopter. Furthermore, the governmental intrusion did not advance legitimate interests. Because petitioner's reasonable expectation of privacy was invaded and the observations constituted a search under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Fla. Const. art. I, § 12, the district court's decision was quashed and the case was remanded for reinstatement of the suppression order.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the district court's decision that reversed an order to suppress evidence and remanded the case for reinstatement of the suppression order, because observations of petitioner's curtilage from a helicopter constituted a search that required a search warrant. Under the Katz test, petitioner had a reasonable expectation of privacy in the curtilage.

 

86 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Kight v. State


No. 65,749


Supreme Court of Florida


512 So. 2d 922; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2056; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 357



July 9, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 14, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, James L. Harrison, Sr., Judge - Case No. 83-2598-CF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court, in and for Duval County (Florida), that convicted appellant of first degree murder and sentenced appellant to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death. The court affirmed the conviction and the sentence, holding that appellant failed to demonstrate reversible error. The court held that although appellant's initial statement to police was obtained in violation of appellant's U.S. Const. amend. V rights, because it resulted from an unwarned custodial interrogation, two subsequent statements were properly admitted because a Miranda warning cured the procedural violation. Furthermore, the error was harmless because the properly admitted statements were cumulative. In addition, appellant's statements were voluntary, appellant had no U.S. Const. amend. VI right to counsel during the interrogation, and sufficient evidence supported the first degree murder conviction. Moreover, it was not error to exclude evidence of appellant's mental capacity, because in the absence of a plea of not guilty by reason of insanity, testimony of appellant's mental state was inadmissible during the trial's guilt phase. Finally, although jury deliberation instructions were improper, the subsequent voir dire adequately ensured appellant's right to an impartial sentencing jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence for first degree murder because the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction, statements made to police after the issuance of Miranda warnings were properly admitted, and appellant was ensured the right to an impartial jury.

 

87 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Wilcott v. State


No. 67,473


Supreme Court of Florida


509 So. 2d 261; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 1894; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 248



May 21, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions, First District - Case No. BC-223.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed an application for review of the decision of the District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida) affirming his conviction of unlawfully introducing or possessing contraband upon the grounds of a state correctional institution in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 944.47(1)(a) and (c) (1983) and finding that defendant was not entitled to a lesser-included offense instruction on possession of less than 20 grams of cannabis.


OVERVIEW: Defendant inmate, participated in an outside work program. Defendant apparently discovered a small bag of cannabis at his workplace. Upon his return to the correctional center, a correctional officer searched defendant and found the cannabis in his underwear. Defendant was charged with unlawfully introducing or possessing contraband upon the grounds of a state correctional institution in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 944.47(1)(a) and (c) (1983). During the charge conference, defendant's trial counsel requested a jury instruction on possession of less than 20 grams of cannabis, Fla. Stat. ch. 893.13(1)(f) (1983), as a lesser-included offense. The trial court denied the request, and the jury found defendant guilty. The court of appeal affirmed. Defendant filed an application for review. The court quashed the decision of the court of appeal and remanded for further proceedings, holding that possession of less than 20 grams of cannabis was a lesser-included offense because the information charged introduction or possession in the alternative. Because it was the next lower lesser-included offense, the failure to instruct on possession constituted reversible error.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the decision of the court of appeal and remanded for further proceedings, holding that possession of less than 20 grams of cannabis was a lesser-included offense because the information charged introduction or possession in the alternative. Because it was the next lower lesser-included offense, the failure to instruct on possession constituted reversible error.

 

88 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Nibert v. State


No. 67,072


Supreme Court of Florida


508 So. 2d 1; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 1835; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 225



May 7, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 10, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Harry Lee Coe III, Judge, No. 84-13431 A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death. Appellant asserted that the trial court erred in instructing the jury, and in finding premeditation in both the guilt and sentencing phases of the trial.


OVERVIEW: Finding no merit in appellant's guilt-phase assignments of error, the court affirmed the conviction; finding that the heightened level of premeditation required by Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141(5)(i) had not been proved beyond a reasonable doubt, the court vacated the death sentence and remanded for resentencing. The court held that no instruction regarding the inapplicability of the felony-murder rule was required where it was clear from all the circumstances that no predicate felony was involved. The court held that appellant failed to object to the trial court's failure to give written instructions to the jury, and held that this was not fundamental error. Because the testimony indicated that appellant ordered the victim to his knees before stabbing him 17 times, the court held that sufficient premeditation existed to support the conviction. On the other hand, the court held that the evidence did not rise to the heightened level of premeditation required to support the cold, calculated, and premeditated aggravator of ch. 921.141(5)(i). Where this left but one aggravating factor, the court held that the death penalty was not indicated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the first-degree murder conviction but vacated the death sentence and remanded for resentencing. The court found no merit in appellant's complaints regarding jury instructions, expert testimony, or the guilt-phase finding of premeditation. The court held, however, that the level of premeditation proved was insufficient to support the cold, calculated, and premeditated aggravating circumstance.

 

89 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Department of Corrections v. Florida Nurses Ass'n


No. 68,986


Supreme Court of Florida


508 So. 2d 317; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 1844; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 221



May 7, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 13, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Leon County, Charles E. Miner, Jr., Judge, Case No. 85-2380, Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. BN-256.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant agencies sought review of a judgment from the trial court, in and for Leon County (Florida), which found for appellee doctor's union and held that 1985 Fla. Laws ch. 318 was unconstitutional as applied to certain of appellee's members, because it deprived them of permanent status in the career service system.


OVERVIEW: Holding that even tenured employees had no vested or contractual rights in the continuation of legislatively created employment once that employment was legislatively abolished, the court reversed the judgment to the extent that it declared 1985 Fla. Laws ch. 318 unconstitutional. The court applied a rational basis test to determine the statute's constitutionality. The court found that the legislature's intent was to create a highly qualified and responsive staff, and its means was increasing pay and benefits but requiring that employees serve at will. The court held that the objective was legitimate, and that the means bore a rational and reasonable relationship to that objective. The court also held that because the legislature created the employment enjoyed by members of appellee doctor's union, the legislature could take that employment away without affecting the rights of tenured employees in the employment. The court noted that appellee's members were also given the opportunity to remain in the career service in any position for which they were qualified, albeit not as physicians since those positions no longer existed in the career service.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment for appellee doctor's union, and held that a statute that effectively stripped appellee's members of their tenured status was constitutional. The court held that while tenured government employees undoubtedly had rights in their employment, they had no right to that employment once the legislature had abolished the employment.

 

90 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Department of Ins.


Nos. 69,551, 69,703, 69,704


Supreme Court of Florida


507 So. 2d 1080; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2133; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 277



April 23, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 2, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Leon County, Charles E. Miner, Jr., Judge, Case Nos. 86-2262, 86-2272 & 86-2363, Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case Nos. BQ-90, BQ-91, BQ-75, BQ-76 & BQ-77; BQ-201; and BQ-317.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, attorneys and insurance companies, challenged the decision of a trial court, which held that substantially all of the Tort Reform and Insurance Act, 1986 Fla. Laws ch. 86-160, was constitutional. The First District Court of Appeal certified the question to the court. Appellees included the State, state department of insurance, a medical association, a railroad association, and a utility company.


OVERVIEW: The reviewing court affirmed, except for the portions approving a cap on noneconomic damages and imposing rate changes. The court held the Act did not violate the single subject rule under Fla. Const. art. III, § 6 because there was an opportunity for debate and hearing and the provisions were germane to the subject of the Act. However, the cap on noneconomic damages was impermissible under Fla. Const. art I, § 21 because no overpowering public necessity for abolishment and no alternative method of redress was shown. Further, the legislature did not have sufficient authority to impair insurance contracts by changing the agreed-to premiums. However, those portions were severable and the Act remained valid after the invalid provisions were stricken.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment except as to those portions approving the cap on noneconomic damages and impairing existing contracts, which were found unconstitutional.

 

91 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Broward County v. La Rosa


No. 68,649


Supreme Court of Florida


505 So. 2d 422; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 1742; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 171



April 9, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal, Constitutional Construction, Fourth District, Case No. 84-404.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner county appealed a decision from the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida), which found the Broward County Human Rights Ordinance, Broward County, Fla., Code § 16 1/2-67(b) (1978) unconstitutional because it empowered petitioner county's human rights board to award common law damages to victims of race discrimination.


OVERVIEW: Complainant, an African-American male, filed a complaint with petitioner county's human rights board contending that respondent landlord refused to lease him an apartment because of his race. Pursuant to the Broward County Human Rights Ordinance, Broward County, Fla., Code § 16 1/2-67(b), the board found that respondent engaged in a discriminatory practice and ordered him to pay complainant compensation for humiliation. Respondent initiated a declaratory judgment action contending that the county ordinance was unconstitutional because it violated the separation of powers clause of the Fla. Const. art. II, § 3. The appellate court affirmed the decision, concluding that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it empowered the board to award damages for noneconomic injuries. The supreme court approved the decision because the board's power was an unconstitutional delegation of judicial authority. The ordinance authorized the board to exercise powers that were fundamentally judicial in nature. The board was empowered with quasi-judicial functions, but its act of awarding damages after an adjudicatory proceeding was purely judicial.


OUTCOME: The supreme court approved the appellate court's decision, which found petitioner county's ordinance unconstitutional. The supreme court concluded that the ordinance was unconstitutional because the ordinance empowered petitioner county's human rights board with functions that were fundamentally judicial in nature. The board's power to award damages for humiliation after an adjudicatory proceeding was a purely judicial function.

Markham v. Evangelical Covenant Church


No. 68,396


Supreme Court of Florida


502 So. 2d 1239; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 1567; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 112



February 26, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fourth District - Case No. 85-794.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner county officials filed an application for review of the decision of the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District (Florida) finding unconstitutional the income test set forth in Fla. Stat. ch. 196.1975(4), by which petitioners denied respondent church a full exemption from property taxes on a home for the aged owned and operated by respondent, and the court of appeal certified the question as one of great public importance.


OVERVIEW: Respondent church filed a complaint challenging the decision of petitioner county property appraiser not to grant respondent a full exemption from property taxes on a home for the aged owned and operated by respondent. Petitioners utilized the income test set forth in Fla. Stat. ch. 196.1975(4) (1985) in denying the full exemption. The income test linked the extent of property tax exemption with the income of the home's residents. The court of appeal found that the income test was unconstitutional and certified as a question of great public importance whether the court's previous opinion finding the income test unconstitutional continued to have vitality and, if so, did the amended income test pass constitutional muster. Petitioners filed an application for review. The court affirmed and struck as unconstitutional paragraph (4) of Fla. Stat. ch. 196.1975, holding that the income test was too narrow in scope to conform to the tax limitation set forth in Fla. Const. art. VII, § 3, and the subsequent amendment was only superficial and did not change the constitutionally impermissible character of the income test.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals holding the income test unconstitutional and struck as unconstitutional the statutory paragraph containing the income test, holding that the income test was too narrow in scope to conform to the constitutional tax limitation on charitably operated property, and the amendment did not change the constitutionally impermissible character of the income test.

Duboise v. State


No. 67,082


Supreme Court of Florida


1987 Fla. LEXIS 2701



February 19, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Rehearing Denied and Opinion Withdrawn and Modified February 4, 1988


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal and Cross-Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Harry Lee Coe III, Judge - Case Nos. 82-11925, 82-11926, 82-11670 & 83-12669 Division "A"


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction of first-degree murder, three convictions of violation of probation, and sentence of death, imposed by the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County (Florida). The state cross-appealed the trial court's order arresting judgment on a jury verdict of guilt of attempted sexual battery.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder and three counts of probation violation. The trial court granted appellant's motion to arrest a judgment of conviction for sexual battery. Appellant sought review and the state cross-appealed. The court affirmed appellant's convictions, finding no reversible error in the trial court proceedings. The court, however, reversed the trial judge's order granting appellant's motion for arrest of judgment on the sexual battery charge. The court found that the appellant had not moved to quash the indictment before trial as was required by Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.610, and the indictment was not so defective that it would not support the judgment of conviction. The court ordered judgment to be entered pursuant to the verdict of guilty of attempted sexual battery. The court also found that there was sufficient evidence on which the jury could have relied in recommending a life sentence. Therefore, the court reversed the death sentence and remanded for imposition of a life sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions of first-degree murder, and three convictions of violation of probation. The court reversed the trial court's order arresting judgment on grounds appellant failed to raise the defective indictment claim prior to trial. The court also reversed the death sentence and remanded for imposition of a life sentence, finding the trial court should have followed the jury's recommendation.

 

94 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Routly v. Wainwright


No. 69,089


Supreme Court of Florida


502 So. 2d 901; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 1528; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 101



February 12, 1987 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner filed a petition for the issuance of a writ of habeas corpus regarding his conviction for first degree murder and sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner prisoner was convicted of first-degree murder. The trial court overrode the jury recommendation of life and imposed a death sentence. The conviction and sentence were affirmed on appeal. Thereafter, petitioner filed a petition for the issuance of a writ of habeas corpus. The court held that appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to obtain a reversal on the ground that respondent prosecution made four improper remarks regarding petitioner's right to take the stand. First, only one of those statements was objected to at trial and thus could be raised on appeal. Second, appellate counsel did present the argument as to that statement on appeal, but it was rejected. Thus, the court declined to address the issue again because it was already raised and ruled upon on appeal. The court then held that it did not intend to establish a requirement of a formal hearing or inquiry regarding a prospective appointee through its prior decision. Furthermore, there was no evidence that the appointing judge failed to conscientiously perform his assigned duties in appointing counsel. Finding the remaining contentions to be meritless, the court denied the petition.


OUTCOME: Petitioner prisoner's habeas corpus petition seeking relief from his murder conviction and sentence was denied because appellate counsel did raise the argument of prosecutorial misconduct as to the one statement objected to at trial, but it was rejected, there was no evidence that the appointing judge failed to perform his duties in appointing counsel, and the remaining contentions were meritless.

 

95 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Spence v. Hughes


No. 68,569


Supreme Court of Florida


500 So. 2d 538; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 1375; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 30



January 5, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance, Fifth District - Case No. 85-319.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed the decision from the Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida), affirming the trial court's ruling in petitioner's personal injury case that the tort exemption in Fla. Stat. ch. 627.737 (1983) applied to respondent nonresidents who voluntarily obtained PIP coverage which complied with Florida's no-fault law.


OVERVIEW: The court approved the district court's opinion and adopted it in its entirety. The district court had affirmed a judgment for respondent nonresidents in petitioner resident's tort action against them following an automobile accident in Florida. Although not required by Florida law to do so, respondent nonresident owner had obtained PIP coverage meeting the requirements of Florida's no-fault statute. Petitioner admitted to the trial court that she did not suffer threshold injuries but argued that she could maintain a tort action against respondents because the tort exemption in Fla. Stat. ch. 627.737 (1983) did not apply to nonresidents. The court agreed with the district court that the tort exemption applied not only to those individuals required by statute to provide PIP coverage but to every individual, resident or nonresident, who actually provided PIP coverage conforming to the no-fault law. This construction avoided an unconstitutional distinction between residents and nonresidents and was consistent with the purpose of Florida's no-fault statute.


OUTCOME: The court approved and adopted the district court's opinion holding that Florida's tort exemption applied to respondent nonresidents who voluntarily obtained PIP coverage which complied with Florida's no-fault law because this construction of the statute avoided an unconstitutional distinction between residents and nonresidents and furthered the best interests of Florida's residents.

Falzone v. State


No. 68,178


Supreme Court of Florida


500 So. 2d 1337; 1987 Fla. LEXIS 1387; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 31



January 5, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity. Second District - Case No. 85-64.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner political committee member challenged a Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) decision that expressly declared Florida's Campaign Finance Law to be constitutional and held that petitioner's failure to file a statement of organization was punishable under Fla. Stat. ch. 106.19 (1983).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner political committee member challenged an appeals court decision that held Florida's Campaign Finance Law was constitutional and that petitioner's failure to file a statement of organization, as required under Fla. Stat. ch. 106.19 (1983), was a punishable misdemeanor. The state supreme court affirmed the appeals court decision. Requiring political committees to file a statement of organization, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 106.03 (Supp. 1984), was supported by the compelling state interest of informing the electorate of those involved in raising and spending money for elections. Chapter 106.03 was not vague or overbroad in light of Fla. Stat. ch. 106.011(1983)'s definition of a political committee. Chapter 106.19(c) created a misdemeanor for deliberately failing to provide information called for in the statement of organization required by ch. 106.03, and petitioner knowingly failed to provide such information.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed an appeals court decision that held Florida's Campaign Finance Law (the law) was constitutional and that petitioner political committee member committed a misdemeanor by failing to file a statement of organization as required under the law. The law was not vague or overbroad, and petitioner violated the law by knowingly failing to file the requisite information.

Tompkins v. State


No. 67,974


Supreme Court of Florida


502 So. 2d 415; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 3020; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 44



December 30, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 9, 1987.
Writ of certiorari denied Tompkins v. Florida, 483 U.S. 1033, 107 S. Ct. 3277, 97 L. Ed. 2d 781, 1987 U.S. LEXIS 3042, 55 U.S.L.W. 3872 (1987)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Tompkins v. Dugger, 549 So. 2d 1370, 1989 Fla. LEXIS 868 (Fla., 1989)
Post-conviction proceeding at Tompkins v. State, 872 So. 2d 230, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1718 (Fla., 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at Tompkins v. State, 894 So. 2d 857, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 49 (Fla., 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Tompkins v. State, 980 So. 2d 451, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 848 (Fla., 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied, Writ denied by Tompkins v. State, 994 So. 2d 1072, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 2055 (Fla., 2008)

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Harry Lee Coe, III, Judge, No. 84-10538 A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from judgment of the Circuit Court of Hillsborough County (Florida), convicting defendant of first-degree murder, and sentencing him to death for the strangulation murder of a 15-year-old girl whose body was found buried under a house.


OVERVIEW: When defendant tried to force himself on the 15-year-old victim, she kicked him in the groin. Defendant then strangled her and buried her under the house along with her pocketbook and some clothing to make it appear as if she had run away. Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. Defendant challenged his conviction on four grounds. The supreme court held that: (1) defendant's confession was properly admitted; (2) the trial court did not violate defendant's sixth amendment right to confront witnesses by allegedly limiting his cross-examination of two state's witnesses; (3) the trial court did not err in permitting the state to elicit certain testimony from a witness on redirect examination; and (4) death-qualified juries were constitutional. In addition, defendant's six claims of error in the penalty phase of the proceeding were without merit.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction of first-degree murder and death sentence for the strangulation murder of a minor was affirmed because his allegations of procedural and evidentiary error were without merit and, therefore, did not mandate reversal of his conviction or sentence on appeal.

99 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Schommer v. Bentley


No. 68,335


Supreme Court of Florida


500 So. 2d 118; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 3009; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 55



December 24, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal, Certified Great Public Importance, Second District - Case No. 85-1289.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorneys sought review of a decision of the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida), which certified questions of great public importance after affirming a trial court's denial of petitioner's motions for attorney fees in excess of those allowed under Fla. Stat. ch. 925.036 (1983).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner attorneys were appointed to represent a defendant charged with murder. After the trial, petitioners filed motions for attorney fees in excess of those allowed under Fla. Stat. ch. 925.036 (1983). The trial judge acknowledged that the fees requested were reasonable under the circumstances, but believed he could not award more than the maximum allowed under the statute. The intermediate court affirmed the trial court's final order and petitioners sought review. The appellate court quashed the decision and remanded the case for a determination of reasonable fees. The court found that trial courts had the inherent power to allow, in extraordinary and unusual cases, departure from the statute's fee guidelines when necessary in order to ensure that an attorney who had served the public by defending an accused was not compensated in an amount which was insufficient given his or her time, energy, and talent.


OUTCOME: The court quashed and remanded the decision that petitioner attorneys' motion for attorney fees in excess of those allowed by statute where the court found that departure from statutory fee guidelines was allowed when necessary to appropriately compensate an attorney who served the public by defending an accused.

 

100 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wimberly


No. 67,847


Supreme Court of Florida


498 So. 2d 929; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2930; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 633



December 11, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance, First District - Case No. BD-470.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state sought review of a judgment from the First District Court of Appeal (Florida) that reversed respondent's conviction for battery of a law enforcement officer because the trial judge refused to instruct the jury on the necessarily included lesser included offense of simple battery. Petitioner asserted that under amended Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.510, the judge did not have to instruct that there was no supporting evidence.


OVERVIEW: In a certified question appeal, the court held that if the evidence at trial was sufficient to convict respondent of a necessarily lesser included offense, and the same evidence also incontrovertibly showed that the necessarily lesser included offense could not have been committed without also committing the greater charged offense, Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.510(b) required the trial judge to instruct the jury on the necessarily lesser included offense. Respondent was charged with battery of a law enforcement officer pursuant to Fla. Stat. Ann. § 843.01. The trial judge refused to instruct the jury on the necessarily included lesser included offense of simple battery. The court held that the trial judge had no discretion and must instruct on all necessarily included lesser included offenses, regardless of the degree of proof supporting the conviction for the greater offense. The court explained that instructing on the necessarily included lesser included offense allowed the jury to retain its pardon power and was required under amendments to Rule 3.510(b).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that reversed respondent's conviction. The court held that the trial judge erred by refusing to instruct on the necessarily included lesser included offense of simple battery. The court held that under the amended rules of procedure, a trial judge must instruct on all necessarily included lesser included offenses regardless of the degree of proof supporting the conviction for the greater offense.

 

101 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. Wainwright


No. 69,608


Supreme Court of Florida


497 So. 2d 872; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2809; 12 Fla. L. Weekly 89



November 13, 1986 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner, under a second death warrant after his conviction for first-degree murder, petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus and asked for a stay of his impending execution, raising several claims.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner prisoner's conviction for first-degree murder and his sentence of death were affirmed on direct appeal. After the signing of his first death warrant, petitioner filed a motion for post-conviction relief that the trial court denied. The supreme court affirmed the denial of relief. The signing of petitioner's second death warrant prompted petitioner to petition for a writ of habeas corpus and ask for the stay of his impending execution. Petitioner's counsel first claimed that he was incompetent for execution. If petitioner's counsel wished to pursue the claim, the supreme court directed them to initiate the sanity proceedings set out in Fla. Stat. ch. 922.07 (1985). If necessary, they would then to follow the procedure provided in Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.811. As to the remainder of the points in the petition, the supreme court found that they were either without merit or not cognizable in habeas corpus proceedings. Furthermore, regarding petitioner's claim of ineffective assistance of appellate counsel, the court found that he failed to meet the test set out in Strickland. The supreme court denied the petition for habeas corpus relief and the requested stay of execution.


OUTCOME: The supreme court denied petitioner prisoner's petition for a writ of habeas corpus and the requested stay of his impending execution. The supreme court found that most of petitioner's claims were either without merit or not cognizable in habeas corpus proceedings.

 

102 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Carroll v. Firestone


Nos. 69,410, 69,426


Supreme Court of Florida


497 So. 2d 1204; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2827; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 578



November 13, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Original Proceeding - Mandamus and a Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Leon County, J. Lewis Hall, Jr., Judge, Case No. 86-2952, Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. BP-345.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant electors sought review of a decision from the First District Court of Appeal (Florida), affirming a summary judgment finding that a proposed amendment to the Florida Constitution did not contravene Fla. Stat. ch. 101.161 or Fla. Const. art. XI, § 3. Appellants also filed an original petition for a writ of mandamus to direct appellee secretary of state to remove the proposed amendment from the ballot.


OVERVIEW: Appellant electors filed a petition for a writ of mandamus to compel appellee secretary of state to remove a proposed amendment to the Florida Constitution from the ballot. Appellants also sought review of a decision affirming a grant of summary judgment finding that the proposed amendment did not violate Fla. Const. art. XI, § 3, for failing to embrace but one subject and matter directly connected therewith, and Fla. Stat. ch. 101.161, for a ballot summary that did not adequately inform the electorate of the substance of the amendment. The court denied the writ of mandamus and affirmed the summary judgment, finding the provisions of the amendment directly related to each other because one identified a potential income source and the other identified the tentative recipient of the revenue. The court noted that the amendment itself specified which section would remain and which would be negated in the event a violation of the subject matter requirement were found to exist. The court concluded that the ballot summary sufficiently explained the substance of the amendment and that the summary was not required to explain every ramification of the proposed amendment.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for a writ of mandamus and affirmed the summary judgment, finding that the proposed amendment to the state constitution embraced but one subject and matter directly connected to it. The court determined that the ballot summary met the statutory requirement to adequately inform the electorate of the substance of the amendment.

 

103 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bloom


No. 68,900


Supreme Court of Florida


497 So. 2d 2; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2797; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 573



November 6, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Proceeding, Petition for Writ of Mandamus/or in the Alternative Writ of Prohibition.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state sought a writ of prohibition prohibiting respondent, a circuit court judge, from determining prior to trial the appropriateness of the death penalty in the event defendant was convicted of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner state requested the court to issue a writ of prohibition to prevent respondent, a circuit judge, from determining prior to trial the appropriateness of the death penalty in the event that defendant was convicted of first-degree murder. Petitioner also sought a writ of mandamus compelling respondent to excuse jurors who were unable to recommend a sentence of death. Petitioner argued that respondent had no authority to prejudge the death penalty's appropriateness because such a ruling unconstitutionally infringed on an executive function exclusively within a prosecutor's discretion. The court held that respondent had no authority to interfere with the prosecutor's discretion in proceeding as a death penalty case. The court reasoned that allowing respondent to make pre-trial determinations of the death penalty's applicability would effectively create a statutorily unauthorized trifurcated death sentence procedure. Based on this conclusion, the court granted the petition for writ of prohibition but withheld the formal issuance of the writ.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner state's request for a writ of prohibition preventing respondent circuit judge from determining prior to trial the appropriateness of the death penalty in the event of a conviction of first-degree murder. The court held that respondent lacked authority to decide before trial whether the death penalty would be imposed in a first-degree murder case.

 

104 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


State v. Powell


No. 67,755


Supreme Court of Florida


497 So. 2d 1188; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 3044; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 557



October 30, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 22, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Marion County, William T. Swigert, Judge - Case Nos. 83-2790 B & 84-2025 B - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, Fifth District - Case Nos. 85-1354 & 85-1380.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a decision from the Trial Court, in and for Marion County (Florida) which found Fla. Stat. ch. 732.9185, authorizing the removal of corneal tissue from deceased persons, to be unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellee family members sued appellant state after appellant coroner removed corneal tissue from decedents pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 732.9185. The trial court granted summary judgment to the appellees and found that the statute was unconstitutional because it deprived survivors of their fundamental personal property rights to dispose of their deceased next of kin and, further, because it was an unconstitutional taking for a non-public purpose. Appellant state sought review. The court reversed and remanded. It found that Fla. Stat. ch. 732.9185 was constitutional because the record clearly established that the statute reasonably achieved the permissible legislative objective of providing sight to citizens. Furthermore, the court found that a person's constitutional rights terminated at death, that the next of kin did not have property rights in the remains of a decedent, and that the corneal tissue removal was not a taking of property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court decision and found that the corneal tissue statute was constitutional because it promoted a permissible state objective and because family members had no property interests in a deceased person's body.

 

105 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Provenzano v. State


No. 65,663


Supreme Court of Florida


497 So. 2d 1177; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2755; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 541



October 16, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 22, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Clifford B. Shepard, Judge - Case No. 84-835-CF Div. 11.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida) decision that, after a jury trial, convicted him of first-degree murder under the transferred intent doctrine and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged a trial court decision that convicted him, following a jury trial, of first-degree murder under the theory of transferred intent and sentenced him to death. The state supreme court affirmed the decision of the trial court. Appellant's conviction was supported by substantial and competent evidence. A jury instruction on transferred intent was proper because it was supported by evidence that indicated that appellant had a premeditated design to kill police officers that directly resulted in the death of another human being. The facts indicated that at the time the murder was committed, appellant was attempting to effectuate his premeditated design to kill police officers. Substantial evidence indicated that appellant formed a premeditated design to kill the victim. The trial court did not deny appellant a fair trial by denying his venue change request. The trial court did not have a great difficulty in impaneling a fair and impartial jury and appellant failed to raise a presumption of partiality. The imposition of the death sentence was proper after the trial court judge found that aggravating circumstances far outweighed any mitigating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed a trial court decision that, after a jury trial, convicted appellant of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death. Appellant's conviction was supported by substantial and competent evidence of transferred intent and premeditation. The death sentence imposed was proper after the trial court judge determined that mitigating factors were far outweighed by aggravating factors.

107 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Marr v. State


No. 67,349


Supreme Court of Florida


494 So. 2d 1139; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2687; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 499



September 25, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance, First District - Case No. AU-499.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, who was convicted him of sexual battery, sought review of an order of the First District Court of Appeal (Florida), on rehearing, that upheld a finding that Fla. Stat. ch. 794.022(2) (1983) was constitutional but vacated a decision holding that a jury instruction requested by petitioner should have been given. A question was certified regarding the appropriateness of the instruction.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of sexual battery. The sole evidence offered by the state was the testimony of the victim. Petitioner tried to inquire into the victim's sexual relationship with her boyfriend. The trial court held that the questions were barred by Fla. Stat. ch. 794.022(2) (1983), and held that the statute did not deny petitioner his constitutional right to confrontation. Petitioner's requested jury instruction requiring rigid scrutiny of the victim's testimony was denied. The district court, on rehearing, vacated a decision requiring that the instruction be given and posed a certified question regarding whether the instruction was appropriate. The supreme court held that it was not and approved the district court's decision. The standard jury instruction was adequate, counsel had the opportunity to indicate that the case turned on the victim's testimony, and petitioner's constitutional rights were not abridged. The requested instruction was improper because it went to the weight of the evidence. A victim's sexual activity with others was not admissible unless relevant. In petitioner's case, any relevance regarding the victim's bias was outweighed by policy concerns.


OUTCOME: The court answered a certified question in the negative and approved the decision of the district court on rehearing, holding that petitioner's requested instruction regarding rigid scrutiny of the victim's testimony was not appropriate in a sexual battery case. Defense counsel had the opportunity to indicate that the case turned on the victim's testimony, and the instruction was improper because it related to the weight to be given the evidence.

Post-conviction relief denied at Lambrix v. State, 124 So. 3d 890, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 1306 (Fla., June 27, 2013)
Post-conviction relief denied at Lambrix v. State, 139 So. 3d 298, 2014 Fla. LEXIS 1058 (Fla., Mar. 27, 2014)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Lambrix v. Sec'y, Fla. Dep't of Corr., 756 F.3d 1246, 2014 U.S. App. LEXIS 12052 (11th Cir. Fla., June 26, 2014)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Lambrix v. State, 217 So. 3d 977, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 510 (Fla., Mar. 9, 2017)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Lambrix v. Jones, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 1929 (Fla., Sept. 26, 2017)
Post-conviction relief denied at Lambrix v. State, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 1944 (Fla., Sept. 29, 2017)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Without prejudice, Motion denied by, Without prejudice Lambrix v. Sec'y, DOC, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 162170 (M.D. Fla., Oct. 2, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Glades County, Case No. 83-12, Richard M. Stanley, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Glades County (Florida) that convicted him of two counts of first-degree murder and imposed two death sentences. Appellant contended that numerous errors occurred during the guilt phase of his trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction of two counts of first-degree murder and his two death sentences, asserting that errors occurred during the guilt phase of the trial. He argued that death-qualified juries were unconstitutional, that a juror was improperly excluded for cause, and that his U.S. Const. amend. VI right to confront witnesses was violated by improper restriction on the cross-examination of a witness, among other alleged errors. The supreme court affirmed the convictions and sentences. The court reasserted its position that death-qualified juries were constitutional, noting that the proper standard for excluding jurors in death cases was the Adams test, which held that a juror could not be challenged for his views on capital punishment unless those views prevented or impaired his performance of duties as a juror under his instructions and oath. The supreme court held that the trial judge was in the best position to make the judgment and found no error. Further, the court found that cross-examination was not unduly restricted when the question posed might have been relevant, but its probative value was outweighed by the danger of misleading or confusing the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's first-degree murder convictions and death sentences. The trial court did not commit error in allowing a death-qualified jury or in excluding a juror for cause after determining that the juror's views would impair the performance of her duties. Nor did the trial court err by restricting cross examination when the question posed was potentially relevant but was likely to mislead the jury.

Rinker Materials Corp. v. Lake Park


No. 68,582


Supreme Court of Florida


494 So. 2d 1123; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2434; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 437

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County (Florida) that validated bonds issued by appellee town council for certain planned roadway, drainage, water, and sewer improvements.


OVERVIEW: Appellee town council adopted a resolution, under Fla. Stat. Ch. 170.03, authorizing the construction and financing of roadway, drainage, water, and sewer improvements. The resolution also provided that the assessments should be levied on a combined front-foot and square-foot basis and instructed consulting engineers to prepare and file with the clerk and assessment roll. However, appellee decided to change the method of assessment and did so by adopting a new resolution. Ch. 163 did not apply to the present case, and thus, the parties' arguments regarding this statute were inapplicable. Also, the court held that the assessment of appellant's property was not arbitrary because it was based on sufficient recommendations from an expert.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that validated the bonds issued by appellee and held that appellant was offered adequate notice as not to deprive it of due process.

In Interest of R.W.


No. 68,245


Supreme Court of Florida


495 So. 2d 133; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2469; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 427



August 21, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 22, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal -- Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity, Fifth District - Case No. 84-1414.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant agency sought review of an order of the Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida) reversing an order terminating appellee mother's parental rights based on a finding that Fla. Stat. ch. 39.41(1)(f)1.d (1983) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant agency's petition for permanent termination of appellee mother's parental rights under Fla. Stat. ch. 39.41(1)(f)1.d (1983) was granted based solely on appellee's failure to substantially comply with a performance agreement drafted by appellant. The appellate court reversed the termination order, finding that Fla. Stat. ch. 39.41(1)(f)1.d (1983) was unconstitutional. Appellant sought review. The court held that in order for appellee's parental rights to be permanently terminated, appellant had to show abandonment and abuse or neglect of the children by clear and convincing evidence. Because the statute allowed appellee's parental rights to be permanently terminated based solely on her failure to comply with a performance agreement, the statute unconstitutionally infringed on appellee's fundamental right to custody of her children. The court therefore affirmed the appellate court order reversing the termination of appellee's parental rights.


OUTCOME: The order reversing an order terminating appellee mother's parental rights was affirmed because appellee's parental rights were terminated solely because of her failure to comply with a performance agreement drafted by appellant agency, and the statute allowing termination on such grounds was unconstitutional.

112 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


United Tel. Co. v. Public Service Com.


Nos. 66,673, 66,633 (Consolidated)


Supreme Court of Florida


496 So. 2d 116; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2401; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 330



July 17, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 14, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Consolidated Appeals from the Public Service Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant local exchange carriers sought review of an order from the Florida Public Service Commission, which modified a revenue distribution contract between appellants. Appellants urged that the commission had no jurisdiction to modify the contract.


OVERVIEW: Appellant local exchange carriers (LEC) had a revenue-sharing agreement that was based in part on certain accounting expenses each incurred. Because another LEC, which was a party to the agreement, was also a regional Bell operating company, it had been required to divest certain assets to which the expenses related, and it petitioned the Florida Public Service Commission (commission) for a rate increase. The commission instead issued an order modifying the revenue-sharing agreement to permit this LEC to participate in the revenues as if it was still incurring the expenses. Holding that the commission lacked jurisdiction to modify the agreement, the court quashed the order and remanded. The court held that the presumption of regularity applicable upon review of commission orders did not apply to those orders that were beyond the commission's power. The court held that neither Fla. Stat. ch. 364.055 nor Fla. Stat. ch. 364.14 conferred authority on the commission to alter practices that did not affect ratepayers. The court also held that such unauthorized interference was an unconstitutional impairment of the obligation of contracts.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the order and remanded. The court held that the order was entered without jurisdiction because the public service agency had no authority to modify the revenue-sharing agreement where the agreement did not adversely affect ratepayers.

 

113 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Makemson v. Martin County


No. 66,780


Supreme Court of Florida


491 So. 2d 1109; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2359; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 337



July 17, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance, Fourth District - Case No. 83-1138.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorneys challenged an order of the Court of Appeal, Fourth District (Florida) that quashed the trial court's order declaring Fla. Stat. ch. 925.036 unconstitutional. Petitioners sought to obtain an amount that exceeded the statutory maximum for fees for representation of indigent criminal defendants.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner attorneys were appointed by the court pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 925.036 to represent an indigent defendant at trial and on appeal. Petitioners sought more than the amount allowed by Fla. Stat. ch. 925.036(2)(e) for attorney fees because an extraordinary amount of time was spent on the case. The court found that it was within the inherent power of Florida's trial courts to allow, in extraordinary and unusual cases, departure from the statute's fee guidelines when necessary in order to ensure that an attorney who has served the public by defending the accused was not compensated in an amount which was confiscator of his or her time, energy, and talents. In sum, the court found that find the statute delineating the amount of attorney fees for indigent criminal defendants was directory rather than mandatory. Although facially valid, the statute was unconstitutional as applied because it curtailed the inherent power of the court to ensure adequate representation of the criminally accused.


OUTCOME: The order declaring that the maximum attorney fees statute was constitutional was quashed because petitioner attorneys were entitled to just compensation for the extraordinary and tenuous legal representation provided in their case. The court held that although facially valid, the statute was unconstitutional when applied in such a manner as to curtail its power to ensure adequate representation of the criminally accused.

 

114 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Parikh v. Cunningham


No. 67,033


Supreme Court of Florida


493 So. 2d 999; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2410; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 309



July 10, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 17, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity, Fifth District - Case No. 83-763.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant physician sought review of a decision of the Fifth District Court of Appeal, (Florida), which reversed a trial court decision that had declared as unconstitutional the Medical Consent statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 768.46 (1983). A determination was sought concerning whether the statute was statutorily or constitutionally invalid.


OVERVIEW: Appellee and her husband brought an action against appellant physician on theories of negligence and lack of informed consent after appellee wife suffered complications from a surgery appellant had performed. Fla. Stat. ch. 768.46(3)(a)(2), part of the Florida medical consent law, required that physicians explain the proposed treatment or procedure, any medically acceptable alternatives to the proposed treatment or procedure, and the substantial risks and hazards inherent in the proposed treatment or procedure. The trial court had held for appellant physician but provided the jury with an improper instruction that suggested that a written consent was a valid consent. Appellees successfully challenged the trial court decision on appeal when appellant's application for state supreme court review was granted and ch. 768.46 was upheld as constitutional. The court found the appeals court had misread a crucial element of ch. 768.46(4)(a) that provided a consent which was evidenced in writing and met ch. 768.46(3) was presumed to be a valid consent, but remanded for a new trial on the issue of informed consent because the misleading jury instruction possibly affected the jury verdict.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appeals court as to the finding of unconstitutionality because the appeals court had misread a crucial element of the statutory presumption, but affirmed that because the jury's verdict may have been based on a misleading instruction suggesting that a written consent was a valid consent, the erroneous jury instruction given required remand for a new trial on the issue of informed consent.

McGuire v. State


No. 66,925


Supreme Court of Florida


489 So. 2d 729; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2225; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 263



June 12, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance, Fourth District - Case No. 84-648.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirming the trial court's conviction of defendant for violating a state regulation, Fla. Admin. Code Ann. r. 16D-2.04(1)(e), by appearing topless on a public beach.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was cited for jogging topless on a public beach in violation of a regulation requiring proper bathing attire. The court of appeal upheld defendant's conviction and rejected her contention that the regulation in question, Fla. Admin. Code Ann. r. 16D-2.04(1)(e), was vague and overbroad. On further appeal, the state supreme court upheld the rulings of both lower courts. The court noted that defendant had no grounds to complain about any overbreadth in the regulation because public nudity was unprotected by U.S. Const. amend. I. Thus, it was entirely within the state's purview to prohibit total and partial public nudity. The court further held that the posted regulation's language, while perhaps not as precise as it could have been, was nonetheless sufficiently clear that a person of ordinary intelligence would understand what it prohibited. Accordingly, the court affirmed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for violating the decency regulation was affirmed. The court held that defendant lacked standing to complain about the challenged regulation's overbreadth, public nudity being constitutionally unprotected activity, and further held that the regulation in question was sufficiently clear as to give defendant fair warning of what actions were prohibited.

 

117 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


State v. Saiez


No. 67,249


Supreme Court of Florida


489 So. 2d 1125; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2234; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 262



June 12, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory of Constitutional Invalidity Third District - Case No. 84-1619.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought reversal of the judgment of the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida) declaring Fla. Stat. ch. 817.63 (1983) unconstitutional and upholding a trial court's dismissal on constitutional grounds of charges of unlawful possession of embossing machines brought against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant moved to dismiss charges of unlawful possession of embossing machines on the ground that the statute criminalizing such possession was unconstitutional. The trial court ruled that the statute in question, Fla. Stat. ch. 817.63 (1983), was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague, and the trial court dismissed the charges. A state appellate court upheld that judgment. On further appeal, the state supreme court affirmed, albeit on different grounds. The court ruled that ch. 817.63 was not overbroad, inasmuch as free speech rights were not implicated; nor was it vague, inasmuch as a person of ordinary intelligence could discern what conduct the statute deemed criminal. However, the court held that ch. 817.63 violated substantive due process restrictions in that it criminalized mere possession of ordinary objects without any requirement that the object be possessed with criminal intent. As such, it unconstitutionally invaded the sphere of personal liberty.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was affirmed because the statute criminalizing the possession of embossing machines unconstitutionally failed to require that such possession be with criminal intent.

Cantor v. Davis


Nos. 64,663, 64,664


Supreme Court of Florida


489 So. 2d 18; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2189; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 249



June 5, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Applications for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity, Third District - Case No. 82-1392.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner physicians sought review of an order from the District Court of Appeal, Third District (Florida), awarding respondent patient attorney fees in her medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner physicians challenged an order awarding respondent patient attorney fees in her medical malpractice action. Petitioners contended that Fla. Stat. ch. 768.56 (1981), which provided for the award of attorney fees in civil actions, was unconstitutional as applied to respondent's action. The court reversed and remanded the order and found that the statute had been unconstitutionally applied to respondent's case. The court further found that petitioners were not given a realistic opportunity to argue the matter in the lower court.


OUTCOME: The order awarding respondent patient attorney fees in her medical malpractice action against petitioner physicians was reversed and remanded because the state statute providing for the award of attorney fees was unconstitutionally applied to respondent's case.

 

119 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Garcia v. State


No. 64,841


Supreme Court of Florida


492 So. 2d 360; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2190; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 251



June 5, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 25, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal and a Cross-Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Manatee County, Robert E. Hensley, Judge -- Case No. 82-1196F-B.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Circuit Court in and for Manatee County (Florida) for two counts of first-degree murder, three counts of robbery, and one count of conspiracy to commit an armed robbery with a firearm. Defendant further appealed two death sentences on the murder convictions.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for two counts of first-degree murder, three counts of robbery, and one count of conspiracy to commit an armed robbery with a firearm. The court found that no reversible error occurred based on defendant's absences during crucial stages of his trial because he either waived his absence or the alleged absence constituted harmless error. The court held that defendant's statements to officers were voluntary because defendant acknowledged and waived his right to remain silent and to have a lawyer present. With respect to a statement to an officer who transported him to jail, the court held that the trial court properly admitted this statement because defendant gave it spontaneously and not under interrogation by the officer. The court held that defendant's remaining points of error were without merit and affirmed his two death sentences. The court found no error in the fact that defendant's three accomplices were not sentenced to death because defendant's aggravating factors far outweighed his mitigating factors. The court reversed the lower court's dismissal of defendant's attempted murder charge and remanded for sentencing on that charge.


OUTCOME: The court found no reversible error and affirmed defendant's conviction for two counts of first-degree murder, three counts of robbery, and one count of conspiracy to commit an armed robbery with a firearm. The court affirmed defendant's death sentences and reversed the lower court's dismissal of defendant's attempted murder charge and remanded for sentencing on that charge.

Department of Ins. v. Dade County Consumer Advocate's Office


No. 66,178


Supreme Court of Florida


492 So. 2d 1032; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2237; 90 A.L.R.4th 193; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 240



June 3, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 10, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity First District - Case No. AV-400.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the state department of insurance, sought review from a First District Court of Appeal (Florida) decision that found insurance anti-rebate statutes, Fla. Stat. chs. 626.611(11) and 626.9541(1)(h) (1983), were unconstitutional and an invalid exercise of the state's police power. The action was brought by appellees, a county consumer advocates office, challenging the statutes.


OVERVIEW: Appellees filed a complaint alleging that the anti-rebate statutes, Fla. Stat. chs. 626.111(11) and 626.9541(1)(h) (1983), violated Fla. Const. art. I, § 9 by preventing price competition with respect to insurance agents' commissions. The trial court found that the challenged statutes were a valid exercise of state police power and entered summary judgment in favor of appellants. The district court reversed and held that there was no legitimate state interest to justify the continued existence of the anti-rebate statutes. The state supreme court affirmed the district court's decision and held that the anti-rebate statutes were void under the state constitution to the extent they prevented rebating any portion of an insurance agent's commission to insurance customers. The court held that that the legislation was not within the scope of state police power. There was no identifiable relationship between the anti-rebate statutes and a legitimate state purpose in safeguarding public health, safety, or general welfare.


OUTCOME: In affirming the district court's decision, the state supreme court held that the anti-rebate statutes were unconstitutional because the legislation was not designed to promote public health, safety, or welfare and there was no relationship between the enactments and any legitimate state interest.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court in and for Seminole County (Florida), denying his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 from a death sentence imposed by the trial judge after the jury convicted defendant of first degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner collaterally attacked via Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 a death sentence imposed by the trial court after a jury convicted him of committing first degree murder. On appeal, the court held that (1) defendant was permitted to present evidence of non-statutory mitigating factors at his sentencing hearing; (2) defense counsel was not ineffective for failing to discover and reveal the suggestiveness of hypnosis performed on a key state's witness even though, nine years after defendant's conviction, such evidence was held to be per se inadmissible in Florida criminal trials; (3) counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise defendant's competency as an issue; and (4) Florida's jury override procedure was constitutional under the federal and state constitutions. The court affirmed denial of postconviction relief and vacated its stay of execution.
