Commission on Ethics v. Sullivan


No. 67,689


Supreme Court of Florida


489 So. 2d 10; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2168; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 210



May 8, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 24, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Leon County, J. Lewis Hall, Jr., Judge - Case No. 81-1330 Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. BI-273.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Florida Commission on Ethics, appealed the judgment of the trial court in Leon County (Florida), which held that Fla. Code Ann. § 112.321(1) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Two complaints were filed with the Florida Commission on Ethics (FCE) against appellees alleging breach of the public trust while each served as supervisor of elections and deputy supervisor of elections for the county. The circuit court held that the statute regarding the FCE, Fla. Code Ann. § 112.321(1), was unconstitutional. The Commission appealed, and the question of the constitutionality of the statute was certified. Appellees contended that the FCE belonged to the executive department, and was subject to the appointments clause of the Florida Constitution, Fla. Const. art. IV, § 1(f), which places the power to appoint vacancies of the executive branch with the governor. They claimed FCE members were improperly appointed. The court found that the FCE was constitutional and reversed the order of the trial court and remanded. The court found the FCE is a part of the legislative branch of Florida government, and its membership may be drawn in whatever manner the legislature deems appropriate. Thus, the appointments scheme did not violate the Florida Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the trial court, finding that the Florida Commission on Ethics was constitutionally constituted, and its appointment scheme did not violate the Florida Constitution.

 

126 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Storer Cable T.V., Inc. v. Summerwinds Apartments Associates, Ltd.


Nos. 65,620, 65,993


Supreme Court of Florida


493 So. 2d 417; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 1741; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 100



March 13, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Consolidated Appeals from the District Court of Appeal, Third District - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity, Case Nos. 83-2433 and 83-2769.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review from the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida), which declared Fla. Stat. Ann. § 83.66 (1982) unconstitutional and found that placement of cable television equipment on apartment complex property that was not specifically held out for tenant use constituted a taking.


OVERVIEW: Appellant cable providers responded to tenant requests for cable television service. Appellee landlords refused to allow appellants to provide the service. Appellants alleged it had a right pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 83.66 (1982) to enter appellees' apartment complexes to install cable television equipment. The supreme court affirmed the district court's decision that Fla. Stat. ch. 83.66, which prohibited landlords from denying cable television access to tenants and provided that no compensation would be paid to the landlord for such access, was unconstitutional. Fla. Stat. ch. 83.66 was unconstitutional under the Fifth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. V, because it required a taking of property without justification or due process of law. The supreme court determined that the statute allowed cable providers, under authorization from the state, to install equipment on property that was not held out for tenant use. The supreme court concluded that, essentially, a portion of the landlord's property would be taken. The supreme court further concluded that striking the no compensation language from the statute would arm appellants with eminent domain power.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the district court's decision. The supreme court found that the statute that authorized the placement of cable television equipment on apartment complex property constituted a taking and violated the Fifth Amendment because the statute essentially allowed cable providers, acting under state authorization, to install equipment on property not held out for tenant use, essentially taking landlord property.

Florida Patient's Compensation Fund v. Tillman


Nos. 65,736, 65-997, 65-998, 66,025


Supreme Court of Florida


487 So. 2d 1032; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 1693; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 74



February 27, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 28, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Four Consolidated Cases: Three Notices and One Cross-Notice for Application for Review of the Decisions of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions Fourth District - Case No. 82-1197, 82-1199, 82-1370, 82-1433, 82-1527 & 82-1823 and an Appeal from the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District, Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity, Case Nos. 82-1199 & 82-1370.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Application was made for consolidated review of the decisions of the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida), which, in a medical malpractice case against petitioner doctor, hospital, and compensation fund, affirmed all of respondent's award except the award of attorney fees to respondent and the reduction of respondent's award from petitioner doctor due to respondent's personal negligence.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner doctor argued that the two-year malpractice statute of limitations, Fla. Stat. ch. 95.11(4)(b) (1979), barred respondent's claim. The court found the lower court was correct in concluding that the evidence was sufficient to present a question to the jury. The jury instruction and verdict form on the statute of limitations were also properly presented to the jury. Petitioner doctor had withdrawn his defense of comparative negligence and, therefore, the lower court was correct in assessing the full measure of damages. The lower court was also correct in denying respondent attorney's fees because Fla. Stat. ch. 768.56 (1980) could not be applied to a cause of action accruing before its effective date. Petitioner hospital was correct in its assertions that the limitation of liability provisions of ch. 768.54 were constitutional and that portion of the decision was quashed, but the lower court properly concluded that the issue of negligence was a question for the jury. As to petitioner compensation fund, ch. 95.11(4)(b) precluded recovery in actions brought after the two-year statute of limitations period had expired, and the lower court's decision on that point was quashed.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court was affirmed in part, quashed in part, and remanded. The question of the statute of limitations was properly presented to the jury and full damages were properly assessed where petitioner doctor withdrew his defense. The question of petitioner hospital's negligence was also for the jury and recovery was precluded against petitioner compensation fund in actions brought once the statute of limitations had expired.

 

128 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


State v. Daytona Beach


No. 67,318


Supreme Court of Florida


484 So. 2d 1214; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 1695; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 80



February 27, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, William C. Johnson, Jr., Judge - Case No. 85-166-CA-01 Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review from the Circuit Court, Volusia County (Florida), which validated revenue bonds for redevelopment in the downtown area of appellee city. Appellant contended that requiring contribution of tax increment revenue funds from special taxing districts was an unconstitutional violation of Fla. Const. art. VII, § 9(a).


OVERVIEW: The lower court validated appellee city's proposed redevelopment revenue bonds, the repayment of which was to be obtained from marina operating revenue, utilities service tax, and downtown area tax increment revenue. Appellant state argued that the redevelopment project did not have the required connection with the downtown area tax districts that contributed to the redevelopment fund. The court affirmed. Fla. Stat. ch. 163.353 provided general authority to taxing districts to appropriate funds to redevelopment trust funds and ch. 163.387 provided that no taxing authority was exempt from contributing to a redevelopment tax fund. Such statutes were constitutional, contrary to appellant's assertions. Tax increment revenues were based on the increase brought about by the increased value of redeveloped property, and the amount of the special taxing district's contribution would never exceed the amount of the increment. It was within the legislature's power to make community redevelopment one of the respective purposes of special taxing districts.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court validating the issuance by appellee city of proposed redevelopment revenue bonds was affirmed because special taxing districts were allowed to contribute tax increment revenues for repayment of the bonds based on the increased value of property redeveloped through a redevelopment tax fund as one of the approved purposes of such districts.

 

129 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jones


No. 66,373


Supreme Court of Florida


483 So. 2d 433; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 1669; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 67



February 20, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance, Second District - Case No. 83-2547.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a decision of the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) quashing the circuit court's affirmance and reversing respondent's conviction for driving under the influence in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 316.193 (1981).


OVERVIEW: Police established a roadblock for the admitted purpose of apprehending DUI drivers. The police blocked lanes to form a funnel, requiring all traffic to travel in one lane and to pass an officer stationed on the roadway. That officer had instructions to stop every fifth automobile during heavy traffic and every third automobile during light traffic. Respondent drove a car which the police diverted. After respondent failed several field sobriety tests, the police took him into custody. A decision reversing respondent's conviction for driving under the influence in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 316.193 (1981) was affirmed. It was essential that a written set of uniform guidelines be issued before a roadblock can be utilized. Law enforcement officials had to conduct sobriety checkpoints so as to minimize the discretion of field officers. Roadblocks did not need to stop every car. Law enforcement officials had to keep the degree of intrusion upon motorists and the length of detention of each driver to a minimum. Petitioner failed to prove that the roadblock procedure met the balancing test and therefore it violated the requirements of U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction because, although roadblocks could be set up to pass constitutional muster, the roadblock in respondent's case did not meet the balancing test and violated the Fourth Amendment.

Microtel, Inc. v. Florida Public Service Com.


Nos. 66,125, 66,403, 66,404


Supreme Court of Florida


483 So. 2d 415; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 1801; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 50



February 6, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Three Consolidated Appeals from the Public Service Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant telecommunications corporations sought to overturn the rulings of appellee state public service commission (Florida) granting toll monopolies to local telephone exchange companies for short-haul long-distance telephone service.


OVERVIEW: Appellant telecommunications corporations challenged the decision of appellee state public service commission to grant toll monopolies to local telephone exchange companies for short-haul long distance telephone service. The court affirmed appellee's ruling. The court held that Fla. Stat. ch. 364.335(4) granted appellee the power to grant such monopolies if they were in the public interest, and the legislature was within its rights to grant appellee that authority. The court also held that ch. 364.335(4) was not an unconstitutional grant of legislative authority to appellee, and the lack of standards or guidelines to govern such monopolies was of no moment given that the arrangement was anticipated as being temporary. The court further held that appellee's position with respect to the monopolies was not inconsistent with the position it took on the subject in federal court, and in any event it was within appellee's right to do so.


OUTCOME: The orders of appellee state public service commission granting toll monopolies to local telephone exchange companies were affirmed. Appellee had the authority to grant the monopolies, the grants were in the public interest, and judicial estoppel did not bar the position taken by appellee with respect to the monopolies.

Harvard v. State


No. 67,556


Supreme Court of Florida


486 So. 2d 537; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 1802; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 55

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County (Florida), which denied his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, and also requested a stay of execution. Appellant had been convicted of first degree murder of his former wife and was sentenced to death again upon a resentencing proceeding, to which the court had previously affirmed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first degree murder of his former wife and sentenced to death. The court affirmed the conviction but vacated the death sentence. The trial judge again imposed a death sentence upon resentencing. Appellant moved for postconviction relief, which the trial court denied under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Appellant challenged that order and requested a stay of execution. The court noted that in his order denying relief, the trial judge addressed the allegation that he failed to consider nonstatutory mitigating circumstances and expressly found that reasonable lawyers and judges at the time of appellant's trial could have mistakenly believed that nonstatutory mitigating circumstances could not be considered. In view of the trial judge's statement, and because appellant's presentation at his resentencing proceeding was improperly limited by the court's prior order, the court held that appellant's sentence was imposed in violation of United States Supreme Court precedent. Thus, the decision below was reversed in part, and remanded for a new sentencing hearing in which appellant would be allowed to present all appropriate nonstatutory mitigating evidence.


OUTCOME: The denial of appellant's motion for postconviction relief from death sentence was reversed in part because appellant's presentation at his resentencing proceeding was improperly limited by the court in a prior order and the trial judge had failed to consider nonstatutory mitigating circumstances. The cause was remanded for a new sentencing hearing in which appellant would be allowed to present all appropriate nonstatutory mitigating evidence.

Casselberry v. Orange County Police Benevolent Asso.


No. 66,155


Supreme Court of Florida


482 So. 2d 336; 1986 Fla. LEXIS 1533; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 28



January 9, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Constitutional Construction, First District - Case No. AS-43.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner city appealed the judgment of the First District Court of Appeal (Florida) after it ruled for respondent union and held that petitioner was required to bargain collectively with respondent union on the subject of alternate grievance procedures. Also before the court was whether petitioner committed an unfair labor practice during negotiations with respondent union where respondent union declared an impasse.


OVERVIEW: Before the court was whether petitioner city, which had established provisions for demotion and discharge of police officers in its civil service ordinance, was required to bargain collectively with respondent union on those issues to the extent of establishing and being subject to alternate grievance procedures. The second issue was whether petitioner committed an unfair labor practice during its negotiations with respondent union where respondent union declared an impasse during discussions about the subject of demotion and discharge grievance procedures. The supreme court approved the lower court's decision in part and quashed it in part. The supreme court held that Fla. Stat. ch. 474.401 (1981) was constitutional and that civil service ordinances did not affect the required bargaining powers. The statute did not threaten to undermine local civil service systems statewide because it was designed to co-exist with local civil service systems and was not intended to replace them. The supreme court quashed the lower court's finding that petitioner committed an unfair labor practice because it was not an unfair labor practice to urge a certain position in the bargaining process.


OUTCOME: The supreme court approved in part and quashed in part the lower court's judgment. The supreme court held that the statute at issue was constitutional and that civil service ordinances did not affect the required bargaining powers between petitioner city and respondent union. The supreme court quashed the lower court's finding that petitioner city committed an unfair labor practice during negotiations respondent union.

 

133 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Harden v. Garrett


No. 67,531


Supreme Court of Florida


483 So. 2d 409; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 1421; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 13



December 20, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 12, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Leon County, Charles E. Miner, Jr., Judge, Case No. 84-3311-Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. BI-102.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Leon County Circuit Court (Florida), which dismissed appellant's complaint that alleged irregularities in an election for the Florida House of Representatives. Appellant argued that Fla. Stat. ch. 102.166, 102.168 (1983), pertaining to election contests, vested jurisdiction in the trial court.


OVERVIEW: Appellant lost an election for the Florida House of Representatives by 39 votes. Prior to dismissing his action for lack of jurisdiction, the trial court commented that the election had been "botched," and was fraught with manifest election law irregularities. Holding that Fla. Const. art. III, § 2, conclusively established that each house of Florida's legislature was the sole judge of the qualifications, elections, and returns of its members, the court affirmed the judgment. The court observed that, consistent with the constitution, the House of Representatives, in its internal rule 5.5, provided a mechanism for contesting the election of its members. The court held that a proper respect of the constitutionally mandated separation of powers required it to honor the language of art. III, § 2. The court also noted that the application of Fla. Stat. ch. 102.168 (1983) to a legislative election would actually permit a court to first evaluate the qualifications of and then unseat a member of the legislature, and created an impermissible risk of intrusion upon the constitutionally established legislative domain.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that dismissed appellant's complaint. The court held that pursuant to the state constitution, the houses of the legislature were the sole judges of the qualifications, elections, and returns of their members, and to permit judicial inquiry into the election appellant had lost would unconstitutionally intrude on the legislature's domain and violate the principle of separation of powers.

 

134 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Thompson v. Graham


No. 67,433


Supreme Court of Florida


481 So. 2d 1212; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 1424; 11 Fla. L. Weekly 15



December 19, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 19, 1986.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of mandamus to direct respondent Secretary of State to expunge certain vetoes of respondent governor from Florida's official records.


OVERVIEW: Respondent governor vetoed several of the appropriations in the committee substitute for senate bill 848 (CS/SB 848), 1985 Fla. Laws ch. 85-116. On the grounds that CS/SB 848 was not a general appropriations bill and was not subject to respondent governor's line item veto provided in Fla. Const. art. III, § 8(a), the Florida House of Representatives petitioned for a writ of mandamus directing respondent secretary of state to expunge the vetoes from Florida's official records. Petitioner, the speaker of the house, in his capacity as a citizen and taxpayer, joined the petition. The court treated the petition as if it were brought solely by petitioner in his capacity as a citizen and a taxpayer in order to avoid issues of standing. The court refused to issue the writ of mandamus. CS/SB 848 came within the definition of an appropriations bill. The appropriations contained in CS/SB 848 had been subject to respondent governor's line item veto. To grant mandamus would have had a chilling effect on the balance of power between the governor and the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court declined to issue the writ of mandamus directing respondent secretary of state to expunge respondent governor's vetoes from the state's official records because the appropriations in the bill at issue were subject to respondent governor's line item veto power.

Daytona Beach Shores v. State


Nos. 65,912, 66,700


Supreme Court of Florida


483 So. 2d 405; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 4185; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 629



December 12, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 12, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decision - Fifth District - Case No. 82-263. Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for St. Johns County, Richard O. Watson, Judge - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, Fifth District - Seventh Judicial Circuit, St. Johns County Case Nos. 84-577 CA and 84-578 CA; District Court of Appeal, Fifth District Case Nos. 85-279 and 85-291.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida) struck petitioner municipality's discriminatory ordinance that imposed beach access fees only on drivers, the Trial Court in and for St. Johns County (Florida) struck appellant municipalities' similar ordinance on the same grounds. Petitioner appealed, and the appellate court certified the trial court's judgment for review.


OVERVIEW: In two separate cases, the issue concerned the validity of beach "user fees" charged to drivers of motor vehicles for entry onto the Atlantic beaches within the jurisdictions of petitioner and appellant municipalities. In each case, the lower courts struck petitioner's and appellants' ordinances because the imposition of such access fees discriminated against persons who drove, rather than walked, to the beach. Upon consolidation, the court quashed and reversed the lower courts' opinions because no constitutional provision, including the public trust doctrine, impeded the imposition of reasonable user fees for access to sovereign lands when the revenue received was used solely for the maintenance, operation, and improvement of those lands. Moreover, Fla. Stat. ch. 161.58(2) (1985) resolved the issue by allowing local governments to authorize, by a three-fifths vote, vehicular traffic on public beaches if the revenues were used only for beach maintenance purposes. Finally, reasonable access fees were permissible classifications. Thus, the court remanded to determine if the beach access fees were reasonable and if the ordinances otherwise complied with ch. 161.58.


OUTCOME: After consolidating two cases, the court quashed the appellate court's striking of petitioner's ordinance that imposed public beach access fees upon drivers. Likewise, the court reversed the trial court's striking of appellants' similar ordinance. The court remanded both cases with directions to decide whether the fees were reasonable and whether they met the requirements of a newly enacted statute that allowed such fees under certain conditions.

 

136 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Toole v. State


No. 65,378


Supreme Court of Florida


479 So. 2d 731; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 4150; 51 A.L.R.4th 1231; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 617



November 25, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] A Notice and Cross-Notice of Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, James L. Harrison, Judge - Case No. 84-3340-CF Div. "R".


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of conviction from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida) of felony murder and sentence. Appellant argued, inter alia, trial court erred in allowing testimony he was a homosexual, and his death sentence was unconstitutionally founded upon improper doubling of aggravating circumstances of creating a great risk of death to many persons and committing the capital felony while engaged in commission of arson.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of felony murder conviction and sentence to death. Appellant argued the trial court erred in allowing testimony that he was a homosexual who had a relationship with the victim. The court held the fact that appellant knew the victim and had argued with him was relevant to prove motive, and the probative value outweighed any potential prejudicial impact. Appellant argued that his death sentence was unconstitutionally founded upon an improper doubling of the aggravating circumstances of creating a great risk of death to many persons and committing the capital felony while engaged in the commission of an arson. The court rejected that argument, concluding although arson may involve a great risk of death to many persons, this aggravating factor was dependent upon proof adduced at trial and was not necessarily encompassed by the felony of arson. The court held that the jury should have been properly instructed to consider the specific mitigating factor of mental disturbance. The issue had been preserved when the contemporaneous objection rule was satisfied-- there was a request for an instruction, the trial court understood and denied the specific request.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of guilt for first-degree felony murder. Because the jury should have been properly instructed on mitigating factor of extreme mental or emotional distress, the court vacated the death sentence and remanded.

Porter v. State


No. 67,805


Supreme Court of Florida


478 So. 2d 33; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3931; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 573



October 25, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at Porter v. Wainwright, 805 F.2d 930, 1986 U.S. App. LEXIS 33666 (11th Cir. Fla., 1986)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Charlotte County, Elmer O. Friday, Judge -- Case No. 78-199-CF-A-RMS.
Porter v. State, 429 So. 2d 293, 1983 Fla. LEXIS 2326 (Fla., 1983)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a state prisoner under a current death warrant, sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Charlotte County (Florida) which denied his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion for post-conviction relief without conducting an evidentiary hearing. Appellant also sought a stay of execution.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted appellant of the first-degree murder of an elderly couple in their home and recommended life imprisonment. The trial court, however, imposed two death sentences. Following appeals, remands, and resentencing, the governor signed appellant's death warrant. Appellant then filed a motion for post-conviction relief pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The trial court denied the motion without an evidentiary hearing. The court affirmed on appeal, finding that, because the motion conclusively showed appellant was not entitled to relief, the trial court did not err in denying the motion without a hearing. Appellant claimed, inter alia, that he had received ineffective assistance from trial and resentencing counsel because they failed to develop and present mitigating evidence regarding his long history of juvenile delinquency and drug abuse. The court held that, on its face, this claim failed to meet even the first part of the Strickland test and therefore showed no grounds for relief. The court further held that the remainder of appellant's points were not cognizable on collateral attack. The court denied appellant's application for stay of execution.


OUTCOME: Finding no error, the court affirmed the trial court's denial of appellant's motion for postconviction relief without an evidentiary hearing. The court also denied appellant's request for a stay of execution.

State v. Stacey


No. 66,447


Supreme Court of Florida


482 So. 2d 1350; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3926; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 563



October 17, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 7, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions, First District - Case No. BA-115.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent sought review from a judgment of the District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida) dismissing his pro se motion for postconviction relief, made pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. In his motion, respondent argued that the trial court erred in its retention of jurisdiction over the first third of respondent's sentence for armed robbery because the crime was committed prior to the effective date of Fla. Stat. ch. 947.16(3) (1978).


OVERVIEW: Respondent appealed from dismissal of his pro se motion for post-conviction relief, made pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. In his motion, respondent alleged that the trial court erred in retaining jurisdiction over the first third of his sentence because the crime for which he was convicted was committed before the effective date of Fla. Stat. ch. 947.16(3) (1978). On appeal, the court quashed the decision of the lower court and remanded the case for modification of the sentence. The court recognized that retroactive application of ch. 947.16(3) to a crime occurring before its effective date was an impermissible ex post facto law. However, the court held that the lower court erred in remanding for an evidentiary hearing to determine if the crime was committed prior to the effective date of ch. 947.16(3) because the trial court had already found that the conviction was entered prior to the statute's effective date. Because respondent received ineffective assistance of counsel, the court allowed him to raise the constitutionality of ch. 947.16(3) on appeal despite the fact that his counsel did not object to the application of ch. 947.16(3) at trial.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the lower court's order dismissing respondent's motion for post-conviction relief and held that the retroactive application of the statute in question to a crime occurring before the statute's effective date was an impermissible ex post facto law.

 

140 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Winfield v. Division of Pari-Mutuel Wagering, Dep't of Business Regulation


No. 64-793


Supreme Court of Florida


477 So. 2d 544; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3916; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 548



October 10, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance, Fourth District - Case No. 83-464.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners appealed decision from the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District (Florida) in an action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief from subpoenas duces tecum issued by respondents, Florida Department of Business Regulation and Division of Pari-Mutuel Wagering, to obtain petitioners' banking records without notice to petitioners of investigation. Petitioners alleged subpoenas violated their right to privacy and due process.


OVERVIEW: In an action by petitioners seeking declaratory and injunctive relief against subpoenas duces tecum issued by respondents, Florida Department of Business Regulation and Division of Pari-Mutuel Wagering, petitioners appealed decision permitting subpoenas. Respondents sought banking records of petitioners' bank accounts, giving no notice to petitioners and asking banks not to inform petitioners of their investigation. Petitioners alleged the subpoenas were invalid, they violated petitioners' constitutional right to privacy and due process, and maintenance of public records constituted an additional violation of their constitutional right to privacy. The court held that much of the responsibility of formulating privacy interests was given by the U.S. Supreme Court to the individual states. The right to personal privacy in Florida, under Fla. Const. art. I, § 23, was broader in scope than the federal Constitution. However, there was no complete immunity from governmental regulation and the right to privacy yielded to compelling governmental interests. The state's interest in conducting effective investigations in the pari-mutuel industry was a compelling state interest.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed for respondents, Florida Department of Business Regulation and Division of Pari-Mutuel Wagering. The court concluded that the Florida Constitution did not prevent respondents from subpoenaing a Florida citizen's bank records without notice. The right to privacy yielded to compelling governmental interests such as the state's interest in conducting effective investigations in the pari-mutuel industry.

 

141 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Alexander v. State


No. 65,666


Supreme Court of Florida


477 So. 2d 557; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3923; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 546



October 10, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity Fourth District - Case No. 83-317.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a decision of the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirming the trial court's denial of his motion to dismiss the charge of carrying a concealed weapon in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 790.25(5) (Supp. 1982). Petitioner also claimed that Fla. Stat. ch. 790.01(2) (1981), as refined in Fla. Stat. chs. 790.25(5) and 790.001(15), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged with carrying a concealed weapon in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 790.25(5) (Supp. 1982). The trial court denied petitioner's motion to dismiss, ruling that his pouch was not "securely encased" within the meaning of Fla. Stat. ch. 790.001(16) (Supp.1982). On appeal, petitioner claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motion and that Fla. Stat. ch. 790.01(2) (1981), as refined in Fla. Stat. chs. 790.25(5) and 790.001(15), was unconstitutional. The court explained that a statute was constitutional if it bore a reasonable relation to a permissible legislative objective and was not discriminatory, arbitrary, or capricious. The court explained that promoting firearms safety and crime prevention were permissible legislative objectives and that the prohibition against carrying a concealed weapon was reasonably related to those objectives. Further, the statutes were not void for vagueness. However, the court determined that petitioner's motion to dismiss should have been granted. Under the facts of the case, the court held that petitioner's pouch was a zippered gun case, and therefore his carrying of it in his automobile was not in violation of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the statutes at issue were constitutional because they were reasonably related to permissible legislative objectives. However, the court determined that petitioner's motion to dismiss should have been granted. Under the facts of the case, the court held that petitioner's pouch was a zippered gun case, and therefore his carrying of it in his automobile was not in violation of the statute.

State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co. v. Gant


No. 66,342


Supreme Court of Florida


478 So. 2d 25; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3788; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 532



September 26, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 27, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict. Second District - Case No. 83-1142.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a decision from the Second District Court of Appeals (Florida) which held that an amendment to Fla. Stat. ch. 627.4132 (Supp. 1980), effective October 1, 1980 permitted stacking of uninsured motorist coverage. On rehearing, the court certified to the supreme court a conflict with a decision in another district as to whether the stacking amendment could be applied retroactively.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner issued two automobile insurance liability contracts to the adult respondents. Both policies prohibited the stacking of the uninsured motorist coverage in said policies. While the policies were in effect, and nine days after an amendment to Fla. Stat. ch. 627.4132 (Supp. 1980), effective October 1, 1980 went into effect permitting an insured to stack uninsured motorist coverage, adult respondents' two children were struck by a tortfeasor's automobile. One child was killed and the other seriously injured. The tortfeasor had limited liability coverage in an amount lower than adult respondents' uninsured motorist coverage. Respondents brought a declaratory judgment action in which they sought to invoke the statute's provisions permitting an insured to stack uninsured motorist coverage. The trial court granted summary judgment in respondents' favor on that issue and the district court affirmed the decision but the supreme court reversed, holding that to apply the statute permitting stacking to policies containing anti-stacking provisions and in effect at the time at issue would violate the Florida constitutional provision prohibiting the impairment of contracts.


OUTCOME: The supreme court quashed the district court's decision permitting the stacking of uninsured motorist coverage in insurance policies which contained anti-stacking provisions and which were issued prior to the date of a statutory amendment permitting stacking. The court found that retroactive application of the statute would have been a violation of the constitutional provision prohibiting the impairment of contracts.

Echols v. State


No. 64,246


Supreme Court of Florida


484 So. 2d 568; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3775; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 526



September 19, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing September 30, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, William L. Walker, Judge - Case Nos. 82-8945 & 83-1638 CFANO.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction and sentences from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida) for one count each of first-degree murder, robbery with a firearm, and armed burglary with an assault.


OVERVIEW: Brother-in-law contacted appellant and hired him to murder victim. The motive for the murder was both personal antipathy and a desire to obtain control of the victim's estate. Appellant recounted details of the crimes and the scheme to a wired informer. Police found evidence corroborating appellant's trips and statements he had made on the tapes. Appellant's conviction and sentences for first-degree murder, robbery with a firearm, and armed burglary with an assault were affirmed. The state's interests were not served by excluding relevant evidence which was lawfully obtained in another state. Appellant had known for months that the state had two tapes purporting to contain inculpatory statements that he had made. The jury was capable of determining whether the voice on the tapes was the same. Nothing in the state's chief examiner's direct testimony offered an opening for the cross examination which appellant sought. Aggravating factors were not based on the same essential feature of the crime or of the offender's character. Nothing in the record warranted finding any truly mitigating significance in appellant's age.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentences because: 1) evidence was properly admitted; 2) the jury was properly instructed; 3) cross-examination was properly limited; and 4) the aggravating factors so clearly and convincingly outweighed the mitigating factors that no reasonable person could differ.

Cave v. State


No. 63,172


Supreme Court of Florida


476 So. 2d 180; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3684; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 481



August 30, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 21, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, L. B. Vocelle, Judge - Case No. CR8209546CFANO.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences from the Pinellas County Circuit Court (Florida) for first-degree murder, robbery with a firearm, and kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised 31 claims on an appeal regarding his convictions and sentences for first-degree murder, robbery, and kidnapping. The court reviewed all of them, but discussed only a few. The exclusion of two jurors was not an error, as their unequivocal opposition to the death penalty would not permit them to apply the law or view the facts impartially. Sufficient evidence supported a finding that defendant's confession was freely and voluntarily made. The trial court appropriately limited counsel's closing argument to exclude the claim that defendant would have had to personally kill the victim to be guilty of first-degree murder, because this was felony murder, where that was not so. A response to the jury about the reporting of a split decision during the penalty phase was properly given. When defense counsel argued that defendant was young and his participation in the crime was minor, the trial court properly left entirely to the jury to assign whatever weight it wished to defendant's age and character. The evidence supported the trial court's finding of the aggravating circumstance that the crime was heinous, atrocious, and cruel. The convictions and sentences were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for first-degree murder, robbery, and kidnapping and the sentences for them, because the record showed no error in support of his claims.

146 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Chase Fed. Sav. & Loan Ass'n v. Schreiber


No. 63,017


Supreme Court of Florida


479 So. 2d 90; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3697; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 470



August 30, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 2, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Third District - Case No. 80-1213.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mortgagee applied for review of the decision of the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida), which reversed the judgment of the trial court and held that respondent's deed and petitioner's mortgage should be cancelled because there was no valid consideration for the deed. The district court certified a question for review regarding what the proper scope of review for district courts of appeal in granting rehearings en banc was.


OVERVIEW: The grantor, an elderly lady, transferred title to her home to an unrelated grantee by a quitclaim deed, which showed on its face that the consideration was "love and affection." The grantee sold the property and those buyers mortgaged the property to petitioner mortgagee. Respondent, the personal representative of the grantor's estate, brought this action seeking cancellation of the deeds and mortgage. This court held that the deed was valid and effective to pass legal title although there was no valuable consideration paid and the grantor and grantee were not related. The constitutional law of homestead protection had been changed to eliminate the requirement of a valuable consideration as a condition of a conveyance of homestead property; therefore, there was no such limitation on the right to alienate by gift real property in general. On the certified question of the proper scope of review for district courts in granting rehearings en banc, the court held that the district courts were not limited by the case-law standards applied in the exercise of this court's discretionary conflict jurisdiction, but were free to develop their own concepts of decisional uniformity.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the lower court's decision and answered the certified question by holding that the district courts of appeal, in exercising their en banc power, were free to develop their own concepts of decisional uniformity. The court quashed the lower court's decision on the validity of respondent's deed and petitioner's mortgage because the deed was valid and effective to pass legal title even without valuable consideration.

Pullum v. Cincinnati, Inc.


No. 66,198


Supreme Court of Florida


476 So. 2d 657; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3686; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P10,690; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 428



August 29, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 4, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance - First District - Case No. AU-62.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida), certified the question as to whether Fla. Stat. ch. 95.031(2) (1979) denied equal protection of the laws to persons who were injured by products delivered to the original purchaser between eight and 12 years prior to the injury. That appellate court had previously affirmed a grant of summary judgment against petitioner on grounds that the statute at issue barred his defective product suit.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was injured while operating a press brake machine. Petitioner sued the manufacturer more than 12 years from the date of delivery of the machine to the original purchaser, but within the applicable four-year statute of limitations. The trial court granted summary judgment against petitioner on grounds that his action was barred by Fla. Stat. ch. 95.031(2) (1979), a statute of repose. The appellate court affirmed, and certified the question as to whether that statute denied equal protection of the laws to persons who were injured by products delivered to the original purchaser between eight and 12 years prior to the injury. The court receded from its own prior decision and held that § 95.031(2) did not violate equal protection. Instead, the court noted that the legislature in enacting that statute reasonably decided that perpetual liability placed an undue burden on manufacturers, and that 12 years from the date of sale was a reasonable time for exposure to liability for manufacturing a product. As such, the court held that the classification originally established by the statute bore a reasonable relationship to a proper state objective. The decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment against petitioner in his suit for injuries caused by defective product was affirmed. The court receded from its own prior decision and held that a statute of repose that barred petitioner's action did not violate petitioner's equal protection rights, because the classification established by the statute bore a reasonable relationship to a proper state objective of limiting perpetual liability of manufacturers.

 

149 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


N. Broward Hosp. Dist. v. Fornes


No. 66,115


Supreme Court of Florida


476 So. 2d 154; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3705; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 437



August 29, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 23, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fourth District - Case No. 83-947.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner special taxing district appealed an order of the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) reversing an order dismissing respondent taxpayer's case challenging petitioner's expenditure of public funds. A question of great public importance was certified as to the circumstances under which respondent acquired standing to sue to prevent petitioner's alleged illegal expenditure of public funds, which increased respondent's tax burden.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner special taxing district intended to expand a hospital. Respondent taxpayer sued to enjoin petitioner from proceeding with the expansion, arguing that petitioner did not contract for the lowest bid for the job and thereby prevented the expansion from being completed at the lowest cost to the taxpayers. The order dismissing respondent's suit was reversed on appeal on grounds that respondent had standing to sue to prevent illegal expenditure of public funds because she alleged that the expenditure would increase her tax burden. Petitioner appealed, and a question of great public importance was certified regarding the requirements for standing to challenge government expenditures. The court held that a mere increase in taxes did not confer standing on respondent to challenge petitioner's expenditure. Respondent had to suffer a special injury from petitioner's acts or had to allege that petitioner was acting unconstitutionally to obtain standing. Because respondent suffered no special injury and did not challenge the constitutionality of petitioner's actions, the court quashed the appellate decision.


OUTCOME: The order reversing the order dismissing respondent taxpayer's case was quashed, because a mere increase in taxes did not confer standing on respondent to challenge petitioner special taxing district's expenditures and respondent did not suffer a special injury or challenge the constitutionality of petitioner's actions.

Peede v. State


No. 65,318


Supreme Court of Florida


474 So. 2d 808; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3667; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 397



August 15, 1985

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Michael F. Cycmanick, Judge - Case No. CR83-1682.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioned for review of his conviction and sentence of death by the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida) for the first-degree murder of his estranged wife, contending that the trial court reversibly erred in excusing him, at his request, from attending portions of the guilt phase of his trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder and was sentenced to death. Appellant challenged his conviction and sentence, contending that the trial court reversibly erred in excusing him from attending portions of his trial, at his request, after the start of the trial. Appellant argued that the court committed reversible error in allowing the victim's daughter to testify about the victim's statements and state of mind before the murder. The court affirmed appellant's conviction and death sentence, holding that defendant was entitled to waive his right to be present at stages of his capital trial where he personally chose to do so. The court also found that appellant failed to demonstrate that he made an unequivocal, voluntary, and intelligent election to represent himself and discharge his trial counsel. The court held that the victim's statements to her daughter were properly admitted under the hearsay exception to show the declarant's state of mind, which was relevant to the kidnapping charge that formed the basis for the state's felony murder theory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and death sentence for murder, holding that appellant's due process rights were not violated when he was allowed to voluntarily be absent from stages of his trial. The court also found that appellant failed to demonstrate that he elected to represent himself and discharge his trial counsel. The court held that the victim's statements were properly admitted to show the victim's state of mind.

Belvedere Dev. Corp. v. Department of Transp., Div. of Admin.


No. 62,172


Supreme Court of Florida


476 So. 2d 649; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3484; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 375



July 11, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 4, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fourth District - Case No. 79-2306.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a development corporation, sought review of a decision of the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) that upheld a jury award that compensated petitioners for land taken from them by respondent department of transportation but failed to compensate them for the riparian rights attached to the land.


OVERVIEW: Respondent, the state department of transportation, exercised eminent domain and took portions of petitioners' land adjacent to a lake. Respondent reserved to petitioners the right to use and enjoy the riparian rights pertaining to the land taken and therefore did not compensate petitioners for those rights. The trial court awarded compensation for the land on that basis. Petitioners sought review and the appellate court affirmed and certified the question regarding the riparian rights to the state supreme court. Upon review, the court concluded that the act of condemning petitioners' lands without compensating them for their riparian property rights was an unconstitutional taking. The court held that riparian rights were property rights that could be separated from the upland by bilateral agreement in a deed of conveyance. The court held that all or any interest in riparian rights could be transferred by voluntary act of the upland owner but that riparian rights could not be severed by condemnation proceedings without the consent of the upland owner. The court therefore quashed the decision below and remanded so that petitioners could be compensated for the riparian rights.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the decision below and remanded the case for the purpose of determining the just compensation due petitioners for riparian rights and severance damages after holding that riparian rights could not be severed by condemnation proceedings without the consent of the upland owner.

 

152 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Campus Communications, Inc. v. Department of Revenue


No. 65786


Supreme Court of Florida


473 So. 2d 1290; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3480; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 371



July 11, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 5, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance, First District - Case No. AW-352.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified a question to the court to determine whether Fla. Admin. Code Ann. 12A-1.08, which required taxation of all publications that were not sold but given away, was unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff college newspaper.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought to compel plaintiff newspaper to pay sales taxes for the cost of printing. Plaintiff was a not-for-profit corporation that distributed free newspapers. The trial court granted plaintiff's motion for summary judgment. The intermediate appellate court certified the question of whether Fla. Admin. Code Ann. r. 12A-1.08, which required taxation of all publications that were not sold but given away, was unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff college newspaper. The court found that Fla. Admin. Code Ann. r. 12A-1.08 was void as an invalid exercise of delegated legislative authority insofar as it denied exemption from taxation to a free distribution newspaper. Fla. Stat. Ann. § 212.005 (1983) allowed the state to tax each transaction that involved tangible personal property. The statutory scheme provided that newspapers were exempt from sales tax, thus because plaintiff failed to meet the administrative definition of newspaper, it was not exempt. The court held that imposition of the taxes provided an outcome inconsistent with the legislative intent. Because the primary purpose of the paper was to disseminate news, the court found plaintiff was exempt.


OUTCOME: The court found that plaintiff college newspaper was exempt from taxation on the cost of printing, because even though it did not meet the administrative definition of newspaper, such taxation provided an outcome inconsistent with the legislative intent.

Wright v. State


No. 64391


Supreme Court of Florida


473 So. 2d 1277; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3479; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 364



July 3, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 30, 1985.
Writ of certiorari denied Wright v. Florida, 474 U.S. 1094, 106 S. Ct. 870, 88 L. Ed. 2d 909, 1986 U.S. LEXIS 1175 (1986)
Post-conviction relief denied at Wright v. State, 581 So. 2d 882, 1991 Fla. LEXIS 795 (Fla., 1991)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Putnam County. Robert R. Perry, Judge. (Case No. 83-376CF-M).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Prisoner appealed his conviction of first-degree murder, sexual battery, burglary of a dwelling, and second-degree grand theft from the Circuit Court in and for Putnam County (Florida).


OVERVIEW: Prisoner was convicted of first-degree murder, sexual battery, burglary of a dwelling, and second-degree grand theft. Prisoner contended that it was reversible error for the trial court to have denied the proffered witness an opportunity to testify. The court held that the trial court erred when it failed to exercise its discretion to have determined whether exclusion was warranted under the circumstances, and, instead, applied the sequestration rule as a strict rule of law. However, the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt because the excluded evidence would not have affected the verdict. Prisoner argued that the trial court committed reversible error when it allowed the jury to have considered evidence of a prior crime committed by prisoner. The court held that the evidence that prisoner had previously burglarized the victim's house and, in so doing, had utilized the identical point of entry used on the date of the victim's murder, was, under the Williams rule, legally relevant to show identity and to show that prisoner knew that point of entry was available. The conviction and sentence were affirmed.


OUTCOME: Prisoner's conviction for first-degree murder, sexual battery, burglary of a dwelling and second-degree grand theft was affirmed. The trial court's application of the sequestration rule as a strict rule of law was harmless error.

Department of Transp. v. Durden


No. 66,770


Supreme Court of Florida


471 So. 2d 1271; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3485; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 317



June 20, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reported at: 471 So.2d 1271 at 1271.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of May 10, 1985, Reported at: 471 So.2d 1271. Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Leon County, William L. Gary, Judge, Case No. 84-3528 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. BF-153.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant department of transportation sought review of a decision of the Trial Court, in and for Leon County (Florida), entering judgment for appellees in an action challenging the validity of Fla. Stat. Ann. § 479.105, which allowed removal of illegal advertising signs prior to an administrative hearing. Appellant asserted that Fla. Stat. Ann. § 479.105 was valid under the due process clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and Fla. Const. art. I, § 9.


OVERVIEW: Appellees business and individuals illegally constructed outdoor advertising signs without first obtaining permits required by Fla. Stat. Ann. § 479.07. Appellant department of transportation notified appellees that the signs were in an unpermitted zone and constructed without a permit, in violation of Fla. Stat. Ann. §§ 479.11(1) and 479.07(1). Appellees requested a hearing. Appellant posted the sign faces with a notice of removal. Appellees filed a complaint in circuit court challenging the validity of Fla. Stat. Ann. § 479.105, which allowed removal of illegal advertising signs. The trial court held that Fla. Stat. Ann. § 479.105(1) and (3) violated the due process clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and Fla. Ann. § 479.105(1) and (3) was constitutional both on its face and as applied to appellees because appellees did not have a protectible property interest when the government sought to remove an unlawful outdoor advertising sign erected in disregard of established procedure for securing a permit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed judgment in favor of appellant department of transportation in an action filed by appellees business and individuals challenging the constitutionality of a state statute allowing removal of illegal outdoor advertising signs prior to an administrative hearing. The court held that the state statute was constitutional because appellees did not have a protectible property interest in illegal outdoor signs erected without a permit.

XIV because Fla. 156 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Barclay v. State


No. 64,765


Supreme Court of Florida


470 So. 2d 691; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3418; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 299



May 30, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Hudson Olliff, Judge - Case No. 74-4139 Division: S.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida), which convicted him, upon a jury verdict, of one count of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death, notwithstanding a jury recommendation of a sentence of life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of one count of first-degree murder, and jury recommended a life sentence. The trial court, however, concluded that aggravating factors existed and, therefore, imposed a sentence of death. Appellant argued that the victim's stepfather was improperly permitted to testify as to the deceased's identity. The court agreed with appellant but found that because appellant had failed to make a contemporaneous specific objection to the testimony, the matter was not preserved for appellate review. The court affirmed the conviction but vacated the sentence, holding that the facts did not support finding an aggravating factor. The trial court also erred in finding that a prior conviction of a violent felony was more of an aggravating than a negative factor. The finding suffered from two defects: the information regarding appellant's prior conviction for breaking and entering came solely from a presentence investigation, and the state did not prove this factor beyond a reasonable doubt. Moreover, the court concluded that a conviction of breaking and entering did not, on its face, prove a prior conviction of a violent felony.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court, which convicted appellant of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death, was affirmed. However, the death sentence was vacated with directions that appellant was to be sentenced to life imprisonment with no eligibility for parole for twenty-five years. The trial court erred when it concluded that there existed aggravating factors for which the jury's recommendation should be trumped.

Florida Patient's Compensation Fund v. Von Stetina

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal and Cross-Appeal, Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity, and a Notice and Cross-Notice for Review, Statutory Validity and Direct Conflict, of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District - Case Nos. 82-1332, 82-1341, 82-1597, 82-1686, 82-1992, 82-1993, 82-2070 and 82-2078.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital and patient's compensation fund challenged a decision from the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida), that affirmed a $ 12.47 million medical malpractice verdict and held unconstitutional Fla. Stat. ch. 768.54(2)(b), 768.54(3)(e)3, and 768.51(1981), which related to hospital liability limitation and the method to be used by appellant fund in paying final judgments.

Appellant fund contended that an appellate court must apply the most recent version of the statute when it is the law in effect at the time of the appellate court's final decision. The court found the article irrelevant, and thus inadmissible. The admission was not harmless error. The court vacated the judgment and granted a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the district court holding the subject statutes unconstitutional, and remanded the case for a new trial. The admission into evidence of an article utilized as part of the training materials for intensive care unit nurses was not harmless error.

Trawick v. State


No. 57077


Supreme Court of Florida


473 So. 2d 1235; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3244; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 281



May 16, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 5, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: An appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Wilkie D. Ferguson, Jr., Judge - Case No. 79-355A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), of first-degree murder and other offenses in which the lower court imposed a sentence of death, appellant's convictions having been entered pursuant to pleas of guilty.


OVERVIEW: Following appellant's convictions of first-degree murder and other offenses entered pursuant to appellant's pleas of guilty, the trial court imposed a sentence of death. On appeal, appellant contended that the evidence before the court at the hearing on appellant's plea was such as should have raised a question as to appellant's competency to enter pleas of guilty. The court found appellant's despondency and his ambivalence about his plea did not constitute reasonable grounds to believe he might be incompetent. The mere suggestion of the possibility that the accused was contemplating suicide did not as a matter of law raise a sufficient reasonable ground to believe he was incompetent. The court found no error in the fact that the trial court did not conduct a competency hearing on its own motion. Turning to the sentence of death, the court found merit in the argument that the sentence of death was tainted by the consideration by judge and jury of improper aggravating circumstances. The trial judge went beyond the proper use of statutory aggravating circumstances in his sentencing findings and the sentence of death could not stand. Appellant was entitled to a new sentencing trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for first-degree murder and the other crimes. The court reversed the sentence of death and remanded the case for a new sentencing proceeding before a jury empanelled for that purpose because the jury heard evidence and argument that did not properly relate to any statutory aggravating circumstance, thus the jury recommendation was tainted.

Acosta v. Kraco, Inc.


No. 65,214


Supreme Court of Florida


471 So. 2d 24; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3243; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 267



May 9, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 11, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance - First District - Case No. AT-7.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a judgment of the District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida), which held that Fla. Stat. Ann. § 440.15 (3)(b)3.d did not violate the Supremacy Clause of the United States Constitution because it did not conflict with 42 U.S.C.S. § 403 (f)(3).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued that Fla. Stat. Ann. § 440.15 (3)(b)3.d, which permitted social security recipients between the ages of 65 and 70 to receive full benefits provided the recipient's earned income did not reach a maximum level, violated the Supremacy Clause of the United States Constitution by conflicting with 42 U.S.C.S. § 403 (f)(3). The trial court held in favor of respondents, finding that § 440.15 (3)(b) 3.d was not unconstitutional, and petitioner appealed. The court ruled that § 440.15 (3)(b)3.d. did not deny access to the courts or unconstitutionally discriminate on the basis of age. Further, the court held that § 440.15 (3)(b)3.d. was rationally related to the legitimate state objectives of reducing fringe benefits to reflect productivity declines associated with age, inducing older workers to retire and thereby allow younger workers to advance, and reducing workers' compensation premiums. The court affirmed the judgment, concluding that the valid purposes of § 440.15 (3)(b)3.d. did not conflict with the salutary purposes underlying § 403 (f)(3).


OUTCOME: Judgment in favor of respondents was affirmed where the Supremacy Clause of the Federal Constitution was not violated by a state statute because the statute was rationally related to the legitimate state objectives of reducing fringe benefits to reflect productivity declines associated with age, inducing older workers to retire and thereby allow younger workers to advance, and reducing workers' compensation premiums.

Florida Patient's Compensation Fund v. Rowe


No. 64,459


Supreme Court of Florida


472 So. 2d 1145; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3238; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 249



May 2, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Filed May 16, 1985; Rehearing Denied August 16, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Direct Appeal on Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Lee County, James R. Thompson, Judge, Case No. 81-1045CA-JRT - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, Second District, Case No. 83-2065.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant fund sought review of a decision of the trial court, Lee County (Florida), which held that Fla. Stat. ch. 768.56 (1981), which directed the trial court to award a reasonable attorney fee to the prevailing party in a medical malpractice action, was constitutional, but expressed concern regarding the appropriate method for computing reasonable attorney fees pursuant to the statute.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was the prevailing party in a medical malpractice action and appellant fund was responsible for payment of the portion of the judgment that exceeded the primary coverage. The trial court found Fla. Stat. ch. 768.56 (1981), providing for the payment of attorney fees in medical malpractice, constitutional, but expressed concern as to the computation of the fees. The court affirmed and adopted the federal lodestar approach for computing reasonable attorney fees. Requiring an unsuccessful litigant to pay the prevailing party's attorney fees did not constitute a penalty offensive to the system of justice. The award of attorney fees to the prevailing party was a matter of substantive law properly under the aegis of the legislature. The attorney fee applicant was to present adequate records detailing the work performed. In determining a reasonable hourly rate the court was to take into account certain factors in Fla. Bar. Code Prof. Resp. DR 2-106. The number of hours reasonably expended multiplied by a reasonable hourly rate produced the lodestar, to which a contingency risk multiplier ranging from 1.5 to 3 could be added or subtracted.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court finding a statute permitting the award of attorney fees constitutional in medical malpractice cases was affirmed. The legislature had the power to tax fees as costs and such fees did not constitute a penalty. In determining a reasonable fee amount, the courts were to use the federal lodestar approach.

Hess v. Metropolitan Dade County


No. 64,586


Supreme Court of Florida


467 So. 2d 297; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 2963; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 193



April 4, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions Third District - Case No. 83-2061.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a minor and her parents, sought review of a judgment of the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida), which held that it was precluded from issuing a writ of mandamus challenging the constitutionality of legislation providing that respondent county compensate petitioners for the unpaid balance awarded them in a personal injury action against respondent.


OVERVIEW: The court observed that the trial court ruling, barring it from issuing a writ of mandamus challenging the constitutionality of legislation, conflicted with a ruling in a separate case. In response, the court ruled that Fla. Const. art. V, § 4(b)(3) permitted the trial court to issue writs of mandamus so as to address the merits of a controversy. The court then noted that respondent county, pursuant to Fla. Stat. Ann. § 768.28(5), an immunity statute, paid petitioners, a minor and her parents, only a portion of a negligence judgment awarded to them, the cap permitted, and thereafter challenged the constitutionality of enacted legislation--Fla. Stat. ch. 83-393--directing the payment of the unpaid balance. Holding the act to be constitutional, the court said that waiver of sovereign immunity could only be dealt with by general law of the state legislature and that respondent could not provide for waiver of its sovereign immunity in its home rule charter. Sovereign immunity must be applied uniformly to all governmental entities. Furthermore, respondent could not invoke the cap and then ignore the statutory proviso authorizing recovery of amounts over the cap, when legislated.


OUTCOME: The trial court judgment barring the issuance of a writ of mandamus, which challenged the constitutionality of legislation providing that respondent county compensate petitioners for the unpaid balance awarded in a personal injury action, was quashed; mandamus was an appropriate remedy because the act authorizing payment of balance was constitutional, and an immunity statute that set the cap allowed for payment when legislatively authorized.

Everton v. Willard


No. 63,440


Supreme Court of Florida


468 So. 2d 936; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 2964; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 201



April 4, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 22, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions Second District - Case Nos. 81-2081 and 81-2085.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners applied for review of a decision of the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida), which held than a police officer's decision to make or not make an arrest was under discretionary authority and was covered by basic governmental sovereign immunity that precluded liability.


OVERVIEW: The complaint alleged that the sheriff's deputy had negligently violated a duty to petitioners by allowing a drunk driver to drive subsequent to issuing him a traffic citation and that the violation of this duty resulted in an accident that caused petitioners' injuries. The trial court dismissed the complaint for failure to state a cause of action. In so doing, the court held that a law enforcement officer must have the discretion to enforce the law without being subject to tort liability for injuries to innocent third parties. On appeal, the issue was whether a law enforcement officer's discretionary police authority to make or not make an arrest constituted a basic judgmental or decision making function that was immune from tort liability. The court found that the decision of whether to enforce the law by making an arrest was a basic judgmental or discretionary governmental function that was immune from suit, and approved the decision of the lower court dismissing the complaint. The court reasoned that the decision was a basic discretionary, judgmental decision that was inherent in enforcing the laws of the state.


OUTCOME: The decision of the district court dismissing the complaint for failure to state a cause of action was approved because the decision of whether to enforce the law by making an arrest was a basic judgmental or discretionary governmental function that is immune from suit.

State v. Jenkins


No. 65,810


Supreme Court of Florida


469 So. 2d 733; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 2968; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 188



April 4, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 17, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal, First District, Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity Case No. AV-420.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged the dismissal of appellee county prosecutor's indictment for official misconduct by the District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida), on the ground that Fla. Stat. ch. 839.25(1)(a) (1983) was unconstitutional because it was vague and subject to arbitrary and capricious application.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state sought review of the conclusion of the lower court that appellee county property appraiser's indictment for official misconduct, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 839.25(1)(a) (1983), should be dismissed on the ground that it was unconstitutional because it was vague and subject to arbitrary and capricious application. On appeal, dismissal of the indictment was affirmed. In support of its ruling, the court held that ch. 839.25(1)(a), which defined official misconduct as knowingly refraining, or causing another to refrain from performing a duty imposed upon him by law, impermissibly allowed the imposition of criminal sanctions for the failure to perform duties imposed by statutes, rules, or regulations that may themselves impose either a lesser penalty or no penalty at all. The court further held that because agency rules had the effect of law, any violation of any agency rule could be grounds for imposition of criminal sanctions under ch. 839.25(1)(a). Hence, the court found that ch. 839.25(1)(a) was unconstitutionally vague and susceptible to arbitrary application.


OUTCOME: Dismissal of the indictment was affirmed as the statute in question impermissibly allowed the imposition of criminal sanctions for the failure to perform duties imposed by statutes, rules, or regulations that may themselves have imposed either a lesser penalty or no penalty at all.
