Trianon Park Condo. Ass'n v. City of Hialeah


No. 63,115


Supreme Court of Florida


468 So. 2d 912; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 2962; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 210



April 4, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 22, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Third District - Case Nos. 81-1626 and 81-1634.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Third District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified the question whether under Fla. Stat. ch. 768.28 (1975) a city had sovereign immunity from a suit basing liability solely upon an allegedly negligent inspection of a building where the city had no part in the building's construction. The district court held that respondent city was liable to petitioner condominium owners for damage resulting from negligent inspections by city inspectors.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner condominium association sued respondent city for the negligent inspections by its city inspectors during the construction of petitioner's condominiums. After being held liable at the district court level, the case was certified as a matter of great public importance. The court restated the certified question as whether a governmental entity may be liable in tort to individual property owners for the negligent actions of its building inspectors in enforcing provisions of a building code enacted pursuant to police power vested in that governmental entity. The court went through a thorough evaluation of governmental liability, specifically focusing on discretionary acts, and held that governments had to be free to enact and enforce laws without creating new duties and corresponding liabilities. The court further held that the government had no responsibility to protect personal property interests or ensure the quality of buildings that individuals erect or purchase. The court found that the proper remedy for faulty construction lay in an action against the contractor, developer, or seller. The court quashed the decision of the district court and held for respondent city.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question, as restated, in the negative and quashed the decision of the district court because the city had no responsibility to ensure the quality of buildings that individuals purchased or erected.

 

165 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


No. 64,618


Supreme Court of Florida


465 So. 2d 1229; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3097; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 172



March 14, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Constitutional Construction; First District - Case No. AR-162.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This case came before the court upon application for review of a decision of the District Court of Appeal (Florida), which reversed the trial court's denial of defendant's challenge for cause regarding two jurors, correctional officers, that defendant claimed could not be impartial because the victim in the case was a corrections officer and the defendant was an inmate.


OVERVIEW: Defendant inmate was charged and convicted for battery of a correctional officer. The trial judge had denied defendant's challenge for cause regarding two jurors based upon the fact that they were corrections officers, but the district court reversed. Upon review, the court quashed the district court's ruling. It also disapproved Irby v. State, 436 So.2d 1047 (Fla. 1st DCA 1983), upon which the district court had relied in its ruling, and which held that the fact that the challenged juror was employed in the same position as the victim of the crime created both an appearance and a substantial probability of inherent juror bias. The court held that the test for determining juror competency was whether the juror could lay aside any bias or prejudice and render his verdict solely upon the evidence presented and the instructions on the law given to him by the court. Since the trial judge was best equipped to make this determination, his or her error would not be disturbed unless error was manifest.


OUTCOME: The district court's decision was quashed because no error was present on the part of the trial judge in refusing to deny the challenges for cause regarding the corrections officers serving as jurors.

O'Neil v. Department of Transp.


No. 64,809


Supreme Court of Florida


468 So. 2d 904; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3224; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 157



March 7, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 4, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. First District - Case No. AI-270.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a decision from the District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida), which affirmed the deputy commissioner's decision that Fla. Stat. Ann. § 440.15 precluded petitioner's recovery of wage loss benefits because petitioner was over age 65 and was eligible to receive social security benefits and his decision that the statute was not unconstitutional under the supremacy clause as violative of 29 U.S.C.S. § 623.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner filed a workers' compensation claim for permanent total disability benefits or, in the alternative, for wage loss benefits due to work related injuries. However, she was denied permanent total disability benefits when the deputy commissioner found no competent or substantial evidence of petitioner's inability to return to work. The commissioner also found that Fla. Stat. Ann. § 440.15 precluded recovery of wage loss benefits because petitioner was over age 65 and was eligible to receive social security benefits. The commissioner's order was then affirmed, and it was held that Fla. Stat. Ann. § 440.15(3)(b) 3, was not unconstitutional under the supremacy clause as violative of 29 U.S.C.S. § 623, the Age Discrimination in Employment Act. On appeal of that decision, the court agreed that Fla. Stat. Ann. § 440.15(3)(b)3.d. (1979) did not violate the supremacy clause and did not conflict with the Federal Age Discrimination in Employment Act, 29 U.S.C.S. § 621, since the provisions of Florida's Workers' Compensation Law did not constitute compensation, terms, conditions, or privileges of employment within the meaning of 29 U.S.C.S. § 623. The decision was thereby approved.


OUTCOME: Decision which affirmed the deputy commissioner's decision that petitioner was statutorily precluded from recovering wage loss benefits because petitioner was over age 65 and was eligible to receive social security benefits and the decision that the statute was not unconstitutional under the supremacy clause as violative of the Federal Age Discrimination in Employment Act was approved as proper.

Middleton v. State


Nos. 66,629, 66,632


Supreme Court of Florida


465 So. 2d 1218; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 4008; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 149



March 4, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, David Bruce Levy, Judge - Case No. 80-3289 And An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state prisoner sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), which denied his motion, filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, to vacate his first-degree murder conviction and death sentence. Defendant also filed petitions for a writ of habeas corpus and a stay of execution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and was sentenced to death. In defendant's motion to vacate his sentence and conviction, he argued that he was denied ineffective assistance of counsel at trial and that the trial court erred in denying his motion without an evidentiary hearing. The court determined that the witnesses' testimony that counsel failed to present was clearly to defendant's disadvantage. Similarly, the court found that the psychological evidence that counsel did not present as mitigating factors during the penalty phase was inconsistent with the theory of defense. The court thought that the trial court properly disposed of defendant's motion to vacate without an evidentiary hearing. In defendant's habeas petition, he argued that he was denied the right to a direct appeal due to ineffective assistance of appellate counsel. For each item that defendant raised, the court concluded that he either failed to demonstrate prejudice or to demonstrate that appellate counsel's performance was deficient. The judgment of the lower court was affirmed, and the petitions for a writ of habeas corpus and a stay of execution were denied.


OUTCOME: Judgment that denied defendant state prisoner's motion to vacate his first-degree murder conviction and death sentence was affirmed. The court denied defendant's petitions for a writ of habeas corpus and a stay of execution. In deciding the appeal of the motion to vacate and the petition for habeas corpus, the court rejected defendant's claims of ineffective assistance of both trial and appellate counsel.

Livings v. Davis


No. 63001


Supreme Court of Florida


465 So. 2d 507; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3168; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 129



February 21, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 12, 1985.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, state department of marine patrol and state department of natural resources, sought review of an order from the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida) that dismissed the charges against respondent fishermen for taking small shrimp and prawn from state waters in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 370.15(2)(a) (1979).


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, state department of marine patrol and state department of natural resources, challenged an order dismissing the charges against respondent fishermen for taking small shrimp and prawn from state waters in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 370.15(2)(a) (1979). The lower court dismissed the charges against respondents on the ground that the state statute under which they were charged was unconstitutional because it conflicted with the Magnuson Fishery and Conservation Management Act (Act), 16 U.S.C.S. § 1801 (1976). The court reversed and remanded and found that there was nothing in the Act that curtailed the state's extraterritorial jurisdiction over its registered vessels. The court further found that because the state statute under which respondents were charged did not conflict with any existing federal regulation, the state was not precluded from enforcing its penal statute relative to the taking or possession of small shrimp or prawn within or without the waters of the state. Finally, the court found that the Act made no attempt to preempt the field, but, in fact, recognized continued state jurisdiction over vessels registered under the laws of the various states.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the charges against respondent fishermen for taking small shrimp and prawn from state waters was reversed and remanded because the state statute under which respondents were charged was not in conflict with the Magnuson Fishery and Conservation Management Act (Act). The court found that the Act made no attempt to preempt the field.

In re Estate of Gainer


No. 64,874


Supreme Court of Florida


466 So. 2d 1055; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3206; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 116



February 14, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 1, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal, Fifth District, Statutory Invalidity Case No. 83-498.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant personal representative challenged a decision from the Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida), which reversed the trial court and held that Fla. Stat. ch. 665.063(1)(a) (1981), was unconstitutional under the equal protection clauses of the state and federal constitutions. The personal representative and appellee sisters, all daughters of the decedent, disputed the personal representative's right to savings account funds.


OVERVIEW: The decedent had joint accounts, with the personal representative as survivor, but the funds were excluded from the estate's inventories. The sisters objected, contending that the personal representative could not get the money because the account was only in case the decedent needed help. The trial court held that the state bank funds were estate assets, finding that the decedent's intent was to facilitate dispersal, but intent was immaterial to the federal savings funds because, absent fraud or undue influence, title vested in the survivor, and it found the statutes constitutional. However, the appellate court determined that the sisters were testamentary beneficiaries and received disparate treatment based on the asset's location, finding ch. 665.063(1)(a) unconstitutional. On review, the court asserted that vesting applied, in the absence of fraud, to joint accounts at federal associations and that the sisters were not testamentary beneficiaries. The court found it reasonable to treat accounts governed by the Florida Savings Association Act differently from those governed by the Florida Banking Code and that ch. 665.063(1)(a) was constitutional, reversing the appellate court.


OUTCOME: The court held that the challenged statute was constitutional and reversed the district court's decision holding it invalid. The court held that the conclusive presumption applied to all monies deposited in the savings and loan joint account and that the personal representative was entitled to those assets. The cause was remanded for further proceedings.

Golden Nugget Group v. Metropolitan Dade County


No. 65,324


Supreme Court of Florida


464 So. 2d 535; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 2932; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 113



February 8, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity, Third District - Case No. 83-2799.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner hotel owners sought review of the judgment of the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida), which declared valid Fla. Stat. ch. 212.057, allowing implementation of a hotel "bed tax," but struck down a portion of a respondent county's municipal ordinance allowing for its collection.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner hotel owners challenged the validity of a state law and municipal ordinance providing for the imposition and assessment of a "bed tax" in respondent county. Petitioners contended the state law failed to publish independent tax collection mechanisms and violated equal protection guarantees. Upholding the lower appellate court's finding that the law was valid, the court approved of reasoning that an analogous section of state law provided for collection of the tax. The court also noted that the state legislature corrected any ambiguity regarding collection of the tax subsequent to commencement of the case by explicitly including collection and distribution procedures. Additionally, the court rejected the due process and equal protection challenges to the state law, reasoning that language identical to that in the statute at issue had been declared constitutionally valid in an analogous case. The court also upheld the lower appellate court's decision invalidating the municipal collection ordinance because it purported to authorize collection of the tax by respondent county's tax collector.


OUTCOME: The judgment declaring valid a state law allowing for imposition of a bed tax, while finding the municipal ordinance allowing for the collection of the tax invalid, was affirmed because the municipal ordinance improperly allowed for respondent county's tax agency to collect the tax.

Lake Worth Utilities Authority v. Lake Worth


No. 66,102


Supreme Court of Florida


468 So. 2d 215; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3205; 10 Fla. L. Weekly S 104; 10 Fla. L. Weekly S 297

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified the question of whether Fla. Stat. ch. 69-1215 was unconstitutional under Fla. Const. art. VIII, § 2b as one of great public importance requiring immediate resolution.


OVERVIEW: Appellant utility authority was created by Fla. Stat. ch. 69-1215 (1969) (chapter 69-1215), a special law adopted by referendum. Appellee city subsequently dissolved appellant authority by ordinance and sued, inter alia, appellant authority. Appellant authority filed a counter-complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief, contending that appellee city exceeded its power in passing the ordinance. Appellee moved to dismiss, asserting that the Municipal Home Rule Powers Act, Fla. The lower appellate court certified the question of whether chapter 69-1215 was unconstitutional as one of great public importance. The court reversed the trial court's order. The enactment of chapter 69-1215 was a constitutional exercise of power specifically reserved to the legislature in Fla. Const. Art VIII, § 2(b).

172 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bussey


Nos. 64,966, 64,967, 64,968


Supreme Court of Florida


463 So. 2d 1141; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 4006; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 105



February 7, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Three Consolidated Appeals from the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District - Statutory Invalidity. Case Nos. 82-2145, 83-629 & 83-141.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged orders from the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District (Florida), in which the court entered judgment finding Fla. Stat. ch. 817.563, which made it unlawful to offer to sell an illegal controlled substance to a person and then substitute another substance, unconstitutional. Three cases were consolidated for appeal.


OVERVIEW: The judgment finding Fla. Stat. ch. 817.563 was unconstitutional was reversed. In reversing the lower court's judgment, the supreme court held that the statute was not vague and that it served a legitimate government purpose. According to the supreme court, when interpreting a statute established principles of statutory construction must be utilized. The supreme court determined that the legislative intent behind section 817.563 was not to create a fraud statute. The supreme court held that section 817.563 was not designed to protect illegal drug users and dealers from fraudulent representations by other dealers. The supreme court then held that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague, as it required a general intent and not specific intent. Next, the supreme court held that in the absence of an impingement upon constitutional rights, an act of the legislature was presumed to be constitutional. The supreme court held that the burden was on the challenger to demonstrate that the law did not bear a reasonable relationship to a proper state objective. The supreme court found that the law did serve a legitimate interest of public safety and was valid.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the judgment finding the counterfeit controlled substance statute unconstitutional because the legislative intent behind the statute was not to protect drug users or dealers from fraudulent representations by others, but rather to prevent drug abuse. As such, only general intent was required under the statute.

 

173 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Boedy v. Department of Professional Regulation


No. 64,870


Supreme Court of Florida


463 So. 2d 215; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3200; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 90



January 31, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance; First District - Case No. AR-471.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner physician challenged an order from the District Court of Appeal (Florida), in which the court held that petitioner's U.S. Const. amend. V self-incrimination right was not applicable in administrative proceedings initiated under Fla. Stat. ch. 458.331(1)(s).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner physician objected to the lower court's finding that he was required to submit to a mental or emotional evaluation to retain his license. On appeal, petitioner physician argued that his U.S. Const. amend. V self-incrimination right was violated. The supreme court rejected petitioner physician's assertion. According to the supreme court, the right of a properly qualified and licensed individual to practice medicine was a valuable property right which must be protected under the constitution and laws of Florida. The supreme court held, however, that the right was not absolute but was subject to regulation under the police power of the state. The supreme court held that when there was a conflict it followed that the rights of the physician must yield to the power of the state to prescribe reasonable rules and regulations which protect the people from incompetent and unfit practitioners. The supreme court further held that Fla. Stat. ch. 458.331(1)(s) did not deal with guilt or innocent and was not penal. As such the Fifth Amendment right did not apply to proceedings initiated under the section.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment holding that petitioner physician's Fifth Amendment right was not applicable to an administrative proceeding because the state had a substantial interest in protecting its citizens from unfit practitioners.

 

174 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Roche v. State


No. 65,022


Supreme Court of Florida


462 So. 2d 1096; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 2892; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 72



January 24, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance First District - Case No. ZZ-346.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner convicted of drug trafficking appealed the denial of his petition for rehearing from the First District Court of Appeal (Florida). Petitioner contended that the lower court had erred when it denied his motion to suppress because the statute under which the search warrant was procured, Fla. Stat. ch. 570.15 (1980), had been declared unconstitutional by a United States district court decision.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was stopped at an agricultural inspection site. An inspector discovered a locked compartment in the vehicle, which petitioner refused to open. A regulatory search warrant was procured and upon opening of the compartment 500 pounds of marijuana was found. Petitioner was convicted of trafficking. Petitioner contended that Fla. Stat. ch. 570.15 violated U.S. Const. amend. IV because it allowed administrative searches without a showing of probable cause and without an administrative plan that contained specific neutral criteria. The court noted that a United States district court decision had held that the statute was unconstitutional because, once a legitimate stop occurred, the decision to inspect further had to have been supported by probable cause based on reasonable standards or neutral criteria. The court stated that the statute authorized searches based on an administrative plan that contained specific neutral criteria. The court also stated that all vehicles within the specified statutory class were subject to a search, and the probable cause that attached to the class supported the search. The court held that the statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: Denial of petitioner's motion for rehearing was affirmed. The court held that the statute under which petitioner was stopped and his vehicle was searched was constitutional; therefore, the lower court did not err when it affirmed the trial court's denial of the motion to suppress the contraband.

Division of Pari-Mutuel Wagering, Dep't of Business Regulation v. Florida Horse Council, Inc.


No. 65,820


Supreme Court of Florida


464 So. 2d 128; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 2893; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 68



January 24, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 15, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Dade County, David L. Levy, Judge, Case No. 83-43878 (09) - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, Third District, Case No. 84-1871.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An appeal was certified by the District Court of Appeal, Third District (Florida) in an action filed by appellees race track permit holders against appellants state agencies, seeking to have declared as unconstitutional those provisions of Fla. Stat. ch. 550 that prohibited horse racing and pari-mutuel gambling on Sunday. Appellants asserted that it was error for the trial court to grant appellees' motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, race track permit holders who conducted horse racing at various state tracks, filed a complaint against appellants, state agencies, seeking to declare as unconstitutional provisions of Fla. Stat. ch. 550 that prohibited horse racing and pari-mutuel gambling on Sunday. Appellees filed a motion for summary judgment, which was granted on the basis that the provisions of Fla. Stat. ch. 550 banning pari-mutuel wagering on Sundays was unconstitutional. Appellants sought review of the adverse decision, which was certified for review. The court reversed judgment of the trial court for appellants and held that the Sunday closing law for sporting activities involving pari-mutuel wagering did not constitute unlawful discrimination because it was rationally related to the legitimate state purpose of regulating and controlling gambling. The court held that pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. XIV, states were granted broad police powers to enact laws rationally related to achievement of the state's objective. Further, the court held that the Sunday closing law did not unlawfully discriminate against appellees, because the law treated all pari-mutuel facilities similarly circumstanced.


OUTCOME: The court reversed judgment in favor of appellants, state agencies, in an action filed by appellees, race track permit holders seeking to declare portions of a state statute prohibiting pari-mutuel gambling on Sunday unconstitutional, holding that a Sunday closing law for pari-mutuel wagering did not constitute unlawful discrimination because it was rationally related to appellants' legitimate state purpose of regulating and controlling gambling.

OVERVIEW: At petitioner's trial for loitering and prowling, the state presented testimony that a police officer observed him in the early evening hours looking into cars in a restaurant parking lot. Henderson v. State


No. 63094


Supreme Court of Florida


463 So. 2d 196; 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3408; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 43



January 10, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 28, 1985.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his convictions for three counts of first-degree murder based upon the deaths of three hitchhikers and his sentences of death for each of the three capital offenses from the lower court (Florida), raising several arguments.


OVERVIEW: A jury found appellant guilty of three counts of first-degree murder based upon the deaths of three hitchhikers. It recommended that appellant be sentenced to death, which the trial judge adopted. The trial judge found three aggravating circumstances and no evidence of any statutory mitigating circumstances. He found that the nonstatutory mitigating circumstances were of little if any weight. Appellant sought review. The court reviewed the record and considered each contention, but found no reversible error. There was sufficient evidence to support the finding that appellant knowingly and intelligently waived his right to have counsel present when he made certain statements to law enforcement. Although the testimony concerning appellant's admission to being wanted in other states bore no relevance to any material fact at issue and the motion to exclude all such references should have been granted, the error was harmless. There was no error in allowing the photographs of the victims into evidence. The trial court properly found that there were no mitigating circumstances sufficient to outweigh the aggravating circumstances found. Thus, the lower court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Upon reviewing the record and considering appellant's several arguments, the supreme court found no reversible error and affirmed appellant's convictions for three counts of first-degree murder and the sentences of death. The trial court correctly found that there were no mitigating circumstances sufficient to outweigh the three aggravating circumstances found.

Randolph v. State


No. 54869


Supreme Court of Florida


463 So. 2d 186; 1984 Fla. LEXIS 3742; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 27



December 20, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 26, 1985.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a Florida trial court decision that convicted him, after a jury trial, of first-degree murder and attempted robbery and that sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged a trial court decision that, after a jury trial, convicted him of first-degree murder and attempted robbery and sentenced him to death. The state supreme court affirmed appellant's conviction but remanded for resentencing upon consideration of the one valid aggravating circumstance and any existing mitigating circumstances. Appellant's conviction was supported by sufficient evidence. Moreover, no reversible procedural or evidentiary errors occurred. Furthermore, custodial statements appellant made and physical evidence seized pursuant to a consent to search were admissible because they were not the fruit of an illegal arrest. The exigency rule was applicable as the police reasonably believed an emergency existed. Evidence of appellant's prior nonviolent felony convictions was properly admitted after appellant became a witness to illuminate the quality of his testimony. Appellant was entitled to resentencing after the appellate court found that only one valid aggravating circumstance was present in the instant case rather than the multiple aggravating circumstances found by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed appellant's first-degree murder and attempted robbery convictions but vacated his death sentence and remanded for resentencing. Appellant's conviction was supported by sufficient evidence and no reversible procedural or evidentiary errors occurred. Reconsideration of appellant's sentence was necessary in light of the single valid aggravating factor and any applicable mitigating factors.

 

181 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Ruffin v. Wainwright


No. 65,117


Supreme Court of Florida


461 So. 2d 109; 1984 Fla. LEXIS 3751; 10 Fla. L. Weekly 20



December 20, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Proceeding - The Florida Bar.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a convicted murderer, filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus alleging that he was denied effective assistance of appellate counsel.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted and sentenced to death for the first-degree murder of a 21-year-old woman who was seven months pregnant at the time she was murdered. After exhausting the appellate process, petitioner filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus with the federal district court. Because he raised a claim of ineffective assistance of appellate counsel, the federal court abated the proceedings until the state supreme court could rule on his petition. The supreme court found that the majority of the omissions alleged by petitioner related to matters which his counsel was procedurally precluded from raising on appeal. The counsel could not be considered incompetent or ineffective for failing to raise issues that he was procedurally barred from raising because they were not properly presented at trial. Moreover, none of the alleged omissions constituted fundamental error that could be raised on direct appeal without their having been raised in the trial court. The supreme court denied habeas relief because petitioner failed to demonstrate that his appellate counsel's performance fell short of prevailing professional norms or was substantially deficient under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The petition for writ of habeas corpus filed by petitioner was denied because petitioner failed in his burden to show that he was entitled to relief. Petitioner failed to demonstrate that his appellate counsel's performance fell short of prevailing professional norms or was substantially deficient.

Polk County v. Florida Public Service Com.


Nos. 63,875, 63,892 CONSOLIDATED


Supreme Court of Florida


460 So. 2d 370; 1984 Fla. LEXIS 3749; 9 Fla. L. Weekly 507



December 6, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two consolidated Appeals from the Public Service Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant counties sought review of a rule adopted by appellee Public Service Commission permitting municipal electric utilities to impose a surcharge on customers outside corporate limits equal to the service tax imposed on customers within corporate limits.


OVERVIEW: An order of appellee Public Service Commission was affirmed as a proper act within appellee's authority. The rule allowed a municipal electric utility to impose a surcharge on customers outside of its corporate limits equal to the service tax imposed on customers within its corporate limits. While appellee had no authority to regulate specific dollar amounts charged for specific services, the rule set up a rate structure that was within the jurisdiction and authority of appellee. Due process was not violated because the surcharge resulted in equal overall charges to both residents and nonresidents. Also, persons challenging the surcharge were entitled to a public hearing.


OUTCOME: A rule adopted by appellee Public Service Commission and challenged by appellant counties was affirmed. In permitting municipal electric utilities to impose a surcharge on customers outside corporate limits equal to the service tax imposed on customers within corporate limits, the rule set up a permissible rate structure rather than specific rates and resulted in equal overall charges to residents and nonresidents.

Alvord v. State

Supreme Court of Florida

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Proceeding - All Writs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a death row inmate, sought a writ of extraordinary relief and requested the court to require a judicial determination of his competency to be executed for first degree murder and to stay his execution.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner filed for a writ of extraordinary relief and for a stay of execution, arguing that he was incompetent to be executed. The court denied the petition for writ of extraordinary relief and for stay of execution.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner a writ of extraordinary relief or a stay of execution, holding that a Florida statute permitting petitioner to be examined for competency to be executed did not deny petitioner due process of law and that petitioner was not entitled to a judicial determination of competency to be executed at an adversarial proceeding.

Stano v. State


No. 63,947


Supreme Court of Florida


460 So. 2d 890; 1984 Fla. LEXIS 3562; 9 Fla. L. Weekly 475



November 1, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 15, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, S. James Foxman, Judge - Case Nos. 83-188-CC and 83-189-CC.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his adjudication of guilty from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County (Florida) on two counts of first-degree murder and his two death sentences.


OVERVIEW: Appellant had pleaded guilty to two murders, one for the strangulation/drowning of one woman and two years later the shooting/drowning of another woman. In sentencing appellant to death on each murder, the court found three aggravating circumstances: previous convictions of six first-degree murders; heinous, atrocious, or cruel murders; and murders committed in a cold, calculated, and premeditated manner. The supreme court affirmed the adjudications and held that the trial court had properly imposed the death sentence. The court explained there was a competent basis for the court's acceptance of appellant's pleas and adjudication. The large number of prior murder convictions was the dominant factor. The trial court did not err in finding that the murders were heinous, atrocious or cruel and committed in a cold, calculated, and premeditated manner. The court also held that the trial court had not erred in denying appellant's motion to preclude the death penalty. Sentencing appellant to death for these last two murders was not disproportionate. Comparing these cases to other death sentence cases, the court found appellant's sentences to be both proportionate and warranted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction on two counts of first-degree murder and his two death sentences and held that the trial court had not improperly imposed the death sentence nor had the court erred in denying appellant's motion to preclude the death penalty.

 

186 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Mikenas v. State


No. 64,317


Supreme Court of Florida


460 So. 2d 359; 1984 Fla. LEXIS 3565; 9 Fla. L. Weekly 473



November 1, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 3, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, M. William Graybill, Judge - Case No. 75-5790.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Arguing that his sentence of death was based on an invalid guilty plea and that he was denied effective assistance of counsel, appellant sought review from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County (Florida) which denied his motion for post-conviction relief filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder and of second-degree murder. He was sentenced to death and life imprisonment. On direct appeal, the court affirmed the convictions but remanded for resentencing because the trial judge considered a nonstatutory aggravating factor. Appellant's sentence to death was affirmed. Certiorari was denied and appellant brought a motion for post-conviction relief pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The court rejected appellant's arguments and affirmed the denial of his motion for post-conviction relief. The court found that appellant's sentence of death was based on a voluntary and valid guilty plea. The court noted that the record demonstrated that his guilty plea was intelligent and fully understood. The court also concluded that he was not denied effective assistance of counsel during the course of the penalty trial. The court reasoned that he could not show that there was a reasonable probability that, but for counsel's unprofessional errors, the result of the proceeding would have been different.


OUTCOME: The denial of appellant's motion for post-conviction relief was affirmed because he failed to establish that his plea was involuntary and because the record established that the conduct of his counsel was not unreasonable under the circumstances.

 

187 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


In re Adoption of H.Y.T.


No. 65,515


Supreme Court of Florida


458 So. 2d 1127; 1984 Fla. LEXIS 3554; 9 Fla. L. Weekly 459



October 25, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 12, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Volusia County, C. McFerrin Smith, Judge, Case No. 77-3022-CA-01, D Certified by the District Court of Appeal, Fifth District, Case No. 84-780.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney-ad-litem sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Volusia County (Florida) which denied his motion to close adoption proceeding pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 63.162(1). The trial court held that the statute was an unconstitutional restriction on the media's right of access to court proceedings under U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: Maternal and paternal grandparents battled over custody to their orphaned granddaughter. The press gave the bitter dispute great play and covered all the early proceedings. After appellant was appointed attorney-ad-litem for the child, he requested that the trial court close the adoption proceedings pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 63.162(1) (1983). The trial court denied the motion, holding that ch. 63.162(1) was unconstitutionally overbroad because it permitted no discretion in weighing the constitutional guarantee of a fair trial against the media's right under U.S. Const. amend. I of access to court proceedings On direct review, the court reversed the order of the trial court and held that ch. 63.162(1) was constitutional. According to the court, the Florida legislature had recognized an overriding public policy of protecting from harmful publicity parties to and the subject to adoption proceedings. The court found that any impairment of the media's freedoms ch. 63.162(1) created affected only matters of newsworthiness rather than matters of real public or general concern, and, by the admission of the newspaper's own counsel, the impairment was minimal.


OUTCOME: Upholding the constitutionality of the statute allowing for closed adoption proceedings, the court reversed the order of the trial court and directed that all proceedings be conducted in compliance with the statute.

 

188 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Markham v. Fogg


No. 60,759


Supreme Court of Florida


458 So. 2d 1122; 1984 Fla. LEXIS 3450; 9 Fla. L. Weekly 445



October 18, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 12, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions Fourth District - Case No. 79-205.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, including county property appraiser, sought review of an opinion of the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) construing Fla. Stat. ch. 193.461(4)(c)(1973) regarding the reclassification of agricultural land, which the court certified as being directly in conflict with other district's opinion.


OVERVIEW: Respondent landowners brought actions for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief to have their property classified and taxed as agricultural. Petitioner county property appraiser had reclassified the property as nonagricultural pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 193.461 (1973). In quashing the decision of the district court and instructing it to affirm the judgment of the trial court upholding the reclassification, the court found ample evidence to sustain the trial judge's findings, with the exception of the application of the "three times rule" of § 193.461(4)(c); since there was no completed sale of the land, the rule did not apply. The court determined that the statute was constitutional, since the legislature's concern was reasonably aroused by the possibility of landowners taking advantage of the agricultural classification, the statute proscribed speculative rezoning and thus was rationally related to the legislative purpose, and the landowner was permitted to rebut the presumption of nonagricultural use. Rejecting the claim of equal protection violation, the court found that the statute was rationally related to the state goal of discouraging speculative rezoning.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the decision of the district court and instructed it to enter an order affirming the judgment of the trial court holding that the statute mandating a change in an agricultural classification to a nonagricultural reclassification for tax purposes was constitutional and was proper as applied to the facts of this case, thus upholding the nonagricultural classification of respondent landowners' property.

Miller v. Publicker Industries, Inc.

Supreme Court of Florida


457 So. 2d 1374; 1984 Fla. LEXIS 3486; 9 Fla. L. Weekly 437

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of an order of the Leon County Court, Florida, that declared chapter 84-353, Laws of Florida, a tax exemption law, unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, foreign importers of ethyl alcohol, filed suit and had chapter 84-353, Laws of Florida, declared unconstitutional. The court affirmed the order. The court held said law constituted discriminatory taxation based upon the foreign origin of a product in violation of the U.S. Constitution's import-export clause, unlawfully discriminating against foreign commerce.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order declaring the tax exemption law unconstitutional.

 

190 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Foster v. Wainwright


No. 65,967


Supreme Court of Florida


457 So. 2d 1372; 1984 Fla. LEXIS 3485; 9 Fla. L. Weekly 433



October 10, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court was petitioner's application for a writ of habeas corpus upon his conviction for robbery and first-degree murder, for which he was sentenced to death. Petitioner argued that he did not receive meaningful appellate review of his death sentence, and that his sentence was disproportionate to his crimes.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of robbery and first-degree murder, for which he was sentenced to death. This court affirmed petitioner's conviction and sentence. After petitioner was subsequently denied post-conviction relief, he filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The trial court and the district court of appeal denied relief and his application for certiorari relief to the U.S. Supreme Court was subsequently rejected. Petitioner then filed the instant petition for a writ of habeas corpus. This court denied petitioner relief. Petitioner first argued that he did not receive a meaningful review of his death sentence because this court's consideration of whether to use non-record materials in the review of his death sentence on direct appeal was not made known to his counsel. The court found this contention without merit, concluding that availability of information to it concerning petitioner, a capital defendant, that was not presented at trial and was not part of the trial record or record on appeal was not unconstitutional. In reaching its decision to deny relief, the court further rejected petitioner's claim that his death sentence was disproportionate to his crimes.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's application for a writ of habeas corpus. The court first held that it was not unconstitutional to make available to this court information concerning petitioner that was not presented at trial and was not part of the trial record or record on appeal. The court further ruled that petitioner's sentence was proportionate to his crimes.

 

191 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Eutzy v. State


No. 64,212


Supreme Court of Florida


458 So. 2d 755; 1984 Fla. LEXIS 3412; 9 Fla. L. Weekly 397



September 20, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 3, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County, William S. Rowley, Judge - Case No. 83-1105-F.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County (Florida), which convicted him of murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder and sentenced to death. On appeal, his conviction and death sentence were affirmed by the state supreme court. The court rejected appellant's claim that the judicial override provision was unconstitutional, finding the claim unpreserved. The court also found appellant's claim that the jury was misinstructed at the penalty phase irrelevant, given that the jurors recommended mercy. The court further held that appellant's challenge to the cold-calculated-premeditated murder aggravator was meritless, the jury itself having found the murder was premeditated. The court did agree that the commission-during-a-robbery aggravator was unproven, although that decision did not affect the sentence. As to the trial court's decision to reject the jury's mercy recommendation, the court held that, given the fact that there were two aggravators proven and no viable mitigator upon which mercy could have been recommended, the recommendation was unreasonable and need not have been followed.


OUTCOME: Appellant's murder conviction and death sentence were affirmed. Of appellant's claims which were preserved, none warranted relief; the aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating circumstances because no mitigating circumstances existed, and the jury's recommendation of mercy was unreasonable.

193 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Thomas v. State


No. 61,170


Supreme Court of Florida


456 So. 2d 454; 1984 Fla. LEXIS 3395; 9 Fla. L. Weekly 392



September 13, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Thomas M. Coker, Jr., Judge - Case Nos. 81-5569-CG and 81-11122.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida) decision that convicted him, after a jury trial, of two first-degree murder counts and sentenced him to death on one of the counts.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged a trial court decision that convicted him, following a jury trial, of two counts of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death on one count. The state supreme court affirmed the decision of the trial court. Appellant's convictions were supported by substantial, competent evidence. The evidence showed the nature of the intentionally inflicted injuries and supported the jury's finding that appellant intended the consequences of his actions. Appellant's confession was not suppressible as it was not the product of coercion, confusion, or intoxication. An improper judicial remark about a defense witness was corrected by a curative jury instruction. The trial court did not err by overriding the jury's recommended life sentence and imposing a death sentence because aggravating circumstances, including appellant's other first-degree murder conviction, that the murder was committed to prevent arrest, that the murder was especially cruel, and that the murder was cold and premeditated, outweighed the mitigating factors that appellant lacked a significant criminal history and that appellant was only 20 years old at the time of the capital felony.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed a trial court decision that convicted appellant of two first-degree murder counts and sentenced him to death on one count. No reversible procedural or evidentiary errors occurred. The trial court judge was justified in overriding the jury's recommended life sentence and imposing the death sentence after finding that the statutory aggravating factors far outweighed the mitigating circumstances.

Copeland v. State


No. 57,788


Supreme Court of Florida


457 So. 2d 1012; 1984 Fla. LEXIS 3398; 9 Fla. L. Weekly 388



September 13, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 15, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Wakulla County, Kenneth E. Cooksey, Judge - Case No. 78-CF-66.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction and death sentence from the Circuit Court in and for Wakulla County (Florida) for first-degree murder, kidnapping, robbery, and sexual battery.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and death sentence for first-degree murder, kidnapping, robbery, and sexual battery. The court denied appellant's contention that it should find the death penalty unconstitutional because all arguments in that area had been previously decided by the court. The court also rejected appellant's argument that exclusion from jury service of all veniremen, whose views on capital punishment were such as to preclude them from assuming the duties of a juror in a capital case, robbed him of a representative jury. The court held that the trial judge did not abuse his discretion in denying appellant's motion for change of venue because appellant did not demonstrate a general atmosphere of hostility against him in the community. The court found appellant's other claims to be without merit. The court held that the trial judge properly considered aggravating factors in imposing the death sentence, such as appellant's willing participation in the felony, resulting in the victim's murder. The court did vacate appellant's separate sentence for kidnapping as that was the underlying felony to the felony murder conviction, and the two should have been merged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and death sentence for first-degree murder, kidnapping, robbery, and sexual battery. The court found that the trial judge did not abuse his discretion in denying appellant's motion for change of venue because appellant did not demonstrate a general atmosphere of hostility against him in the community. The court held that appellant's other claims were without merit.

Forsberg v. Housing Authority of Miami Beach


No. 54,623


Supreme Court of Florida


455 So. 2d 373; 1984 Fla. LEXIS 3326; 10 Media L. Rep. 2511; 9 Fla. L. Weekly 335



August 30, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, William A. Herin, Judge - Case No. 77-27260.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff public housing tenants appealed an order of the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), granting defendant housing authority's motion to dismiss their suit to enjoin defendant from allowing public access to information provided by public housing tenants and prospective tenants, and ruling that Fla. Stat. ch. 119 violated neither Fla. Const. art. I, § 2, nor U.S. Const. amends. I, II, IV, V, IX, or XIV.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff public housing tenants filed a class action suit seeking to enjoin defendant housing authority from allowing public access to information provided by public housing tenants and prospective tenants. Plaintiffs appealed the trial court's order granting defendant's motion to dismiss. The trial court ruled that Fla. Stat. ch. 119 violated neither Fla. Const. art. I, § 2, nor U.S. Const. amends. I, II, IV, V, IX, or XIV, and that the complaint failed to state a cause of action. The supreme court ruled that under Fla. Stat. ch. 119.01, public records were open for personal inspection, and the housing authority was an agency whose records were public under Fla. Stat. ch. 119.011. While certain records were statutorily exempted from the public's right to inspect pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 119.07, the court's examination of the statutes revealed no exemption pertaining to the records involved in plaintiffs' appeal. The supreme court affirmed the trial court's order, ruling that there was no exemption or constitutional right of privacy that prevented inspection of the records.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting defendant housing authority's motion to dismiss an action to enjoin defendant from allowing public access to information provided by public housing tenants and prospective tenants, and ruling that a statute at issue was constitutional. The legislature clearly stated that public records should be open for public inspection, and the records at issue were public records.

 

196 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Dobbert v. State


Nos. 65,465, 65,782


Supreme Court of Florida


456 So. 2d 424; 1984 Fla. LEXIS 3330; 9 Fla. L. Weekly 326



August 28, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, R. Hudson Olliff, Judge - Case No. 73-5068CF - Div. S. and an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner who was convicted of first degree murder, second degree murder, child torture, and child abuse appealed the orders from the Circuit Court, Duval County (Florida), which denied his motions to vacate his judgment and death sentence. Petitioner also filed a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, who was convicted of murder, child abuse, and child torture contended the trial court erred when it denied his motions to vacate his judgment and death sentence. Petitioner argued his counsel was ineffective. The court held petitioner failed to demonstrate the ineffectiveness of his counsel because he failed to show his counsel's performance was deficient and the deficient performance prejudiced his defense. The court affirmed the denial of petitioner's motion to vacate. In his habeas petition, he contended appellate counsel was ineffective when counsel failed to challenge a jury instruction on felony murder, which included reference to the offense of the abominable and detestable crime against nature. Because the instruction was not objected to at trial, the only way appellate counsel could have obtained review was if the error was fundamental. The court held the instruction did not render petitioner's trial fundamentally unfair, and the failure of his appellate counsel to raise this point on appeal was not a substantial and serious deficiency measurably below the standard of performance expected of competent counsel. Order of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Order of the trial court that denied petitioner's motion to vacate judgment and sentence was affirmed. Petition for habeas corpus was denied. Petitioner argued that his counsel was ineffective, but failed to demonstrate counsel's performance was deficient and the deficient performance prejudiced his defense.

 

197 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Chase Fed. S&L Ass'n v. Schreiber


No. 63,017


Supreme Court of Florida


1984 Fla. LEXIS 3193



July 26, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Rehearing Granted August 30, 1985; Opinion Withdrawn August 30, 1985


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mortgagee sought review of an en banc decision of the Third District Court of Appeals (Florida), which ruled that a deed given to a non-relative in return for love and affection was invalid on its face, but which certified the question of what scope of review should district courts of appeal properly apply when granting rehearings en banc.


OVERVIEW: The court held that district courts of appeal, in exercising their en banc power, were not limited by case-law standards adopted by the Supreme Court of Florida in the exercise of their discretionary conflict jurisdiction, but were free to develop their own concept of decisional uniformity. Such a ruling was justified as case loads increased throughout the district courts; this en banc process would help avoid decisional conflicts, would assure harmonious decisions within court boundaries, and would develop predictability within the law. The process could only serve finality and uniformity of the law within each court jurisdiction. This was particularly true in cases where, as here, broad decisional discretion was required to attain "uniformity of decisions" when controlling facts in conflicting cases were not the same. As for the instant case, the court ruled that a deed, conveyed by a 90-year old woman to a non-relative for "love and affection," placed a subsequent grantee on notice that the deed was void for lack of consideration. Thus, the court concluded, the deeds to both grantees must be canceled, as well as the mortgage issued by petitioner bank to the latter grantee.


OUTCOME: En banc decision affirmed that a deed given to a non-relative in return for love and affection was invalid on its face for lack of consideration and placed subsequent grantee -- and petitioner, the grantee's mortgagee -- on notice that the deed might be void, and that en banc power of district courts of appeal properly developed own concept of decisional uniformity to harmonize decision with conflicting ruling.

 

198 of 2089 DOCUMENTS


Gulfstream Park Racing Asso. v. Hialeah, Inc.


No. 64686


Supreme Court of Florida


453 So. 2d 812; 1984 Fla. LEXIS 3270



July 19, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner racing association sought review of a decision of the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida) that determined that there should not be a departure from the rule of rotation which was deemed to remain a part of the pertinent law of Florida, in an action brought by respondent race course to determine which track should be awarded the middle racing dates.


OVERVIEW: The Florida Pari-Mutuel Commission (the Commission) determined that petitioner racing association should be awarded the middle racing dates based on the criteria enumerated in Gulfstream. The determination was reversed, and petitioner sought review. A question was certified to determine the standards applicable to the award of racing dates in Florida, including the viability and application of the "rotation rule" in making that determination. The court held that the district court should have reviewed the record to determine whether there was competent substantial evidence to support the Commission's findings of fact. Rotation was not something departed from, but rather something resorted to, after application of the Gulfstream criteria failed to result in identification of the proper track to be awarded the middle dates. The Commission was vested with the nondelegable discretionary power to allocate racing dates, and the legislature chose not to establish rotation as a rule to be presumptively followed. The Commission was to exercise its discretion according to the Gulfstream standards that the legislature implicitly adopted.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the decision not to departure from the rule of rotation, holding the Florida Pari-Mutuel Commission was vested with the nondelegable discretionary power to allocate racing dates, and could rotate when necessary. The court ruled that rotation was something resorted to after application of the criteria failed to result in identification of the proper track to be awarded the middle dates.
